EXPLANATORY

In this buuk a number of diealects ar uezd, to wit: th Missouri negro diealect; th extremest form of th bakwuuds Southwestern diealect; th ordinairy “Piek County” diealect; and foer modified varieetys of this last. Th shaedings hav not bin dun in a haphazard fashun, or bi geswerk; but paenstaekingly, and with th trustwerthy giedans and suport of personal familiarrity with thees several forms of speech.

I maek this explanaeshun for th reezon that without it meny reeders wuud supoez that all thees carracters wer trieing to tauk aliek and not sucseeding.

Th AUTHOR.





Huklberry FINN



Seen: Th Mississippi Valy Tiem: Forty to fifty yeers ago











CHAPTER I.

U don’t noe about me without u hav red a buuk bi th naem of Th Advenchers of Tom Sawyer; but that ain’t no mater. That buuk was maed bi Mr. Mark Twaen, and he toeld th trooth, maenly. Thair was things which he strecht, but maenly he toeld th trooth. That is nuthing. I never seen enybody but lied wun tiem or anuther, without it was Ant Polly, or th wido, or maybe Mary. Ant Polly—Tom’s Ant Polly, she is—and Mary, and th Wido Douglas is all toeld about in that buuk, which is moestly a troo buuk, with sum stretchers, as I sed befor.

Now th way that th buuk wiends up is this: Tom and me found th muny that th robers hid in th caev, and it maed us rich. We got six thouzand dolars apees—all goeld. It was an awful siet of muny when it was pield up. Wel, Juj Thatcher he tuuk it and puut it out at interest, and it fetched us a dolar a day apees all th yeer round—mor than a body cuud tel whut to do with. Th Wido Douglas she tuuk me for her sun, and alowd she wuud sivilize me; but it was ruf living in th hous all th tiem, considering how dizmal reguelar and deesent th wido was in all her ways; and so when I couldn’t stand it no longger I lit out. I got into mi oeld rags and mi shuugar-hogzhed agen, and was free and satisfied. But Tom Sawyer he hunted me up and sed he was going to start a band of robers, and I miet join if I wuud go bak to th wido and be respectabl. So I went bak.

Th wido she cried oever me, and calld me a pur lost lam, and she calld me a lot of uther naems, too, but she never ment no harm bi it. She puut me in them nue cloeths agen, and I couldn’t do nuthing but swet and swet, and feel all cramped up. Wel, then, th oeld thing comenst agen. Th wido rung a bel for super, and u had to cum to tiem. When u got to th taebl u couldn’t go riet to eeting, but u had to waet for th wido to tuk doun her hed and grumbl a litl oever th victuals, tho thair worn’t reealy enything th mater with them,—that is, nuthing oenly evrything was cuukt bi itself. In a barrel of ods and ends it is diferent; things get mixt up, and th joos kiend of swaps around, and th things go beter.

After super she got out her buuk and lernd me about Moses and th Bulrushers, and I was in a swet to fiend out all about him; but bi and bi she let it out that Moses had bin ded a considerabl long tiem; so then I didn’t cair no mor about him, becauz I don’t taek no stok in ded peepl.









Prity soon I wonted to smoek, and askt th wido to let me. But she wouldn’t. She sed it was a meen practis and wasn’t cleen, and I must tri to not do it eny mor. That is just th way with sum peepl. Thay get doun on a thing when thay don’t noe nuthing about it. Heer she was a-bothering about Moses, which was no kin to her, and no ues to enybody, being gon, u see, yet fiending a power of fallt with me for doing a thing that had sum guud in it. And she tuuk snuff, too; of cors that was all riet, becauz she dun it herself.

Her sister, Mis Watson, a tolerabl slim oeld maed, with gogls on, had just cum to liv with her, and tuuk a set at me now with a speling-buuk. She werkt me midling hard for about an our, and then th wido maed her eez up. I couldn’t stuud it much longger. Then for an our it was dedly dul, and I was fijety. Mis Watson wuud say, “Don’t puut yur feet up thair, Huklberry;” and “Don’t scrunch up liek that, Huklberry—set up straet;” and prity soon she wuud say, “Don’t gap and strech liek that, Huklberry—whi don’t u tri to behaev?” Then she toeld me all about th bad plaes, and I sed I wisht I was thair. She got mad then, but I didn’t meen no harm. All I wonted was to go somewheres; all I wonted was a chaenj, I worn’t particuelar. She sed it was wiked to say whut I sed; sed she wouldn’t say it for th hoel werld; she was going to liv so as to go to th guud plaes. Wel, I couldn’t see no advantej in going whair she was going, so I maed up mi miend I wouldn’t tri for it. But I never sed so, becauz it wuud oenly maek trubl, and wouldn’t do no guud.









Now she had got a start, and she went on and toeld me all about th guud plaes. She sed all a body wuud hav to do thair was to go around all day long with a harp and sing, forever and ever. So I didn’t think much of it. But I never sed so. I askt her if she rekond Tom Sawyer wuud go thair, and she sed not bi a considerabl siet. I was glad about that, becauz I wonted him and me to be together.

Mis Watson she kept pecking at me, and it got tiersum and loensum. Bi and bi thay fetched th niggers in and had prairs, and then evrybody was off to bed. I went up to mi room with a pees of candl, and puut it on th taebl. Then I set doun in a chair bi th windo and tried to think of sumthing cheerful, but it worn’t no ues. I felt so loensum I moest wisht I was ded. Th stars wer shiening, and th leevs rusld in th wuuds ever so mornful; and I herd an oul, away off, hoo-whooing about sumbody that was ded, and a whippowill and a daug crieing about sumbody that was going to die; and th wiend was trieing to whisper sumthing to me, and I couldn’t maek out whut it was, and so it maed th coeld shivers run oever me. Then away out in th wuuds I herd that kiend of a sound that a goest maeks when it wonts to tel about sumthing that’s on its miend and can’t maek itself understuud, and so can’t rest eezy in its graev, and has to go about that way evry niet greeving. I got so doun-hearted and scaird I did wish I had sum cumpany. Prity soon a spieder went cralling up mi shoelder, and I flipt it off and it lit in th candl; and befor I cuud buj it was all shriveld up. I didn’t need enybody to tel me that that was an awful bad sien and wuud fech me sum bad luk, so I was scaird and moest shuuk th cloeths off of me. I got up and ternd around in mi traks three tiems and crosst mi brest evry tiem; and then I tied up a litl lok of mi hair with a thred to keep wiches away. But I hadn’t no confidens. U do that when u’ve lost a hors-shoo that u’ve found, insted of naeling it up oever th dor, but I hadn’t ever herd enybody say it was eny way to keep off bad luk when u’d kild a spieder.

I set doun agen, a-shaeking all oever, and got out mi piep for a smoek; for th hous was all as stil as deth now, and so th wido wouldn’t noe. Wel, after a long tiem I herd th clok away off in th toun go boom—boom—boom—twelv licks; and all stil agen—stiller than ever. Prity soon I herd a twig snap doun in th dark amungst th trees—sumthing was a stering. I set stil and lisend. Directly I cuud just bairly heer a “me-yow! me-yow!” doun thair. That was guud! Sez I, “me-yow! me-yow!” as sofft as I cuud, and then I puut out th liet and scrambld out of th windo on to th shed. Then I slipt doun to th ground and cralld in amung th trees, and, shur enuf, thair was Tom Sawyer waeting for me.
















CHAPTER II.

We went tiptoeing along a path amungst th trees bak tords th end of th wido’s garden, stooping doun so as th branches wouldn’t scraep our heds. When we was pasing bi th kichen I fel oever a root and maed a noiz. We scrouched doun and laed stil. Mis Watson’s big nigger, naemd Jim, was seting in th kichen dor; we cuud see him prity cleer, becauz thair was a liet behiend him. He got up and strecht his nek out about a minit, lisening. Then he sez:

“Hoo dah?”

He lisend sum mor; then he cum tiptoeing doun and stuud riet between us; we cuud a tucht him, neerly. Wel, liekly it was minits and minits that thair worn’t a sound, and we all thair so cloez together. Thair was a plaes on mi ankl that got to iching, but I dasn’t scrach it; and then mi eer begun to ich; and next mi bak, riet between mi shoelders. Seemd liek I’d die if I couldn’t scrach. Wel, I’ve noetist that thing plenty tiems sinss. If u ar with th qolity, or at a fueneral, or trieing to go to sleep when u ain’t sleepy—if u ar anywheres whair it wun’t do for u to scrach, whi u wil ich all oever in upwards of a thouzand plaeses. Prity soon Jim sez:

“Say, hoo is u? Whar is u? Daug mi cats ef I didn’ heer sumf’n. Wel, I noe whut I’s gwyne to do: I’s gwyne to set doun heer and lisen tel I heers it agin.”









So he set doun on th ground betwixt me and Tom. He leend his bak up agenst a tree, and strecht his legs out til wun of them moest tucht wun of mien. Mi noez begun to ich. It itched til th teers cum into mi ies. But I dasn’t scrach. Then it begun to ich on th insied. Next I got to iching underneeth. I didn’t noe how I was going to set stil. This miserableness went on as much as six or seven minits; but it seemd a siet longger than that. I was iching in eleven diferent plaeses now. I rekond I couldn’t stand it mor’n a minit longger, but I set mi teeth hard and got redy to tri. Just then Jim begun to breeth hevy; next he begun to snor—and then I was prity soon cumfortabl agen.

Tom he maed a sien to me—kiend of a litl noiz with his mouth—and we went creeping away on our hands and nees. When we was ten fuut off Tom whisperd to me, and wonted to tee Jim to th tree for fun. But I sed no; he miet waek and maek a disterbans, and then thay’d fiend out I worn’t in. Then Tom sed he hadn’t got candls enuf, and he wuud slip in th kichen and get sum mor. I didn’t wont him to tri. I sed Jim miet waek up and cum. But Tom wonted to resk it; so we slid in thair and got three candls, and Tom laed fiev sents on th taebl for pay. Then we got out, and I was in a swet to get away; but nuthing wuud do Tom but he must crall to whair Jim was, on his hands and nees, and play sumthing on him. I waeted, and it seemd a guud whiel, evrything was so stil and loensum.

As soon as Tom was bak we cut along th path, around th garden fens, and bi and bi fetched up on th steep top of th hil th uther sied of th hous. Tom sed he slipt Jim’s hat off of his hed and hung it on a lim riet oever him, and Jim sterd a litl, but he didn’t waek. Afterwards Jim sed th wiches be witched him and puut him in a trans, and roed him all oever th Staet, and then set him under th trees agen, and hung his hat on a lim to sho hoo dun it. And next tiem Jim toeld it he sed thay roed him doun to Nue Orleans; and, after that, evry tiem he toeld it he spred it mor and mor, til bi and bi he sed thay roed him all oever th werld, and tierd him moest to deth, and his bak was all oever sadl-boils. Jim was monstrus proud about it, and he got so he wouldn’t hardly noetis th uther niggers. Niggers wuud cum miels to heer Jim tel about it, and he was mor luukt up to than eny nigger in that cuntry. Straenj niggers wuud stand with thair mouths oepen and luuk him all oever, saem as if he was a wunder. Niggers is allways tauking about wiches in th dark bi th kichen fier; but whenever wun was tauking and leting on to noe all about such things, Jim wuud hapen in and say, “Hm! Whut u noe ’bout wiches?” and that nigger was corkt up and had to taek a bak seet. Jim allways kept that fiev-senter pees round his nek with a string, and sed it was a charm th devil giv to him with his oen hands, and toeld him he cuud cuer enybody with it and fech wiches whenever he wonted to just bi saying sumthing to it; but he never toeld whut it was he sed to it. Niggers wuud cum frum all around thair and giv Jim enything thay had, just for a siet of that fiev-senter pees; but thay wouldn’t tuch it, becauz th devil had had his hands on it. Jim was moest rooind for a servant, becauz he got stuk up on acount of having seen th devil and bin roed bi wiches.

Wel, when Tom and me got to th ej of th hiltop we luukt away doun into th vilej and cuud see three or foer liets twinkling, whair thair was sik foeks, maybe; and th stars oever us was sparkling ever so fien; and doun bi th vilej was th river, a hoel miel braud, and awful stil and grand. We went doun th hil and found Jo Harper and Ben Rogers, and too or three mor of th boys, hid in th oeld tanyard. So we unhicht a skif and puuld doun th river too miel and a haf, to th big scar on th hilsied, and went ashor.

We went to a clump of buushes, and Tom maed evrybody swair to keep th seecret, and then shoed them a hoel in th hil, riet in th thikest part of th buushes. Then we lit th candls, and cralld in on our hands and nees. We went about too hundred yards, and then th caev oepend up. Tom poekt about amungst th pasejes, and prity soon dukt under a wall whair u wouldn’t a noetist that thair was a hoel. We went along a narro plaes and got into a kiend of room, all damp and swety and coeld, and thair we stopt. Tom sez:

“Now, we’ll start this band of robers and call it Tom Sawyer’s Gang. Evrybody that wonts to join has got to taek an oeth, and riet his naem in blud.”









Evrybody was wiling. So Tom got out a sheet of paeper that he had roet th oeth on, and red it. It swor evry boy to stik to th band, and never tel eny of th seecrets; and if enybody dun enything to eny boy in th band, whichever boy was orderd to kil that person and his family must do it, and he mustn’t eet and he mustn’t sleep til he had kild them and hakt a cross in thair brests, which was th sien of th band. And noebody that didn’t belong to th band cuud ues that mark, and if he did he must be sood; and if he dun it agen he must be kild. And if enybody that belongd to th band toeld th seecrets, he must hav his throet cut, and then hav his carcas bernt up and th ashes scaterd all around, and his naem bloted off of th list with blud and never menshund agen bi th gang, but hav a curs puut on it and be forgot forever.

Evrybody sed it was a reeal buetiful oeth, and askt Tom if he got it out of his oen hed. He sed, sum of it, but th rest was out of pieret-buuks and rober-buuks, and evry gang that was hi-toned had it.

Sum thaut it wuud be guud to kil th familys of boys that toeld th seecrets. Tom sed it was a guud iedeea, so he tuuk a pensil and roet it in. Then Ben Rogers sez:

“Heer’s Huck Finn, he hain’t got no family; whut u going to do ’bout him?”

“Wel, hain’t he got a faather?” sez Tom Sawyer.

“Yes, he’s got a faather, but u can’t never fiend him thees days. He uezd to lay drunk with th hogs in th tanyard, but he hain’t bin seen in thees parts for a yeer or mor.”

Thay taukt it oever, and thay was going to rool me out, becauz thay sed evry boy must hav a family or sumbody to kil, or els it wouldn’t be fair and sqair for th uthers. Wel, noebody cuud think of enything to do—evrybody was stumpt, and set stil. I was moest redy to cri; but all at wuns I thaut of a way, and so I offerd them Mis Watson—thay cuud kil her. Evrybody sed:

“O, she’ll do. That’s all riet. Huck can cum in.”

Then thay all stuk a pin in thair finggers to get blud to sien with, and I maed mi mark on th paeper.

“Now,” sez Ben Rogers, “whut’s th lien of biznes of this Gang?”

“Nuthing oenly robery and merder,” Tom sed.

“But hoo ar we going to rob?—houses, or catl, or—”

“Stuf! steeling catl and such things ain’t robery; it’s berglary,” sez Tom Sawyer. “We ain’t berglars. That ain’t no sort of stiel. We ar highwaymen. We stop staejes and carrejes on th roed, with masks on, and kil th peepl and taek thair woches and muny.”

“Must we allways kil th peepl?”

“O, sertenly. It’s best. Sum authoritys think diferent, but moestly it’s considerd best to kil them—exsept sum that u bring to th caev heer, and keep them til thay’re ransomed.”

“Ransomed? Whut’s that?”

“I don’t noe. But that’s whut thay do. I’ve seen it in buuks; and so of cors that’s whut we’ve got to do.”

“But how can we do it if we don’t noe whut it is?”

“Whi, blaem it all, we’ve got to do it. Don’t I tel u it’s in th buuks? Do u wont to go to doing diferent frum whut’s in th buuks, and get things all muddled up?”

“O, that’s all verry fien to say, Tom Sawyer, but how in th naeshun ar thees feloes going to be ransomed if we don’t noe how to do it to them?—that’s th thing I wont to get at. Now, whut do u rekon it is?”

“Wel, I don’t noe. But per’aps if we keep them til thay’re ransomed, it meens that we keep them til thay’re ded.”

“Now, that’s sumthing liek. That’ll anser. Whi couldn’t u sed that befor? We’ll keep them til thay’re ransomed to deth; and a bothersum lot thay’ll be, too—eeting up evrything, and allways trieing to get loos.”

“How u tauk, Ben Rogers. How can thay get loos when thair’s a gard oever them, redy to shoot them doun if thay moov a peg?”

“A gard! Wel, that is guud. So sumbody’s got to set up all niet and never get eny sleep, just so as to woch them. I think that’s foolishnes. Whi can’t a body taek a club and ransum them as soon as thay get heer?”

“Becauz it ain’t in th buuks so—that’s whi. Now, Ben Rogers, do u wont to do things reguelar, or don’t u?—that’s th iedeea. Don’t u rekon that th peepl that maed th buuks noes whut’s th corect thing to do? Do u rekon u can lern ’em enything? Not bi a guud deel. No, ser, we’ll just go on and ransum them in th reguelar way.”

“All riet. I don’t miend; but I say it’s a fool way, enyhow. Say, do we kil th wimen, too?”

“Wel, Ben Rogers, if I was as ignorant as u I wouldn’t let on. Kil th wimen? No; noebody ever saw enything in th buuks liek that. U fech them to th caev, and u’re allways as poliet as pi to them; and bi and bi thay fall in luv with u, and never wont to go hoem eny mor.”

“Wel, if that’s th way I’m agreed, but I don’t taek no stok in it. Miety soon we’ll hav th caev so cluterd up with wimen, and feloes waeting to be ransomed, that thair wun’t be no plaes for th robers. But go ahed, I ain’t got nuthing to say.”

Litl Tommy Barnes was asleep now, and when thay waekt him up he was scaird, and cried, and sed he wonted to go hoem to his maa, and didn’t wont to be a rober eny mor.

So thay all maed fun of him, and calld him cri-baeby, and that maed him mad, and he sed he wuud go straet and tel all th seecrets. But Tom giv him fiev sents to keep qieet, and sed we wuud all go hoem and meet next week, and rob sumbody and kil sum peepl.

Ben Rogers sed he couldn’t get out much, oenly Sundays, and so he wonted to begin next Sunday; but all th boys sed it wuud be wiked to do it on Sunday, and that setld th thing. Thay agreed to get together and fix a day as soon as thay cuud, and then we elected Tom Sawyer ferst capten and Jo Harper second capten of th Gang, and so started hoem.

I clumb up th shed and crept into mi windo just befor day was braeking. Mi nue cloeths was all greest up and clayey, and I was daug-tierd.


















CHAPTER III.

Wel, I got a guud going-oever in th morning frum oeld Mis Watson on acount of mi cloeths; but th wido she didn’t scoeld, but oenly cleend off th grees and clay, and luukt so sorry that I thaut I wuud behaev awhiel if I cuud. Then Mis Watson she tuuk me in th clozet and prayd, but nuthing cum of it. She toeld me to pray evry day, and whutever I askt for I wuud get it. But it worn’t so. I tried it. Wuns I got a fish-lien, but no huuks. It worn’t eny guud to me without huuks. I tried for th huuks three or foer tiems, but sumhow I couldn’t maek it werk. Bi and bi, wun day, I askt Mis Watson to tri for me, but she sed I was a fool. She never toeld me whi, and I couldn’t maek it out no way.

I set doun wun tiem bak in th wuuds, and had a long think about it. I sez to mieself, if a body can get enything thay pray for, whi don’t Deecon Winn get bak th muny he lost on pork? Whi can’t th wido get bak her silver snufbox that was stoel? Whi can’t Mis Watson fat up? No, sez I to mi self, thair ain’t nuthing in it. I went and toeld th wido about it, and she sed th thing a body cuud get bi praying for it was “spirichual gifts.” This was too meny for me, but she toeld me whut she ment—I must help uther peepl, and do evrything I cuud for uther peepl, and luuk out for them all th tiem, and never think about mieself. This was inclooding Mis Watson, as I tuuk it. I went out in th wuuds and ternd it oever in mi miend a long tiem, but I couldn’t see no advantej about it—exsept for th uther peepl; so at last I rekond I wouldn’t wery about it eny mor, but just let it go. Sumtiems th wido wuud taek me wun sied and tauk about Providens in a way to maek a body’s mouth wauter; but maybe next day Mis Watson wuud taek hoeld and nok it all doun agen. I jujd I cuud see that thair was too Providenses, and a pur chap wuud stand considerabl sho with th wido’s Providens, but if Mis Watson’s got him thair worn’t no help for him eny mor. I thaut it all out, and rekond I wuud belong to th wido’s if he wonted me, tho I couldn’t maek out how he was a-going to be eny beter off then than whut he was befor, seeing I was so ignorant, and so kiend of lo-doun and ornery.

Pap he hadn’t bin seen for mor than a yeer, and that was cumfortabl for me; I didn’t wont to see him no mor. He uezd to allways whael me when he was soeber and cuud get his hands on me; tho I uezd to taek to th wuuds moest of th tiem when he was around. Wel, about this tiem he was found in th river drownded, about twelv miel abuv toun, so peepl sed. Thay jujd it was him, enyway; sed this drownded man was just his siez, and was raged, and had uncomon long hair, which was all liek pap; but thay couldn’t maek nuthing out of th faes, becauz it had bin in th wauter so long it worn’t much liek a faes at all. Thay sed he was floeting on his bak in th wauter. Thay tuuk him and berryd him on th bank. But I worn’t cumfortabl long, becauz I hapend to think of sumthing. I knowed miety wel that a drownded man don’t floet on his bak, but on his faes. So I knowed, then, that this worn’t pap, but a wuuman drest up in a man’s cloeths. So I was uncumfortabl agen. I jujd th oeld man wuud tern up agen bi and bi, tho I wisht he wouldn’t.

We playd rober now and then about a munth, and then I reziend. All th boys did. We hadn’t robd noebody, hadn’t kild eny peepl, but oenly just pretended. We uezd to hop out of th wuuds and go charjing doun on hog-drievers and wimen in carts taeking garden stuf to market, but we never hived eny of them. Tom Sawyer calld th hogs “ingots,” and he calld th ternips and stuf “julery,” and we wuud go to th caev and powwow oever whut we had dun, and how meny peepl we had kild and markt. But I couldn’t see no profit in it. Wun tiem Tom sent a boy to run about toun with a blaezing stik, which he calld a sloegan (which was th sien for th Gang to get together), and then he sed he had got seecret nues bi his spies that next day a hoel parsel of Spanish merchants and rich A-rabs was going to camp in Caev Holo with too hundred elefants, and six hundred camels, and oever a thouzand “sumter” muels, all loeded doun with di’monds, and thay didn’t hav oenly a gard of foer hundred soeljers, and so we wuud lay in ambuscaed, as he calld it, and kil th lot and scoop th things. He sed we must slik up our sords and guns, and get redy. He never cuud go after eeven a ternip-cart but he must hav th sords and guns all scourd up for it, tho thay was oenly lath and broomsticks, and u miet scour at them til u rotted, and then thay worn’t werth a mouthful of ashes mor than whut thay was befor. I didn’t beleev we cuud lik such a croud of Spaniards and A-rabs, but I wonted to see th camels and elefants, so I was on hand next day, Saturday, in th ambuscaed; and when we got th werd we rusht out of th wuuds and doun th hil. But thair worn’t no Spaniards and A-rabs, and thair worn’t no camels nor no elefants. It worn’t enything but a Sunday-scool picnik, and oenly a primer-clas at that. We busted it up, and chaest th children up th holo; but we never got enything but sum doughnuts and jam, tho Ben Rogers got a rag dol, and Jo Harper got a him-buuk and a tract; and then th teecher charjd in, and maed us drop evrything and cut.









I didn’t see no di’monds, and I toeld Tom Sawyer so. He sed thair was loeds of them thair, enyway; and he sed thair was A-rabs thair, too, and elefants and things. I sed, whi couldn’t we see them, then? He sed if I worn’t so ignorant, but had red a buuk calld Don Quixote, I wuud noe without asking. He sed it was all dun bi enchantment. He sed thair was hundreds of soeljers thair, and elefants and trezher, and so on, but we had enemys which he calld majishans; and thay had ternd th hoel thing into an infant Sunday-scool, just out of spiet. I sed, all riet; then th thing for us to do was to go for th majishans. Tom Sawyer sed I was a numskul.

“Whi,” sed he, “a majishan cuud call up a lot of genies, and thay wuud hash u up liek nuthing befor u cuud say Jak Robinson. Thay ar as tall as a tree and as big around as a cherch.”

“Wel,” I sez, “s’poez we got sum genies to help us—can’t we lik th uther croud then?”

“How u going to get them?”

“I don’t noe. How do thay get them?”

“Whi, thay rub an oeld tin lamp or an ieern ring, and then th genies cum tairing in, with th thunder and lietning a-riping around and th smoek a-roeling, and evrything thay’re toeld to do thay up and do it. Thay don’t think nuthing of puuling a shot-tower up bi th roots, and belting a Sunday-scool superintendent oever th hed with it—or eny uther man.”

“Hoo maeks them teer around so?”

“Whi, hooever rubs th lamp or th ring. Thay belong to hooever rubs th lamp or th ring, and thay’ve got to do whutever he sez. If he tels them to bild a palas forty miels long out of di’monds, and fil it fuul of chooing-gum, or whutever u wont, and fech an emperor’s dauter frum Chiena for u to marry, thay’ve got to do it—and thay’ve got to do it befor sun-up next morning, too. And mor: thay’ve got to wallts that palas around oever th cuntry whairever u wont it, u understand.”

“Wel,” sez I, “I think thay ar a pak of flat-heds for not keeping th palas themselvs ’sted of fooling them away liek that. And whut’s mor—if I was wun of them I wuud see a man in Jericho befor I wuud drop mi biznes and cum to him for th rubing of an oeld tin lamp.”

“How u tauk, Huck Finn. Whi, u’d hav to cum when he rubd it, whether u wonted to or not.”

“Whut! and I as hi as a tree and as big as a cherch? All riet, then; I wuud cum; but I lay I’d maek that man cliem th hieest tree thair was in th cuntry.”

“Shuks, it ain’t no ues to tauk to u, Huck Finn. U don’t seem to noe enything, sumhow—perfect saphead.”

I thaut all this oever for too or three days, and then I rekond I wuud see if thair was enything in it. I got an oeld tin lamp and an ieern ring, and went out in th wuuds and rubd and rubd til I swet liek an Injun, calcuelaeting to bild a palas and sel it; but it worn’t no ues, nun of th genies cum. So then I jujd that all that stuf was oenly just wun of Tom Sawyer’s lies. I rekond he beleevd in th A-rabs and th elefants, but as for me I think diferent. It had all th marks of a Sunday-scool.


















CHAPTER IV.

Wel, three or foer munths run along, and it was wel into th winter now. I had bin to scool moest all th tiem and cuud spel and red and riet just a litl, and cuud say th multiplicaeshun taebl up to six tiems seven is therty-fiev, and I don’t rekon I cuud ever get eny ferther than that if I was to liv forever. I don’t taek no stok in mathematics, enyway.

At ferst I haeted th scool, but bi and bi I got so I cuud stand it. Whenever I got uncomon tierd I playd hookey, and th hieding I got next day dun me guud and cheerd me up. So th longger I went to scool th eezyer it got to be. I was geting sort of uezd to th wido’s ways, too, and thay worn’t so raspy on me. Living in a hous and sleeping in a bed puuld on me prity tiet moestly, but befor th coeld wether I uezd to slied out and sleep in th wuuds sumtiems, and so that was a rest to me. I liekt th oeld ways best, but I was geting so I liekt th nue wuns, too, a litl bit. Th wido sed I was cuming along slo but shur, and doing verry satisfactory. She sed she worn’t ashaemd of me.

Wun morning I hapend to tern oever th sallt-selar at brekfast. I reecht for sum of it as qik as I cuud to thro oever mi left shoelder and keep off th bad luk, but Mis Watson was in ahed of me, and crosst me off. She sez, “Taek yur hands away, Huklberry; whut a mes u ar allways maeking!” Th wido puut in a guud werd for me, but that worn’t going to keep off th bad luk, I knowed that wel enuf. I started out, after brekfast, feeling weryd and shaeky, and wundering whair it was going to fall on me, and whut it was going to be. Thair is ways to keep off sum kiends of bad luk, but this wasn’t wun of them kiend; so I never tried to do enything, but just poekt along lo-spirited and on th woch-out.

I went doun to th frunt garden and clumb oever th stiel whair u go thru th hi bord fens. Thair was an inch of nue sno on th ground, and I seen sumbody’s traks. Thay had cum up frum th qorry and stuud around th stiel a whiel, and then went on around th garden fens. It was funy thay hadn’t cum in, after standing around so. I couldn’t maek it out. It was verry cuerius, sumhow. I was going to folo around, but I stoopt doun to luuk at th traks ferst. I didn’t noetis enything at ferst, but next I did. Thair was a cross in th left boot-heel maed with big naels, to keep off th devil.

I was up in a second and shinning doun th hil. I luukt oever mi shoelder evry now and then, but I didn’t see noebody. I was at Juj Thatcher’s as qik as I cuud get thair. He sed:

“Whi, mi boy, u ar all out of breth. Did u cum for yur interest?”

“No, ser,” I sez; “is thair sum for me?”

“O, yes, a haf-yeerly is in last niet—oever a hundred and fifty dolars. Qiet a forchun for u. U had beter let me invest it along with yur six thouzand, becauz if u taek it u’ll spend it.”

“No, ser,” I sez, “I don’t wont to spend it. I don’t wont it at all—nor th six thouzand, nuther. I wont u to taek it; I wont to giv it to u—th six thouzand and all.”









He luukt serpriezd. He couldn’t seem to maek it out. He sez:

“Whi, whut can u meen, mi boy?”

I sez, “Don’t u ask me no qeschuns about it, pleez. U’ll taek it—wun’t u?”

He sez:

“Wel, I’m puzld. Is sumthing th mater?”

“Pleez taek it,” sez I, “and don’t ask me nuthing—then I wun’t hav to tel no lies.”

He studyd a whiel, and then he sez:

“Oho-o! I think I see. U wont to sel all yur property to me—not giv it. That’s th corect iedeea.”

Then he roet sumthing on a paeper and red it oever, and sez:

“Thair; u see it sez ‘for a consideraeshun.’ That meens I hav baut it of u and paed u for it. Heer’s a dolar for u. Now u sien it.”

So I siend it, and left.

Mis Watson’s nigger, Jim, had a hair-ball as big as yur fist, which had bin tuuk out of th foerth stumac of an ox, and he uezd to do majic with it. He sed thair was a spirit insied of it, and it knowed evrything. So I went to him that niet and toeld him pap was heer agen, for I found his traks in th sno. Whut I wonted to noe was, whut he was going to do, and was he going to stay? Jim got out his hair-ball and sed sumthing oever it, and then he held it up and dropt it on th flor. It fel prity solid, and oenly roeld about an inch. Jim tried it agen, and then anuther tiem, and it acted just th saem. Jim got doun on his nees, and puut his eer agenst it and lisend. But it worn’t no ues; he sed it wouldn’t tauk. He sed sumtiems it wouldn’t tauk without muny. I toeld him I had an oeld slik counterfit qorter that worn’t no guud becauz th bras shoed thru th silver a litl, and it wouldn’t pas nohow, eeven if th bras didn’t sho, becauz it was so slik it felt greezy, and so that wuud tel on it evry tiem. (I rekond I wouldn’t say nuthing about th dolar I got frum th juj.) I sed it was prity bad muny, but maybe th hair-ball wuud taek it, becauz maybe it wouldn’t noe th diferens. Jim smelt it and bit it and rubd it, and sed he wuud manej so th hair-ball wuud think it was guud. He sed he wuud split oepen a raw Irish potaeto and stik th qorter in between and keep it thair all niet, and next morning u couldn’t see no bras, and it wouldn’t feel greezy no mor, and so enybody in toun wuud taek it in a minit, let aloen a hair-ball. Wel, I knowed a potaeto wuud do that befor, but I had forgot it.









Jim puut th qorter under th hair-ball, and got doun and lisend agen. This tiem he sed th hair-ball was all riet. He sed it wuud tel mi hoel forchun if I wonted it to. I sez, go on. So th hair-ball taukt to Jim, and Jim toeld it to me. He sez:

“Yo’ oelay faather doan’ noe yit whut he’s a-gwyne to do. Sumtiems he spec he’ll go ’way, en den agin he spec he’ll stay. De bes’ way is to res’ eezy en let de oelay man taek his oen way. Day’s too aenjels hoverin’ roun’ ’bout him. Wun uv ’em is whiet en shieny, en t’uther wun is blak. De whiet wun gits him to go riet a litl whiel, den de blak wun sael in en bust it all up. A body can’t tel yit which wun gwyne to fech him at de las’. But u is all riet. U gwyne to hav considable trubl in yo’ lief, en considable joy. Sumtiems u gwyne to git hert, en sumtiems u gwyne to git sik; but evry tiem u’s gwyne to git wel agin. Day’s too gals flyin’ ’bout u in yo’ lief. Wun uv ’em’s liet en t’uther wun is dark. Wun is rich en t’uther is po’. U’s gwyne to marry de po’ wun fust en de rich wun bi en bi. U wonts to keep ’way fum de wauter as much as u kin, en don’t run no resk, ’kase it’s doun in de bils dat u’s gwyne to git hung.”

When I lit mi candl and went up to mi room that niet thair sat pap his oen self!












CHAPTER V.

I had shut th dor to. Then I ternd around and thair he was. I uezd to be scaird of him all th tiem, he tand me so much. I rekond I was scaird now, too; but in a minit I see I was mistaeken—that is, after th ferst joelt, as u may say, when mi breth sort of hicht, he being so unexpected; but riet away after I see I worn’t scaird of him werth bothring about.

He was moest fifty, and he luukt it. His hair was long and tanggld and greezy, and hung doun, and u cuud see his ies shiening thru liek he was behiend viens. It was all blak, no gray; so was his long, mixt-up whiskers. Thair worn’t no culor in his faes, whair his faes shoed; it was whiet; not liek anuther man’s whiet, but a whiet to maek a body sik, a whiet to maek a body’s flesh crall—a tree-toed whiet, a fish-bely whiet. As for his cloeths—just rags, that was all. He had wun ankl resting on t’uther nee; th boot on that fuut was busted, and too of his toes stuk thru, and he werkt them now and then. His hat was laying on th flor—an oeld blak slouch with th top caevd in, liek a lid.

I stuud a-luuking at him; he set thair a-luuking at me, with his chair tilted bak a litl. I set th candl doun. I noetist th windo was up; so he had clumb in bi th shed. He kept a-luuking me all oever. Bi and bi he sez:

“Starchy cloeths—verry. U think u’re a guud deel of a big-bug, don’t u?”

“Maybe I am, maybe I ain’t,” I sez.

“Don’t u giv me nun o’ yur lip,” sez he. “U’ve puut on considerabl meny frils sinss I bin away. I’ll taek u doun a peg befor I get dun with u. U’re ejucaeted, too, thay say—can red and riet. U think u’re beter’n yur faather, now, don’t u, becauz he can’t? I’ll taek it out of u. Hoo toeld u u miet medl with such hifalut’n foolishnes, hay?—hoo toeld u u cuud?”

“Th wido. She toeld me.”

“Th wido, hay?—and hoo toeld th wido she cuud puut in her shuvel about a thing that ain’t nun of her biznes?”

“Noebody never toeld her.”

“Wel, I’ll lern her how to medl. And luuky heer—u drop that scool, u heer? I’ll lern peepl to bring up a boy to puut on airs oever his oen faather and let on to be beter’n whut he is. U lemme cach u fooling around that scool agen, u heer? Yur muther couldn’t red, and she couldn’t riet, nuther, befor she died. Nun of th family couldn’t befor thay died. I can’t; and heer u’re a-sweling yurself up liek this. I ain’t th man to stand it—u heer? Say, lemme heer u red.”

I tuuk up a buuk and begun sumthing about Jeneral Washington and th wors. When I’d red about a haf a minit, he fetched th buuk a whak with his hand and nokt it across th hous. He sez:

“It’s so. U can do it. I had mi douts when u toeld me. Now luuky heer; u stop that puuting on frils. I wun’t hav it. I’ll lay for u, mi smarty; and if I cach u about that scool I’ll tan u guud. Ferst u noe u’ll get relijon, too. I never see such a sun.”

He tuuk up a litl bloo and yaller pikcher of sum cows and a boy, and sez:

“Whut’s this?”

“It’s sumthing thay giv me for lerning mi lesons guud.”

He tore it up, and sez:

“I’ll giv u sumthing beter—I’ll giv u a cow-hied.”

He set thair a-mumbling and a-grouling a minit, and then he sez:

“Ain’t u a sweet-sented dandy, tho? A bed; and bedcloeths; and a luuk’n’-glas; and a pees of carpet on th flor—and yur oen faather got to sleep with th hogs in th tanyard. I never see such a sun. I bet I’ll taek sum o’ thees frils out o’ u befor I’m dun with u. Whi, thair ain’t no end to yur airs—thay say u’re rich. Hay?—how’s that?”









“Thay lie—that’s how.”

“Luuky heer—miend how u tauk to me; I’m a-standing about all I can stand now—so don’t gimme no sass. I’ve bin in toun too days, and I hain’t herd nuthing but about u bein’ rich. I herd about it away doun th river, too. That’s whi I cum. U git me that muny to-morro—I wont it.”

“I hain’t got no muny.”

“It’s a lie. Juj Thatcher’s got it. U git it. I wont it.”

“I hain’t got no muny, I tel u. U ask Juj Thatcher; he’ll tel u th saem.”

“All riet. I’ll ask him; and I’ll maek him pungle, too, or I’ll noe th reezon whi. Say, how much u got in yur poket? I wont it.”

“I hain’t got oenly a dolar, and I wont that to—”

“It don’t maek no diferens whut u wont it for—u just shel it out.”

He tuuk it and bit it to see if it was guud, and then he sed he was going doun toun to get sum whisky; sed he hadn’t had a drink all day. When he had got out on th shed he puut his hed in agen, and cussed me for puuting on frils and trieing to be beter than him; and when I rekond he was gon he cum bak and puut his hed in agen, and toeld me to miend about that scool, becauz he was going to lay for me and lik me if I didn’t drop that.

Next day he was drunk, and he went to Juj Thatcher’s and bullyragged him, and tried to maek him giv up th muny; but he couldn’t, and then he swor he’d maek th law fors him.

Th juj and th wido went to law to get th cort to taek me away frum him and let wun of them be mi gardian; but it was a nue juj that had just cum, and he didn’t noe th oeld man; so he sed corts mustn’t interfeer and separaet familys if thay cuud help it; sed he’d druther not taek a chield away frum its faather. So Juj Thatcher and th wido had to qit on th biznes.

That pleezd th oeld man til he couldn’t rest. He sed he’d cow-hied me til I was blak and bloo if I didn’t raez sum muny for him. I borroed three dolars frum Juj Thatcher, and pap tuuk it and got drunk, and went a-bloeing around and cussing and hooping and carrying on; and he kept it up all oever toun, with a tin pan, til moest midniet; then thay jaeld him, and next day thay had him befor cort, and jaeld him agen for a week. But he sed he was satisfied; sed he was boss of his sun, and he’d maek it worm for him.

When he got out th nue juj sed he was a-going to maek a man of him. So he tuuk him to his oen hous, and drest him up cleen and nies, and had him to brekfast and diner and super with th family, and was just oeld pi to him, so to speek. And after super he taukt to him about temperans and such things til th oeld man cried, and sed he’d bin a fool, and foold away his lief; but now he was a-going to tern oever a nue leef and be a man noebody wouldn’t be ashaemd of, and he hoept th juj wuud help him and not luuk doun on him. Th juj sed he cuud hug him for them werds; so he cried, and his wief she cried agen; pap sed he’d bin a man that had allways bin misunderstuud befor, and th juj sed he beleevd it. Th oeld man sed that whut a man wonted that was doun was simpathy, and th juj sed it was so; so thay cried agen. And when it was bedtiem th oeld man roez up and held out his hand, and sez:

“Luuk at it, jentlmen and laedys all; taek a-hoeld of it; shaek it. Thair’s a hand that was th hand of a hog; but it ain’t so no mor; it’s th hand of a man that’s started in on a nue lief, and’ll die befor he’ll go bak. U mark them werds—don’t forget I sed them. It’s a cleen hand now; shaek it—don’t be afeard.”









So thay shuuk it, wun after th uther, all around, and cried. Th juj’s wief she kist it. Then th oeld man he siend a plej—maed his mark. Th juj sed it was th holiest tiem on record, or sumthing liek that. Then thay tukt th oeld man into a buetiful room, which was th spair room, and in th niet sum tiem he got powerful thersty and clumb out on to th porch-roof and slid doun a stanshun and traeded his nue coet for a jug of forty-rod, and clumb bak agen and had a guud oeld tiem; and tords dayliet he cralld out agen, drunk as a fidler, and roeld off th porch and broek his left arm in too plaeses, and was moest froez to deth when sumbody found him after sun-up. And when thay cum to luuk at that spair room thay had to taek soundings befor thay cuud navigaet it.

Th juj he felt kiend of sor. He sed he rekond a body cuud reform th oeld man with a shotgun, maybe, but he didn’t noe no uther way.
















CHAPTER VI.

Wel, prity soon th oeld man was up and around agen, and then he went for Juj Thatcher in th corts to maek him giv up that muny, and he went for me, too, for not stoping scool. He catched me a cupl of tiems and thrasht me, but I went to scool just th saem, and dojd him or outrun him moest of th tiem. I didn’t wont to go to scool much befor, but I rekond I’d go now to spiet pap. That law trieal was a slo biznes—apeerd liek thay worn’t ever going to get started on it; so evry now and then I’d borro too or three dolars off of th juj for him, to keep frum geting a cowhiding. Evry tiem he got muny he got drunk; and evry tiem he got drunk he raezd Cain around toun; and evry tiem he raezd Cain he got jaeld. He was just sooted—this kiend of thing was riet in his lien.

He got to hanging around th wido’s too much and so she toeld him at last that if he didn’t qit uezing around thair she wuud maek trubl for him. Wel, wasn’t he mad? He sed he wuud sho hoo was Huck Finn’s boss. So he wocht out for me wun day in th spring, and catched me, and tuuk me up th river about three miel in a skif, and crosst oever to th Illinois shor whair it was woody and thair worn’t no houses but an oeld log hut in a plaes whair th timber was so thik u couldn’t fiend it if u didn’t noe whair it was.

He kept me with him all th tiem, and I never got a chans to run off. We livd in that oeld cabin, and he allways lokt th dor and puut th kee under his hed niets. He had a gun which he had stoel, I rekon, and we fished and hunted, and that was whut we livd on. Evry litl whiel he lokt me in and went doun to th stor, three miels, to th ferry, and traeded fish and gaem for whisky, and fetched it hoem and got drunk and had a guud tiem, and likt me. Th wido she found out whair I was bi and bi, and she sent a man oever to tri to get hoeld of me; but pap droev him off with th gun, and it worn’t long after that til I was uezd to being whair I was, and liekt it—all but th cow-hied part.

It was kiend of laezy and joly, laying off cumfortabl all day, smoeking and fishing, and no buuks nor study. Too munths or mor run along, and mi cloeths got to be all rags and dert, and I didn’t see how I’d ever got to liek it so wel at th wido’s, whair u had to wosh, and eet on a plaet, and coem up, and go to bed and get up reguelar, and be forever bothering oever a buuk, and hav oeld Mis Watson pecking at u all th tiem. I didn’t wont to go bak no mor. I had stopt cussing, becauz th wido didn’t liek it; but now I tuuk to it agen becauz pap hadn’t no objecshuns. It was prity guud tiems up in th wuuds thair, taek it all around.









But bi and bi pap got too handy with his hik’ry, and I couldn’t stand it. I was all oever welts. He got to going away so much, too, and loking me in. Wuns he lokt me in and was gon three days. It was dredful loensum. I jujd he had got drownded, and I wasn’t ever going to get out eny mor. I was scaird. I maed up mi miend I wuud fix up sum way to leev thair. I had tried to get out of that cabin meny a tiem, but I couldn’t fiend no way. Thair worn’t a windo to it big enuf for a daug to get thru. I couldn’t get up th chimbly; it was too narro. Th dor was thik, solid oek slabs. Pap was prity cairful not to leev a nief or enything in th cabin when he was away; I rekon I had hunted th plaes oever as much as a hundred tiems; wel, I was moest all th tiem at it, becauz it was about th oenly way to puut in th tiem. But this tiem I found sumthing at last; I found an oeld rusty wuud-saw without eny handl; it was laed in between a rafter and th clapboards of th roof. I greest it up and went to werk. Thair was an oeld hors-blanket naeld agenst th logs at th far end of th cabin behiend th taebl, to keep th wiend frum bloeing thru th chinks and puuting th candl out. I got under th taebl and raezd th blanket, and went to werk to saw a secshun of th big botom log out—big enuf to let me thru. Wel, it was a guud long job, but I was geting tords th end of it when I herd pap’s gun in th wuuds. I got rid of th siens of mi werk, and dropt th blanket and hid mi saw, and prity soon pap cum in.

Pap worn’t in a guud huemor—so he was his nacheral self. He sed he was doun toun, and evrything was going rong. His lawyer sed he rekond he wuud win his lawsoot and get th muny if thay ever got started on th trieal; but then thair was ways to puut it off a long tiem, and Juj Thatcher knowed how to do it. And he sed peepl alowd thair’d be anuther trieal to get me away frum him and giv me to th wido for mi gardian, and thay gest it wuud win this tiem. This shuuk me up considerabl, becauz I didn’t wont to go bak to th wido’s eny mor and be so cramped up and sivilized, as thay calld it. Then th oeld man got to cussing, and cussed evrything and evrybody he cuud think of, and then cussed them all oever agen to maek shur he hadn’t skipt eny, and after that he polisht off with a kiend of a jeneral cuss all round, inclooding a considerabl parsel of peepl which he didn’t noe th naems of, and so calld them whut’s-his-naem when he got to them, and went riet along with his cussing.

He sed he wuud liek to see th wido get me. He sed he wuud woch out, and if thay tried to cum eny such gaem on him he knowed of a plaes six or seven miel off to stow me in, whair thay miet hunt til thay dropt and thay couldn’t fiend me. That maed me prity uneezy agen, but oenly for a minit; I rekond I wouldn’t stay on hand til he got that chans.

Th oeld man maed me go to th skif and fech th things he had got. Thair was a fifty-pound sak of corn meel, and a sied of baecon, amuenishun, and a foer-galon jug of whisky, and an oeld buuk and too nuespaepers for woding, besieds sum toe. I toeted up a loed, and went bak and set doun on th bo of th skif to rest. I thaut it all oever, and I rekond I wuud wauk off with th gun and sum liens, and taek to th wuuds when I run away. I gest I wouldn’t stay in wun plaes, but just tramp riet across th cuntry, moestly niet tiems, and hunt and fish to keep aliev, and so get so far away that th oeld man nor th wido couldn’t ever fiend me eny mor. I jujd I wuud saw out and leev that niet if pap got drunk enuf, and I rekond he wuud. I got so fuul of it I didn’t noetis how long I was staying til th oeld man holerd and askt me whether I was asleep or drownded.









I got th things all up to th cabin, and then it was about dark. Whiel I was cuuking super th oeld man tuuk a swig or too and got sort of wormd up, and went to riping agen. He had bin drunk oever in toun, and laed in th guter all niet, and he was a siet to luuk at. A body wuud a thaut he was Adam—he was just all mud. Whenever his likor begun to werk he moest allways went for th govment, this tiem he sez:

“Call this a govment! whi, just luuk at it and see whut it’s liek. Heer’s th law a-standing redy to taek a man’s sun away frum him—a man’s oen sun, which he has had all th trubl and all th angzieity and all th expens of raezing. Yes, just as that man has got that sun raezd at last, and redy to go to werk and begin to do suthin’ for him and giv him a rest, th law up and goes for him. And thay call that govment! That ain’t all, nuther. Th law baks that oeld Juj Thatcher up and helps him to keep me out o’ mi property. Heer’s whut th law duz: Th law taeks a man werth six thouzand dolars and up’ards, and jams him into an oeld trap of a cabin liek this, and lets him go round in cloeths that ain’t fitten for a hog. Thay call that govment! A man can’t get his riets in a govment liek this. Sumtiems I’ve a miety noeshun to just leev th cuntry for guud and all. Yes, and I toeld ’em so; I toeld oeld Thatcher so to his faes. Lots of ’em herd me, and can tel whut I sed. Sez I, for too sents I’d leev th blaemd cuntry and never cum a-neer it agin. Them’s th verry werds. I sez luuk at mi hat—if u call it a hat—but th lid raezes up and th rest of it goes doun til it’s belo mi chin, and then it ain’t rietly a hat at all, but mor liek mi hed was shuvd up thru a jint o’ stoev-piep. Luuk at it, sez I—such a hat for me to wair—wun of th welthyest men in this toun if I cuud git mi riets.

“O, yes, this is a wunderful govment, wunderful. Whi, luuky heer. Thair was a free nigger thair frum Ohio—a mulatter, moest as whiet as a whiet man. He had th whitest shert on u ever see, too, and th shiniest hat; and thair ain’t a man in that toun that’s got as fien cloeths as whut he had; and he had a goeld woch and chaen, and a silver-heded caen—th awfulest oeld gray-heded naebob in th Staet. And whut do u think? Thay sed he was a p’fessor in a colej, and cuud tauk all kiends of langgwejes, and knowed evrything. And that ain’t th wust. Thay sed he cuud voet when he was at hoem. Wel, that let me out. Thinks I, whut is th cuntry a-cuming to? It was ’lection day, and I was just about to go and voet mieself if I worn’t too drunk to get thair; but when thay toeld me thair was a Staet in this cuntry whair thay’d let that nigger voet, I drawed out. I sez I’ll never voet agin. Them’s th verry werds I sed; thay all herd me; and th cuntry may rot for all me—I’ll never voet agin as long as I liv. And to see th cool way of that nigger—whi, he wouldn’t a giv me th roed if I hadn’t shuvd him out o’ th way. I sez to th peepl, whi ain’t this nigger puut up at aucshun and soeld?—that’s whut I wont to noe. And whut do u rekon thay sed? Whi, thay sed he couldn’t be soeld til he’d bin in th Staet six munths, and he hadn’t bin thair that long yet. Thair, now—that’s a spesimen. Thay call that a govment that can’t sel a free nigger til he’s bin in th Staet six munths. Heer’s a govment that calls itself a govment, and lets on to be a govment, and thinks it is a govment, and yet’s got to set stok-stil for six hoel munths befor it can taek a hoeld of a prouling, theeving, infernal, whiet-shirted free nigger, and—”

Pap was agoing on so he never noetist whair his oeld limber legs was taeking him to, so he went hed oever heels oever th tub of sallt pork and barked boeth shins, and th rest of his speech was all th hotest kiend of langgwej—moestly hoev at th nigger and th govment, tho he giv th tub sum, too, all along, heer and thair. He hopt around th cabin considerabl, ferst on wun leg and then on th uther, hoelding ferst wun shin and then th uther wun, and at last he let out with his left fuut all of a suden and fetched th tub a ratling kik. But it worn’t guud jujment, becauz that was th boot that had a cupl of his toes leaking out of th frunt end of it; so now he raezd a houl that fairly maed a body’s hair raez, and doun he went in th dert, and roeld thair, and held his toes; and th cussing he dun then laed oever enything he had ever dun preevius. He sed so his oen self afterwards. He had herd oeld Sowberry Hagan in his best days, and he sed it laed oever him, too; but I rekon that was sort of pieling it on, maybe.

After super pap tuuk th jug, and sed he had enuf whisky thair for too drunks and wun deleerium tremens. That was allways his werd. I jujd he wuud be bliend drunk in about an our, and then I wuud steel th kee, or saw mieself out, wun or t’uther. He drank and drank, and tumbld doun on his blankets bi and bi; but luk didn’t run mi way. He didn’t go sound asleep, but was uneezy. He groend and moend and thrasht around this way and that for a long tiem. At last I got so sleepy I couldn’t keep mi ies oepen all I cuud do, and so befor I knowed whut I was about I was sound asleep, and th candl berning.









I don’t noe how long I was asleep, but all of a suden thair was an awful screem and I was up. Thair was pap luuking wield, and skiping around evry which way and yeling about snaeks. He sed thay was cralling up his legs; and then he wuud giv a jump and screem, and say wun had bit him on th cheek—but I couldn’t see no snaeks. He started and run round and round th cabin, holering “Taek him off! taek him off! he’s bieting me on th nek!” I never see a man luuk so wield in th ies. Prity soon he was all fagd out, and fel doun panting; then he roeld oever and oever wunderful fast, kiking things evry which way, and strieking and grabing at th air with his hands, and screeming and saying thair was devils a-hoeld of him. He wor out bi and bi, and laed stil a whiel, moaning. Then he laed stiller, and didn’t maek a sound. I cuud heer th ouls and th wuulvs away off in th wuuds, and it seemd terribl stil. He was laying oever bi th corner. Bi and bi he raezd up part way and lisend, with his hed to wun sied. He sez, verry lo:

“Tramp—tramp—tramp; that’s th ded; tramp—tramp—tramp; thay’re cuming after me; but I wun’t go. O, thay’re heer! don’t tuch me—don’t! hands off—thay’re coeld; let go. O, let a pur devil aloen!”

Then he went doun on all foers and cralld off, beging them to let him aloen, and he roeld himself up in his blanket and woloed in under th oeld pien taebl, stil a-beging; and then he went to crieing. I cuud heer him thru th blanket.

Bi and bi he roeld out and jumpt up on his feet luuking wield, and he see me and went for me. He chaest me round and round th plaes with a clasp-nief, calling me th Aenjel of Deth, and saying he wuud kil me, and then I couldn’t cum for him no mor. I begd, and toeld him I was oenly Huck; but he laft such a screechy laf, and rord and cussed, and kept on chaesing me up. Wuns when I ternd short and dojd under his arm he maed a grab and got me bi th jaket between mi shoelders, and I thaut I was gon; but I slid out of th jaket qik as lietning, and saevd mieself. Prity soon he was all tierd out, and dropt doun with his bak agenst th dor, and sed he wuud rest a minit and then kil me. He puut his nief under him, and sed he wuud sleep and get strong, and then he wuud see hoo was hoo.

So he doezd off prity soon. Bi and bi I got th oeld split-botom chair and clumb up as eezy as I cuud, not to maek eny noiz, and got doun th gun. I slipt th ramrod doun it to maek shur it was loeded, then I laed it across th ternip barrel, pointing tords pap, and set doun behiend it to waet for him to ster. And how slo and stil th tiem did drag along.












CHAPTER VII.

“Git up! Whut u ’bout?”

I oepend mi ies and luukt around, trieing to maek out whair I was. It was after sun-up, and I had bin sound asleep. Pap was standing oever me luuking sour and sik, too. He sez:

“Whut u doin’ with this gun?”

I jujd he didn’t noe nuthing about whut he had bin doing, so I sez:

“Sumbody tried to get in, so I was laying for him.”

“Whi didn’t u roust me out?”

“Wel, I tried to, but I couldn’t; I couldn’t buj u.”

“Wel, all riet. Don’t stand thair palavering all day, but out with u and see if thair’s a fish on th liens for brekfast. I’ll be along in a minit.”

He unlokt th dor, and I cleerd out up th river-bank. I noetist sum peeses of lims and such things floeting doun, and a sprinkling of bark; so I knowed th river had begun to riez. I rekond I wuud hav graet tiems now if I was oever at th toun. Th June riez uezd to be allways luk for me; becauz as soon as that riez begins heer cums cordwood floeting doun, and peeses of log rafts—sumtiems a duzen logs together; so all u hav to do is to cach them and sel them to th wuud-yards and th sawmil.

I went along up th bank with wun ie out for pap and t’uther wun out for whut th riez miet fech along. Wel, all at wuns heer cums a canoo; just a buety, too, about therteen or forteen fuut long, rieding hi liek a duk. I shot hed-ferst off of th bank liek a frog, cloeths and all on, and struk out for th canoo. I just expected thair’d be sumbody laying doun in it, becauz peepl offen dun that to fool foeks, and when a chap had puuld a skif out moest to it thay’d raez up and laf at him. But it worn’t so this tiem. It was a drift-canoo shur enuf, and I clumb in and paddled her ashor. Thinks I, th oeld man wil be glad when he sees this—she’s werth ten dolars. But when I got to shor pap wasn’t in siet yet, and as I was runing her into a litl creek liek a guly, all hung oever with viens and wiloes, I struk anuther iedeea: I jujd I’d hied her guud, and then, ’sted of taeking to th wuuds when I run off, I’d go doun th river about fifty miel and camp in wun plaes for guud, and not hav such a ruf tiem tramping on fuut.









It was prity cloez to th shanty, and I thaut I herd th oeld man cuming all th tiem; but I got her hid; and then I out and luukt around a bunch of wiloes, and thair was th oeld man doun th path a pees just drawing a beed on a berd with his gun. So he hadn’t seen enything.

When he got along I was hard at it taeking up a “trot” lien. He abuezd me a litl for being so slo; but I toeld him I fel in th river, and that was whut maed me so long. I knowed he wuud see I was wet, and then he wuud be asking qeschuns. We got fiev catfish off th liens and went hoem.

Whiel we laed off after brekfast to sleep up, boeth of us being about wor out, I got to thinking that if I cuud fix up sum way to keep pap and th wido frum trieing to folo me, it wuud be a certainer thing than trusting to luk to get far enuf off befor thay mist me; u see, all kiends of things miet hapen. Wel, I didn’t see no way for a whiel, but bi and bi pap raezd up a minit to drink anuther barrel of wauter, and he sez:

“Anuther tiem a man cums a-prouling round heer u roust me out, u heer? That man worn’t heer for no guud. I’d a shot him. Next tiem u roust me out, u heer?”

Then he dropt doun and went to sleep agen; but whut he had bin saying giv me th verry iedeea I wonted. I sez to mieself, I can fix it now so noebody wun’t think of foloeing me.

About twelv o’clok we ternd out and went along up th bank. Th river was cuming up prity fast, and lots of driftwuud going bi on th riez. Bi and bi along cums part of a log raft—nien logs fast together. We went out with th skif and toed it ashor. Then we had diner. Enybody but pap wuud a waeted and seen th day thru, so as to cach mor stuf; but that worn’t pap’s stiel. Nien logs was enuf for wun tiem; he must shuv riet oever to toun and sel. So he lokt me in and tuuk th skif, and started off towing th raft about haf-past three. I jujd he wouldn’t cum bak that niet. I waeted til I rekond he had got a guud start; then I out with mi saw, and went to werk on that log agen. Befor he was t’uther sied of th river I was out of th hoel; him and his raft was just a spek on th wauter away off yonder.

I tuuk th sak of corn meel and tuuk it to whair th canoo was hid, and shuvd th viens and branches apart and puut it in; then I dun th saem with th sied of baecon; then th whisky-jug. I tuuk all th coffy and shuugar thair was, and all th amuenishun; I tuuk th woding; I tuuk th buket and gord; I tuuk a diper and a tin cup, and mi oeld saw and too blankets, and th skilet and th coffy-pot. I tuuk fish-liens and maches and uther things—evrything that was werth a sent. I cleend out th plaes. I wonted an ax, but thair wasn’t eny, oenly th wun out at th wuudpiel, and I knowed whi I was going to leev that. I fetched out th gun, and now I was dun.

I had wor th ground a guud deel cralling out of th hoel and draging out so meny things. So I fixt that as guud as I cuud frum th outsied bi scatering dust on th plaes, which cuverd up th smoothnes and th sawdust. Then I fixt th pees of log bak into its plaes, and puut too roks under it and wun agenst it to hoeld it thair, for it was bent up at that plaes and didn’t qiet tuch ground. If u stuud foer or fiev fuut away and didn’t noe it was sawd, u wouldn’t never noetis it; and besieds, this was th bak of th cabin, and it worn’t liekly enybody wuud go fooling around thair.

It was all gras cleer to th canoo, so I hadn’t left a trak. I foloed around to see. I stuud on th bank and luukt out oever th river. All saef. So I tuuk th gun and went up a pees into th wuuds, and was hunting around for sum berds when I see a wield pig; hogs soon went wield in them botoms after thay had got away frum th prairy farms. I shot this felo and tuuk him into camp.









I tuuk th ax and smasht in th dor. I beet it and hakt it considerabl a-doing it. I fetched th pig in, and tuuk him bak neerly to th taebl and hakt into his throet with th ax, and laed him doun on th ground to bleed; I say ground becauz it was ground—hard pakt, and no bords. Wel, next I tuuk an oeld sak and puut a lot of big roks in it—all I cuud drag—and I started it frum th pig, and dragd it to th dor and thru th wuuds doun to th river and dumpt it in, and doun it sunk, out of siet. U cuud eezy see that sumthing had bin dragd oever th ground. I did wish Tom Sawyer was thair; I knowed he wuud taek an interest in this kiend of biznes, and thro in th fansy tuches. Noebody cuud spred himself liek Tom Sawyer in such a thing as that.

Wel, last I puuld out sum of mi hair, and bluded th ax guud, and stuk it on th bak sied, and slung th ax in th corner. Then I tuuk up th pig and held him to mi brest with mi jaket (so he couldn’t drip) til I got a guud pees belo th hous and then dumpt him into th river. Now I thaut of sumthing els. So I went and got th bag of meel and mi oeld saw out of th canoo, and fetched them to th hous. I tuuk th bag to whair it uezd to stand, and ript a hoel in th botom of it with th saw, for thair worn’t no nievs and forks on th plaes—pap dun evrything with his clasp-nief about th cuuking. Then I carryd th sak about a hundred yards across th gras and thru th wiloes eest of th hous, to a shalo laek that was fiev miel wied and fuul of rushes—and duks too, u miet say, in th seezon. Thair was a sluf or a creek leding out of it on th uther sied that went miels away, I don’t noe whair, but it didn’t go to th river. Th meel sifted out and maed a litl trak all th way to th laek. I dropt pap’s whetstoen thair too, so as to luuk liek it had bin dun bi acsident. Then I tied up th rip in th meel sak with a string, so it wouldn’t leek no mor, and tuuk it and mi saw to th canoo agen.

It was about dark now; so I dropt th canoo doun th river under sum wiloes that hung oever th bank, and waeted for th moon to riez. I maed fast to a wilo; then I tuuk a biet to eet, and bi and bi laed doun in th canoo to smoek a piep and lay out a plan. I sez to mieself, thay’ll folo th trak of that sakful of roks to th shor and then drag th river for me. And thay’ll folo that meel trak to th laek and go brouzing doun th creek that leeds out of it to fiend th robers that kild me and tuuk th things. Thay wun’t ever hunt th river for enything but mi ded carcas. Thay’ll soon get tierd of that, and wun’t bother no mor about me. All riet; I can stop enywhair I wont to. Jackson’s Ieland is guud enuf for me; I noe that ieland prity wel, and noebody ever cums thair. And then I can padl oever to toun niets, and slink around and pik up things I wont. Jackson’s Ieland’s th plaes.

I was prity tierd, and th ferst thing I knowed I was asleep. When I woek up I didn’t noe whair I was for a minit. I set up and luukt around, a litl scaird. Then I rememberd. Th river luukt miels and miels across. Th moon was so briet I cuud a counted th drift logs that went a-sliping along, blak and stil, hundreds of yards out frum shor. Evrything was ded qieet, and it luukt laet, and smelt laet. U noe whut I meen—I don’t noe th werds to puut it in.

I tuuk a guud gap and a strech, and was just going to unhitch and start when I herd a sound away oever th wauter. I lisend. Prity soon I maed it out. It was that dul kiend of a reguelar sound that cums frum ors werking in rowlocks when it’s a stil niet. I peeped out thru th wilo branches, and thair it was—a skif, away across th wauter. I couldn’t tel how meny was in it. It kept a-cuming, and when it was abrest of me I see thair worn’t but wun man in it. Think’s I, maybe it’s pap, tho I worn’t expecting him. He dropt belo me with th curent, and bi and bi he caem a-swinging up shor in th eezy wauter, and he went bi so cloez I cuud a reecht out th gun and tucht him. Wel, it was pap, shur enuf—and soeber, too, bi th way he laed his ors.

I didn’t looz no tiem. Th next minit I was a-spining doun streem sofft but qik in th shaed of th bank. I maed too miel and a haf, and then struk out a qorter of a miel or mor tords th midl of th river, becauz prity soon I wuud be pasing th ferry landing, and peepl miet see me and hael me. I got out amungst th driftwuud, and then laed doun in th botom of th canoo and let her floet.









I laed thair, and had a guud rest and a smoek out of mi piep, luuking away into th skie; not a cloud in it. Th skie luuks ever so deep when u lay doun on yur bak in th moonshien; I never knowed it befor. And how far a body can heer on th wauter such niets! I herd peepl tauking at th ferry landing. I herd whut thay sed, too—evry werd of it. Wun man sed it was geting tords th long days and th short niets now. T’uther wun sed this worn’t wun of th short wuns, he rekond—and then thay laft, and he sed it oever agen, and thay laft agen; then thay waekt up anuther felo and toeld him, and laft, but he didn’t laf; he ript out sumthing brisk, and sed let him aloen. Th ferst felo sed he ’lowed to tel it to his oeld wuuman—she wuud think it was prity guud; but he sed that worn’t nuthing to sum things he had sed in his tiem. I herd wun man say it was neerly three o’clok, and he hoept dayliet wouldn’t waet mor than about a week longger. After that th tauk got ferther and ferther away, and I couldn’t maek out th werds eny mor; but I cuud heer th mumbl, and now and then a laf, too, but it seemd a long ways off.

I was away belo th ferry now. I roez up, and thair was Jackson’s Ieland, about too miel and a haf doun streem, hevy timberd and standing up out of th midl of th river, big and dark and solid, liek a steemboet without eny liets. Thair worn’t eny siens of th bar at th hed—it was all under wauter now.

It didn’t taek me long to get thair. I shot past th hed at a riping raet, th curent was so swift, and then I got into th ded wauter and landed on th sied tords th Illinois shor. I run th canoo into a deep dent in th bank that I knowed about; I had to part th wilo branches to get in; and when I maed fast noebody cuud a seen th canoo frum th outsied.

I went up and set doun on a log at th hed of th ieland, and luukt out on th big river and th blak driftwuud and away oever to th toun, three miel away, whair thair was three or foer liets twinkling. A monstrus big lumber-raft was about a miel up streem, cuming along doun, with a lantern in th midl of it. I wocht it cum creeping doun, and when it was moest abrest of whair I stuud I herd a man say, “Stern ors, thair! heev her hed to stabboard!” I herd that just as plaen as if th man was bi mi sied.

Thair was a litl gray in th skie now; so I stept into th wuuds, and laed doun for a nap befor brekfast.












CHAPTER VIII.

Th sun was up so hi when I waekt that I jujd it was after aet o’clok. I laed thair in th gras and th cool shaed thinking about things, and feeling rested and ruther cumfortabl and satisfied. I cuud see th sun out at wun or too hoels, but moestly it was big trees all about, and gloomy in thair amungst them. Thair was frekld plaeses on th ground whair th liet sifted doun thru th leevs, and th frekld plaeses swapped about a litl, shoeing thair was a litl breez up thair. A cupl of sqerels set on a lim and jabbered at me verry frendly.

I was powerful laezy and cumfortabl—didn’t wont to get up and cuuk brekfast. Wel, I was doezing off agen when I thinks I heers a deep sound of “boom!” away up th river. I rouses up, and rests on mi elbo and lisens; prity soon I heers it agen. I hopt up, and went and luukt out at a hoel in th leevs, and I see a bunch of smoek laying on th wauter a long ways up—about abrest th ferry. And thair was th ferryboet fuul of peepl floeting along doun. I knowed whut was th mater now. “Boom!” I see th whiet smoek sqert out of th ferryboet’s sied. U see, thay was fiering canon oever th wauter, trieing to maek mi carcas cum to th top.

I was prity hunggry, but it worn’t going to do for me to start a fier, becauz thay miet see th smoek. So I set thair and wocht th canon-smoek and lisend to th boom. Th river was a miel wied thair, and it allways luuks prity on a sumer morning—so I was having a guud enuf tiem seeing them hunt for mi remainders if I oenly had a biet to eet. Wel, then I hapend to think how thay allways puut qiksilver in loevs of bred and floet them off, becauz thay allways go riet to th drownded carcas and stop thair. So, sez I, I’ll keep a luukout, and if eny of them’s floeting around after me I’ll giv them a sho. I chaenjd to th Illinois ej of th ieland to see whut luk I cuud hav, and I worn’t disapointed. A big dubl loef cum along, and I moest got it with a long stik, but mi fuut slipt and she floeted out ferther. Of cors I was whair th curent set in th cloesest to th shor—I knowed enuf for that. But bi and bi along cums anuther wun, and this tiem I wun. I tuuk out th plug and shuuk out th litl dab of qiksilver, and set mi teeth in. It was “baeker’s bred”—whut th qolity eet; nun of yur lo-doun corn-pone.

I got a guud plaes amungst th leevs, and set thair on a log, munching th bred and woching th ferry-boet, and verry wel satisfied. And then sumthing struk me. I sez, now I rekon th wido or th parson or sumbody prayd that this bred wuud fiend me, and heer it has gon and dun it. So thair ain’t no dout but thair is sumthing in that thing—that is, thair’s sumthing in it when a body liek th wido or th parson prays, but it don’t werk for me, and I rekon it don’t werk for oenly just th riet kiend.









I lit a piep and had a guud long smoek, and went on woching. Th ferryboet was floeting with th curent, and I alowd I’d hav a chans to see hoo was abord when she cum along, becauz she wuud cum in cloez, whair th bred did. When she’d got prity wel along doun tords me, I puut out mi piep and went to whair I fished out th bred, and laed doun behiend a log on th bank in a litl oepen plaes. Whair th log forkt I cuud peep thru.

Bi and bi she cum along, and she drifted in so cloez that thay cuud a run out a plank and waukt ashor. Moest evrybody was on th boet. Pap, and Juj Thatcher, and Bessie Thatcher, and Jo Harper, and Tom Sawyer, and his oeld Ant Polly, and Sid and Mary, and plenty mor. Evrybody was tauking about th merder, but th capten broek in and sez:

“Luuk sharp, now; th curent sets in th cloesest heer, and maybe he’s wosht ashor and got tanggld amungst th brush at th wauter’s ej. I hoep so, enyway.”

I didn’t hoep so. Thay all crouded up and leend oever th raels, neerly in mi faes, and kept stil, woching with all thair miet. I cuud see them ferst-raet, but thay couldn’t see me. Then th capten sung out:

“Stand away!” and th canon let off such a blast riet befor me that it maed me deef with th noiz and prity neer bliend with th smoek, and I jujd I was gon. If thay’d a had sum buulets in, I rekon thay’d a got th corps thay was after. Wel, I see I worn’t hert, thanks to guudnes. Th boet floeted on and went out of siet around th shoelder of th ieland. I cuud heer th booming now and then, ferther and ferther off, and bi and bi, after an our, I didn’t heer it no mor. Th ieland was three miel long. I jujd thay had got to th fuut, and was giving it up. But thay didn’t yet a whiel. Thay ternd around th fuut of th ieland and started up th chanel on th Missouri sied, under steem, and booming wuns in a whiel as thay went. I crosst oever to that sied and wocht them. When thay got abrest th hed of th ieland thay qit shooting and dropt oever to th Missouri shor and went hoem to th toun.

I knowed I was all riet now. Noebody els wuud cum a-hunting after me. I got mi traps out of th canoo and maed me a nies camp in th thik wuuds. I maed a kiend of a tent out of mi blankets to puut mi things under so th raen couldn’t get at them. I catched a catfish and haggled him oepen with mi saw, and tords sundoun I started mi camp fier and had super. Then I set out a lien to cach sum fish for brekfast.

When it was dark I set bi mi camp fier smoeking, and feeling prity wel satisfied; but bi and bi it got sort of loensum, and so I went and set on th bank and lisend to th curent swashing along, and counted th stars and drift logs and rafts that cum doun, and then went to bed; thair ain’t no beter way to puut in tiem when u ar loensum; u can’t stay so, u soon get oever it.

And so for three days and niets. No diferens—just th saem thing. But th next day I went exploring around doun thru th ieland. I was boss of it; it all belongd to me, so to say, and I wonted to noe all about it; but maenly I wonted to puut in th tiem. I found plenty strawberrys, riep and priem; and green sumer graeps, and green razberries; and th green blackberries was just begining to sho. Thay wuud all cum handy bi and bi, I jujd.

Wel, I went fooling along in th deep wuuds til I jujd I worn’t far frum th fuut of th ieland. I had mi gun along, but I hadn’t shot nuthing; it was for protecshun; thaut I wuud kil sum gaem ni hoem. About this tiem I miety neer stept on a guud-siezd snaek, and it went slieding off thru th gras and flowers, and I after it, trieing to get a shot at it. I clipt along, and all of a suden I bounded riet on to th ashes of a camp fier that was stil smoeking.









Mi hart jumpt up amungst mi lungs. I never waeted for to luuk ferther, but uncocked mi gun and went sneeking bak on mi tiptoes as fast as ever I cuud. Evry now and then I stopt a second amungst th thik leevs and lisend, but mi breth cum so hard I couldn’t heer nuthing els. I slunk along anuther pees ferther, then lisend agen; and so on, and so on. If I see a stump, I tuuk it for a man; if I trod on a stik and broek it, it maed me feel liek a person had cut wun of mi breths in too and I oenly got haf, and th short haf, too.

When I got to camp I worn’t feeling verry brash, thair worn’t much sand in mi craw; but I sez, this ain’t no tiem to be fooling around. So I got all mi traps into mi canoo agen so as to hav them out of siet, and I puut out th fier and scaterd th ashes around to luuk liek an oeld last yeer’s camp, and then clumb a tree.

I rekon I was up in th tree too ours; but I didn’t see nuthing, I didn’t heer nuthing—I oenly thaut I herd and seen as much as a thouzand things. Wel, I couldn’t stay up thair forever; so at last I got doun, but I kept in th thik wuuds and on th luukout all th tiem. All I cuud get to eet was berrys and whut was left oever frum brekfast.

Bi th tiem it was niet I was prity hunggry. So when it was guud and dark I slid out frum shor befor moonrise and paddled oever to th Illinois bank—about a qorter of a miel. I went out in th wuuds and cuukt a super, and I had about maed up mi miend I wuud stay thair all niet when I heer a plunkety-plunk, plunkety-plunk, and sez to mieself, horses cuming; and next I heer peepl’s voises. I got evrything into th canoo as qik as I cuud, and then went creeping thru th wuuds to see whut I cuud fiend out. I hadn’t got far when I heer a man say:

“We beter camp heer if we can fiend a guud plaes; th horses is about beet out. Let’s luuk around.”

I didn’t waet, but shuvd out and paddled away eezy. I tied up in th oeld plaes, and rekond I wuud sleep in th canoo.

I didn’t sleep much. I couldn’t, sumhow, for thinking. And evry tiem I waekt up I thaut sumbody had me bi th nek. So th sleep didn’t do me no guud. Bi and bi I sez to mieself, I can’t liv this way; I’m a-going to fiend out hoo it is that’s heer on th ieland with me; I’ll fiend it out or bust. Wel, I felt beter riet off.

So I tuuk mi padl and slid out frum shor just a step or too, and then let th canoo drop along doun amungst th shadoes. Th moon was shiening, and outsied of th shadoes it maed it moest as liet as day. I poekt along wel on to an our, evrything stil as roks and sound asleep. Wel, bi this tiem I was moest doun to th fuut of th ieland. A litl ripply, cool breez begun to blo, and that was as guud as saying th niet was about dun. I giv her a tern with th padl and brung her noez to shor; then I got mi gun and slipt out and into th ej of th wuuds. I sat doun thair on a log, and luukt out thru th leevs. I see th moon go off woch, and th darknes begin to blanket th river. But in a litl whiel I see a pael streek oever th treetops, and knowed th day was cuming. So I tuuk mi gun and slipt off tords whair I had run across that camp fier, stoping evry minit or too to lisen. But I hadn’t no luk sumhow; I couldn’t seem to fiend th plaes. But bi and bi, shur enuf, I catched a glimps of fier away thru th trees. I went for it, caushus and slo. Bi and bi I was cloez enuf to hav a luuk, and thair laed a man on th ground. It moest giv me th fan-tods. He had a blanket around his hed, and his hed was neerly in th fier. I set thair behiend a clump of buushes, in about six fuut of him, and kept mi ies on him stedy. It was geting gray dayliet now. Prity soon he gapped and strecht himself and hoev off th blanket, and it was Mis Watson’s Jim! I bet I was glad to see him. I sez:

“Helo, Jim!” and skipt out.

He bounst up and staird at me wield. Then he drops doun on his nees, and puuts his hands together and sez:

“Doan’ hert me—don’t! I hain’t ever dun no harm to a ghos’. I alwuz liekt ded peepl, en dun all I cuud for ’em. U go en git in de river agin, whah u b’longs, en doan’ do nuffn to Oelay Jim, ’at ’uz awluz yo’ fren’.”









Wel, I worn’t long maeking him understand I worn’t ded. I was ever so glad to see Jim. I worn’t loensum now. I toeld him I worn’t afraed of him teling th peepl whair I was. I taukt along, but he oenly set thair and luukt at me; never sed nuthing. Then I sez:

“It’s guud dayliet. Le’s get brekfast. Maek up yur camp fier guud.”

“Whut’s de ues er makin’ up de camp fier to cuuk strawbries en sich truk? But u got a gun, hain’t u? Den we kin git sumfn beter den strawbries.”

“Strawberrys and such truk,” I sez. “Is that whut u liv on?”

“I couldn’ git nuffn els,” he sez.

“Whi, how long u bin on th ieland, Jim?”

“I cum heah de niet arter u’s kild.”

“Whut, all that tiem?”

“Yes—indeedy.”

“And ain’t u had nuthing but that kiend of rubbage to eet?”

“No, sah—nuffn els.”

“Wel, u must be moest starvd, ain’t u?”

“I reck’n I cuud eet a hoss. I think I cuud. How long u ben on de islan’?”

“Sinss th niet I got kild.”

“No! W’y, whut has u livd on? But u got a gun. O, yes, u got a gun. Dat’s guud. Now u kil sumfn en I’ll maek up de fier.”
