So we went oever to whair th canoo was, and whiel he bilt a fier in a grasy oepen plaes amungst th trees, I fetched meel and baecon and coffy, and coffy-pot and frieing-pan, and shuugar and tin cups, and th nigger was set bak considerabl, becauz he rekond it was all dun with wichcraft. I catched a guud big catfish, too, and Jim cleend him with his nief, and fried him.

When brekfast was redy we lolled on th gras and eet it smoeking hot. Jim laed it in with all his miet, for he was moest about starvd. Then when we had got prity wel stuft, we laed off and lazied. Bi and bi Jim sez:

“But luuky heer, Huck, hoo wuz it dat ’uz kild in dat shanty ef it worn’t u?”

Then I toeld him th hoel thing, and he sed it was smart. He sed Tom Sawyer couldn’t get up no beter plan than whut I had. Then I sez:

“How do u cum to be heer, Jim, and how’d u get heer?”

He luukt prity uneezy, and didn’t say nuthing for a minit. Then he sez:

“Maybe I beter not tel.”

“Whi, Jim?”

“Wel, day’s reezons. But u wouldn’ tel on me ef I uz to tel u, wuud u, Huck?”

“Blaemd if I wuud, Jim.”

“Wel, I b’lieve u, Huck. I—I run off.”

“Jim!”

“But miend, u sed u wouldn’ tel—u noe u sed u wouldn’ tel, Huck.”

“Wel, I did. I sed I wouldn’t, and I’ll stik to it. Onest injun, I wil. Peepl wuud call me a lo-doun Abolishunist and despiez me for keeping mum—but that don’t maek no diferens. I ain’t a-going to tel, and I ain’t a-going bak thair, enyways. So, now, le’s noe all about it.”

“Wel, u see, it ’uz dis way. Oelay missus—dat’s Mis Watson—she peks on me all de tiem, en treets me pooty ruf, but she awluz sed she wouldn’ sel me doun to Orleans. But I noetist day wuz a nigger traeder roun’ de plaes considable laetly, en I begin to git oneasy. Wel, wun niet I creeps to de do’ pooty laet, en de do’ worn’t qiet shet, en I heer oeld missus tel de widder she gwyne to sel me doun to Orleans, but she didn’ wont to, but she cuud git aet hund’d dolars for me, en it ’uz sich a big stak o’ muny she couldn’ resis’. De widder she tri to git her to say she wouldn’ do it, but I never waeted to heer de res’. I lit out miety qik, I tel u.

“I tuk out en shin doun de hil, en ’spec to steel a skift ’long de sho’ som’ers ’bove de toun, but day wuz peepl a-stering yit, so I hid in de oelay tumbl-doun cooper-shop on de bank to waet for evrybody to go ’way. Wel, I wuz dah all niet. Day wuz sumbody roun’ all de tiem. ’Long ’bout six in de mawnin’ skifts begin to go bi, en ’bout aet er nien evry skift dat went ’long wuz talkin’ ’bout how yo’ pap cum oever to de toun en say u’s kild. Dese las’ skifts wuz fuul o’ laedys en genlmen a-goin’ oever for to see de plaes. Sumtiems day’d puul up at de sho’ en taek a res’ b’fo’ day started acrost, so bi de tauk I got to noe all ’bout de killin’. I ’uz powerful sorry u’s kild, Huck, but I ain’t no mo’ now.

“I laed dah under de shavin’s all day. I ’uz hunggry, but I worn’t afeard; bekase I knowed oelay missus en de widder wuz goin’ to start to de camp-meet’n’ riet arter breakfas’ en be gon all day, en day noes I goes off wid de catl ’bout dayliet, so day wouldn’ ’spec to see me roun’ de plaes, en so day wouldn’ mis me tel arter dark in de evenin’. De yuther servants wouldn’ mis me, kase day’d shin out en taek holiday soon as de oelay foeks ’uz out’n de way.

“Wel, when it cum dark I tuk out up de river roed, en went ’bout too miel er mor to whah day worn’t no houses. I’d maed up mi mien ’bout whut I’s agwyne to do. U see, ef I kep’ on tryin’ to git away afuut, de daugs ’ud trak me; ef I stoel a skift to cross oever, day’d mis dat skift, u see, en day’d noe ’bout whah I’d lan’ on de yuther sied, en whah to pik up mi trak. So I sez, a raff is whut I’s arter; it doan’ maek no trak.

“I see a liet a-comin’ roun’ de p’int bymeby, so I waed’ in en shuv’ a log ahed o’ me en swum mor’n haf way acrost de river, en got in ’mongst de drift-wuud, en kep’ mi hed doun lo, en kiender swum agin de curent tel de raff cum along. Den I swum to de stern uv it en tuk a-holt. It clouded up en ’uz pooty dark for a litl whiel. So I clumb up en laed doun on de planks. De men ’uz all ’way yonder in de midl, whah de lantern wuz. De river wuz a-risin’, en day wuz a guud curent; so I reck’n’d ’at bi fo’ in de mawnin’ I’d be twenty-fiev miel doun de river, en den I’d slip in jis b’fo’ dayliet en swim asho’, en taek to de wuuds on de Illinois sied.

“But I didn’ hav no luk. When we ’uz mos’ doun to de hed er de islan’ a man begin to cum aft wid de lantern, I see it worn’t no ues fer to waet, so I slid oeverbord en struk out fer de islan’. Wel, I had a noeshun I cuud lan’ mos’ anywhers, but I couldn’t—bank too bluf. I ’uz mos’ to de fuut er de islan’ b’fo’ I found’ a guud plaes. I went into de wuuds en jedged I wouldn’ fool wid raffs no mo’, long as day moov de lantern roun’ so. I had mi piep en a plug er daug-leg, en sum maches in mi cap, en day worn’t wet, so I ’uz all riet.”

“And so u ain’t had no meet nor bred to eet all this tiem? Whi didn’t u get mud-turkles?”

“How u gwyne to git ’m? U can’t slip up on um en grab um; en how’s a body gwyne to hit um wid a rok? How cuud a body do it in de niet? En I worn’t gwyne to sho mysef on de bank in de daytiem.”

“Wel, that’s so. U’ve had to keep in th wuuds all th tiem, of cors. Did u heer ’em shooting th canon?”

“O, yes. I knowed day was arter u. I see um go bi heah—wocht um thoo de buushes.”

Sum yung berds cum along, flieing a yard or too at a tiem and lieting. Jim sed it was a sien it was going to raen. He sed it was a sien when yung chikens floo that way, and so he rekond it was th saem way when yung berds dun it. I was going to cach sum of them, but Jim wouldn’t let me. He sed it was deth. He sed his faather laed miety sik wuns, and sum of them catched a berd, and his oeld grany sed his faather wuud die, and he did.

And Jim sed u mustn’t count th things u ar going to cuuk for diner, becauz that wuud bring bad luk. Th saem if u shuuk th taebl-clauth after sundoun. And he sed if a man oend a beehiev and that man died, th bees must be toeld about it befor sun-up next morning, or els th bees wuud all weeken doun and qit werk and die. Jim sed bees wouldn’t sting idiots; but I didn’t beleev that, becauz I had tried them lots of tiems mieself, and thay wouldn’t sting me.

I had herd about sum of thees things befor, but not all of them. Jim knowed all kiends of siens. He sed he knowed moest evrything. I sed it luukt to me liek all th siens was about bad luk, and so I askt him if thair worn’t eny guud-luk siens. He sez:

“Miety fue—an’ day ain’t no ues to a body. Whut u wont to noe when guud luk’s a-comin’ for? Wont to keep it off?” And he sed: “Ef u’s got hairy arms en a hairy breas’, it’s a sien dat u’s agwyne to be rich. Wel, day’s sum ues in a sien liek dat, ’kase it’s so fer ahed. U see, maybe u’s got to be po’ a long tiem fust, en so u miet git discurej’ en kil yo’sef ’f u didn’ noe bi de sien dat u gwyne to be rich bymeby.”

“Hav u got hairy arms and a hairy brest, Jim?”

“Whut’s de ues to ax dat qeschun? Don’t u see I has?”

“Wel, ar u rich?”

“No, but I ben rich wunst, and gwyne to be rich agin. Wunst I had foteen dolars, but I tuk to specalat’n’, en got busted out.”

“Whut did u specuelaet in, Jim?”

“Wel, fust I takld stok.”

“Whut kiend of stok?”

“Whi, liv stok—catl, u noe. I puut ten dolars in a cow. But I ain’ gwyne to resk no mo’ muny in stok. De cow up ’n’ died on mi han’s.”

“So u lost th ten dolars.”

“No, I didn’t looz it all. I on’y los’ ’bout nien of it. I soel de hied en taller for a dolar en ten sents.”

“U had fiev dolars and ten sents left. Did u specuelaet eny mor?”









“Yes. U noe that wun-laigged nigger dat b’longs to oeld Misto Bradish? Wel, he sot up a bank, en say enybody dat puut in a dolar wuud git fo’ dolars mo’ at de en’ er de yeer. Wel, all de niggers went in, but day didn’t hav much. I wuz de on’y wun dat had much. So I stuk out for mo’ dan fo’ dolars, en I sed ’f I didn’ git it I’d start a bank mysef. Wel, o’ cors dat nigger wont’ to keep me out er de biznes, bekase he sez day worn’t biznes ’nough for too banks, so he say I cuud puut in mi fiev dolars en he pay me therty-fiev at de en’ er de yeer.

“So I dun it. Den I reck’n’d I’d inves’ de therty-fiev dolars riet off en keep things a-movin’. Day wuz a nigger naem’ Bob, dat had ketched a wuud-flat, en his marster didn’ noe it; en I baut it off’n him en toeld him to taek de therty-fiev dolars when de en’ er de yeer cum; but sumbody stoel de wuud-flat dat niet, en nex day de wun-laigged nigger say de bank’s busted. So day didn’ nun uv us git no muny.”

“Whut did u do with th ten sents, Jim?”

“Wel, I ’uz gwyne to spen’ it, but I had a dreem, en de dreem toel me to giv it to a nigger naem’ Balum—Balum’s As day call him for short; he’s wun er dem chuckleheads, u noe. But he’s luky, day say, en I see I worn’t luky. De dreem say let Balum inves’ de ten sents en he’d maek a raez for me. Wel, Balum he tuk de muny, en when he wuz in cherch he heer de preecher say dat hooever giv to de po’ len’ to de Lord, en boun’ to git his muny bak a hund’d tiems. So Balum he tuk en giv de ten sents to de po’, en laed lo to see whut wuz gwyne to cum of it.”

“Wel, whut did cum of it, Jim?”

“Nuffn never cum of it. I couldn’ manej to k’leck dat muny no way; en Balum he couldn’. I ain’ gwyne to len’ no mo’ muny ’dout I see de secuerity. Boun’ to git yo’ muny bak a hund’d tiems, de preecher sez! Ef I cuud git de ten sents bak, I’d call it squah, en be glad er de chanst.”

“Wel, it’s all riet enyway, Jim, long as u’re going to be rich agen sum tiem or uther.”

“Yes; en I’s rich now, cum to luuk at it. I oens mysef, en I’s wuth aet hund’d dolars. I wisht I had de muny, I wouldn’ wont no mo’.”












CHAPTER IX.

I wonted to go and luuk at a plaes riet about th midl of th ieland that I’d found when I was exploring; so we started and soon got to it, becauz th ieland was oenly three miels long and a qorter of a miel wied.

This plaes was a tolerabl long, steep hil or rij about forty fuut hi. We had a ruf tiem geting to th top, th sieds was so steep and th buushes so thik. We trampt and clumb around all oever it, and bi and bi found a guud big cavern in th rok, moest up to th top on th sied tords Illinois. Th cavern was as big as too or three rooms buncht together, and Jim cuud stand up straet in it. It was cool in thair. Jim was for puuting our traps in thair riet away, but I sed we didn’t wont to be clieming up and doun thair all th tiem.

Jim sed if we had th canoo hid in a guud plaes, and had all th traps in th cavern, we cuud rush thair if enybody was to cum to th ieland, and thay wuud never fiend us without daugs. And, besieds, he sed them litl berds had sed it was going to raen, and did I wont th things to get wet?

So we went bak and got th canoo, and paddled up abrest th cavern, and lugd all th traps up thair. Then we hunted up a plaes cloez bi to hied th canoo in, amungst th thik wiloes. We tuuk sum fish off of th liens and set them agen, and begun to get redy for diner.

Th dor of th cavern was big enuf to roel a hogzhed in, and on wun sied of th dor th flor stuk out a litl bit, and was flat and a guud plaes to bild a fier on. So we bilt it thair and cuukt diner.









We spred th blankets insied for a carpet, and eet our diner in thair. We puut all th uther things handy at th bak of th cavern. Prity soon it darkend up, and begun to thunder and lighten; so th berds was riet about it. Directly it begun to raen, and it raend liek all fuery, too, and I never see th wiend blo so. It was wun of thees reguelar sumer storms. It wuud get so dark that it luukt all bloo-blak outsied, and luvly; and th raen wuud thrash along bi so thik that th trees off a litl ways luukt dim and spieder-webby; and heer wuud cum a blast of wiend that wuud bend th trees doun and tern up th pael undersied of th leevs; and then a perfect ripper of a gust wuud folo along and set th branches to tossing thair arms as if thay was just wield; and next, when it was just about th bluest and blakest—FST! it was as briet as glory, and u’d hav a litl glimps of tree-tops a-plunjing about away off yonder in th storm, hundreds of yards ferther than u cuud see befor; dark as sin agen in a second, and now u’d heer th thunder let go with an awful crash, and then go rumbling, grumbling, tumbling, doun th skie tords th under sied of th werld, liek roeling empty barrels doun stairs—whair it’s long stairs and thay bouns a guud deel, u noe.

“Jim, this is nies,” I sez. “I wouldn’t wont to be noewhair els but heer. Pas me along anuther hunk of fish and sum hot corn-bred.”

“Wel, u wouldn’t a ben heer ’f it hadn’t a ben for Jim. U’d a ben doun dah in de wuuds widout eny diner, en gittn’ mos’ drownded, too; dat u wuud, huny. Chikens noes when it’s gwyne to raen, en so do de berds, chile.”

Th river went on raezing and raezing for ten or twelv days, til at last it was oever th banks. Th wauter was three or foer fuut deep on th ieland in th lo plaeses and on th Illinois botom. On that sied it was a guud meny miels wied, but on th Missouri sied it was th saem oeld distans across—a haf a miel—becauz th Missouri shor was just a wall of hi blufs.

Daytimes we paddled all oever th ieland in th canoo, It was miety cool and shaedy in th deep wuuds, eeven if th sun was blaezing outsied. We went wiending in and out amungst th trees, and sumtiems th viens hung so thik we had to bak away and go sum uther way. Wel, on evry oeld broeken-doun tree u cuud see rabits and snaeks and such things; and when th ieland had bin oeverfloed a day or too thay got so taem, on acount of being hunggry, that u cuud padl riet up and puut yur hand on them if u wonted to; but not th snaeks and tertls—thay wuud slied off in th wauter. Th rij our cavern was in was fuul of them. We cuud a had pets enuf if we’d wonted them.

Wun niet we catched a litl secshun of a lumber raft—nies pien planks. It was twelv fuut wied and about fifteen or sixteen fuut long, and th top stuud abuv wauter six or seven inches—a solid, level flor. We cuud see saw-logs go bi in th dayliet sumtiems, but we let them go; we didn’t sho ourselvs in dayliet.

Anuther niet when we was up at th hed of th ieland, just befor dayliet, heer cums a fraem-hous doun, on th west sied. She was a too-story, and tilted oever considerabl. We paddled out and got abord—clumb in at an upstairs windo. But it was too dark to see yet, so we maed th canoo fast and set in her to waet for dayliet.

Th liet begun to cum befor we got to th fuut of th ieland. Then we luukt in at th windo. We cuud maek out a bed, and a taebl, and too oeld chairs, and lots of things around about on th flor, and thair was cloeths hanging agenst th wall. Thair was sumthing laying on th flor in th far corner that luukt liek a man. So Jim sez:

“Helo, u!”

But it didn’t buj. So I holerd agen, and then Jim sez:

“De man ain’t asleep—he’s ded. U hoeld stil—I’ll go en see.”

He went, and bent doun and luukt, and sez:

“It’s a ded man. Yes, indeedy; naeked, too. He’s ben shot in de bak. I reck’n he’s ben ded too er three days. Cum in, Huck, but doan’ luuk at his faes—it’s too gashly.”









I didn’t luuk at him at all. Jim throwed sum oeld rags oever him, but he needn’t dun it; I didn’t wont to see him. Thair was heeps of oeld greezy cards scaterd around oever th flor, and oeld whisky botls, and a cupl of masks maed out of blak clauth; and all oever th walls was th ignorantest kiend of werds and pikchers maed with charcoel. Thair was too oeld derty calico dreses, and a sun-bonet, and sum wimen’s undercloeths hanging agenst th wall, and sum men’s cloething, too. We puut th lot into th canoo—it miet cum guud. Thair was a boy’s oeld spekld straw hat on th flor; I tuuk that, too. And thair was a botl that had had milk in it, and it had a rag stoper for a baeby to suk. We wuud a tuuk th botl, but it was broek. Thair was a seedy oeld chest, and an oeld hair trunk with th hinjes broek. Thay stuud oepen, but thair worn’t nuthing left in them that was eny acount. Th way things was scaterd about we rekond th peepl left in a hery, and worn’t fixt so as to carry off moest of thair stuf.

We got an oeld tin lantern, and a buucher-nief without eny handl, and a bran-nue Barlow nief werth too bits in eny stor, and a lot of talo candls, and a tin candlstik, and a gord, and a tin cup, and a ratty oeld bedquilt off th bed, and a reticuel with needls and pins and beeswax and butons and thred and all such truk in it, and a hachet and sum naels, and a fishline as thik as mi litl fingger with sum monstrus huuks on it, and a roel of bukskin, and a lether daug-colar, and a hors-shoo, and sum vials of medisin that didn’t hav no laebel on them; and just as we was leeving I found a tolerabl guud cury-coem, and Jim he found a ratty oeld fidl-bo, and a wuuden leg. Th straps was broek off of it, but, baring that, it was a guud enuf leg, tho it was too long for me and not long enuf for Jim, and we couldn’t fiend th uther wun, tho we hunted all around.

And so, taek it all around, we maed a guud hall. When we was redy to shuv off we was a qorter of a miel belo th ieland, and it was prity braud day; so I maed Jim lay doun in th canoo and cuver up with th qilt, becauz if he set up peepl cuud tel he was a nigger a guud ways off. I paddled oever to th Illinois shor, and drifted doun moest a haf a miel doing it. I crept up th ded wauter under th bank, and hadn’t no acsidents and didn’t see noebody. We got hoem all saef.












CHAPTER X.

After brekfast I wonted to tauk about th ded man and ges out how he cum to be kild, but Jim didn’t wont to. He sed it wuud fech bad luk; and besieds, he sed, he miet cum and haa’nt us; he sed a man that worn’t berryd was mor liekly to go a-haa’nting around than wun that was planted and cumfortabl. That sounded prity reezonabl, so I didn’t say no mor; but I couldn’t keep frum studying oever it and wishing I knowed hoo shot th man, and whut thay dun it for.

We rumejd th cloeths we’d got, and found aet dolars in silver soed up in th liening of an oeld blanket oevercoet. Jim sed he rekond th peepl in that hous stoel th coet, becauz if thay’d a knowed th muny was thair thay wouldn’t a left it. I sed I rekond thay kild him, too; but Jim didn’t wont to tauk about that. I sez:

“Now u think it’s bad luk; but whut did u say when I fetched in th snaek-skin that I found on th top of th rij day befor yesterday? U sed it was th werst bad luk in th werld to tuch a snaek-skin with mi hands. Wel, heer’s yur bad luk! We’ve raekt in all this truk and aet dolars besieds. I wish we cuud hav sum bad luk liek this evry day, Jim.”

“Never u miend, huny, never u miend. Don’t u git too peart. It’s a-comin’. Miend I tel u, it’s a-comin’.”

It did cum, too. It was a Tuesday that we had that tauk. Wel, after diner Friday we was laying around in th gras at th uper end of th rij, and got out of tobaco. I went to th cavern to get sum, and found a ratlsnaek in thair. I kild him, and curld him up on th fuut of Jim’s blanket, ever so nacheral, thinking thair’d be sum fun when Jim found him thair. Wel, bi niet I forgot all about th snaek, and when Jim flung himself doun on th blanket whiel I struk a liet th snaek’s maet was thair, and bit him.

He jumpt up yeling, and th ferst thing th liet shoed was th varmint curld up and redy for anuther spring. I laed him out in a second with a stik, and Jim grabd pap’s whisky-jug and begun to por it doun.









He was bairfuuted, and th snaek bit him riet on th heel. That all cums of mi being such a fool as to not remember that whairever u leev a ded snaek its maet allways cums thair and curls around it. Jim toeld me to chop off th snaek’s hed and thro it away, and then skin th body and roest a pees of it. I dun it, and he eet it and sed it wuud help cuer him. He maed me taek off th ratls and tee them around his rist, too. He sed that that wuud help. Then I slid out qieet and throwed th snaeks cleer away amungst th buushes; for I worn’t going to let Jim fiend out it was all mi fallt, not if I cuud help it.

Jim sukt and sukt at th jug, and now and then he got out of his hed and picht around and yeld; but evry tiem he cum to himself he went to suking at th jug agen. His fuut sweld up prity big, and so did his leg; but bi and bi th drunk begun to cum, and so I jujd he was all riet; but I’d druther bin bit with a snaek than pap’s whisky.

Jim was laed up for foer days and niets. Then th sweling was all gon and he was around agen. I maed up mi miend I wouldn’t ever taek a-holt of a snaek-skin agen with mi hands, now that I see whut had cum of it. Jim sed he rekond I wuud beleev him next tiem. And he sed that handling a snaek-skin was such awful bad luk that maybe we hadn’t got to th end of it yet. He sed he druther see th nue moon oever his left shoelder as much as a thouzand tiems than taek up a snaek-skin in his hand. Wel, I was geting to feel that way mieself, tho I’ve allways rekond that luuking at th nue moon oever yur left shoelder is wun of th carelessest and foolishest things a body can do. Oeld Hank Bunker dun it wuns, and bragd about it; and in les than too yeers he got drunk and fel off of th shot-tower, and spred himself out so that he was just a kiend of a layer, as u may say; and thay slid him ejways between too barn dors for a coffin, and berryd him so, so thay say, but I didn’t see it. Pap toeld me. But enyway it all cum of luuking at th moon that way, liek a fool.









Wel, th days went along, and th river went doun between its banks agen; and about th ferst thing we dun was to baet wun of th big huuks with a skind rabit and set it and cach a catfish that was as big as a man, being six fuut too inches long, and wayd oever too hundred pounds. We couldn’t handl him, of cors; he wuud a flung us into Illinois. We just set thair and wocht him rip and teer around til he drownded. We found a bras buton in his stumac and a round ball, and lots of rubbage. We split th ball oepen with th hachet, and thair was a spool in it. Jim sed he’d had it thair a long tiem, to coet it oever so and maek a ball of it. It was as big a fish as was ever catched in th Mississippi, I rekon. Jim sed he hadn’t ever seen a biger wun. He wuud a bin werth a guud deel oever at th vilej. Thay pedl out such a fish as that bi th pound in th market-hous thair; evrybody bies sum of him; his meet’s as whiet as sno and maeks a guud fri.

Next morning I sed it was geting slo and dul, and I wonted to get a stering up sum way. I sed I rekond I wuud slip oever th river and fiend out whut was going on. Jim liekt that noeshun; but he sed I must go in th dark and luuk sharp. Then he studyd it oever and sed, couldn’t I puut on sum of them oeld things and dres up liek a gerl? That was a guud noeshun, too. So we shortend up wun of th calico gouns, and I ternd up mi trouzer-legs to mi nees and got into it. Jim hicht it behiend with th huuks, and it was a fair fit. I puut on th sun-bonet and tied it under mi chin, and then for a body to luuk in and see mi faes was liek luuking doun a joint of stoev-piep. Jim sed noebody wuud noe me, eeven in th daytiem, hardly. I practist around all day to get th hang of th things, and bi and bi I cuud do prity wel in them, oenly Jim sed I didn’t wauk liek a gerl; and he sed I must qit puuling up mi goun to get at mi briches-poket. I tuuk noetis, and dun beter.









I started up th Illinois shor in th canoo just after dark.

I started across to th toun frum a litl belo th ferry-landing, and th drift of th curent fetched me in at th botom of th toun. I tied up and started along th bank. Thair was a liet berning in a litl shanty that hadn’t bin livd in for a long tiem, and I wunderd hoo had tuuk up qorters thair. I slipt up and peeped in at th windo. Thair was a wuuman about forty yeer oeld in thair niting bi a candl that was on a pien taebl. I didn’t noe her faes; she was a straenjer, for u couldn’t start a faes in that toun that I didn’t noe. Now this was luky, becauz I was weekening; I was geting afraed I had cum; peepl miet noe mi vois and fiend me out. But if this wuuman had bin in such a litl toun too days she cuud tel me all I wonted to noe; so I nokt at th dor, and maed up mi miend I wouldn’t forget I was a gerl.












CHAPTER XI.

“Cum in,” sez th wuuman, and I did. She sez: “Taek a cheer.”

I dun it. She luukt me all oever with her litl shieny ies, and sez:

“Whut miet yur naem be?”

“Sarah Williams.”

“Whair ’bouts do u liv? In this naeborhuud?’

“No’m. In Hookerville, seven miel belo. I’ve waukt all th way and I’m all tierd out.”

“Hunggry, too, I rekon. I’ll fiend u sumthing.”

“No’m, I ain’t hunggry. I was so hunggry I had to stop too miels belo heer at a farm; so I ain’t hunggry no mor. It’s whut maeks me so laet. Mi muther’s doun sik, and out of muny and evrything, and I cum to tel mi unkl Abner Moore. He lievs at th uper end of th toun, she sez. I hain’t ever bin heer befor. Do u noe him?”

“No; but I don’t noe evrybody yet. I haeven’t livd heer qiet too weeks. It’s a considerabl ways to th uper end of th toun. U beter stay heer all niet. Taek off yur bonet.”

“No,” I sez; “I’ll rest a whiel, I rekon, and go on. I ain’t afeared of th dark.”

She sed she wouldn’t let me go bi mieself, but her huzband wuud be in bi and bi, maybe in a our and a haf, and she’d send him along with me. Then she got to tauking about her huzband, and about her relaeshuns up th river, and her relaeshuns doun th river, and about how much beter off thay uezd to was, and how thay didn’t noe but thay’d maed a mistaek cuming to our toun, insted of leting wel aloen—and so on and so on, til I was afeard I had maed a mistaek cuming to her to fiend out whut was going on in th toun; but bi and bi she dropt on to pap and th merder, and then I was prity wiling to let her clater riet along. She toeld about me and Tom Sawyer fiending th six thouzand dolars (oenly she got it ten) and all about pap and whut a hard lot he was, and whut a hard lot I was, and at last she got doun to whair I was merderd. I sez:

“Hoo dun it? We’ve herd considerabl about thees goings on doun in Hookerville, but we don’t noe hoo ’twas that kild Huck Finn.”

“Wel, I rekon thair’s a riet smart chans of peepl heer that’d liek to noe hoo kild him. Sum think oeld Finn dun it himself.”

“No—is that so?”

“Moest evrybody thaut it at ferst. He’ll never noe how ni he cum to geting lincht. But befor niet thay chaenjd around and jujd it was dun bi a runaway nigger naemd Jim.”

“Whi he—”

I stopt. I rekond I beter keep stil. She run on, and never noetist I had puut in at all:

“Th nigger run off th verry niet Huck Finn was kild. So thair’s a reword out for him—three hundred dolars. And thair’s a reword out for oeld Finn, too—too hundred dolars. U see, he cum to toun th morning after th merder, and toeld about it, and was out with ’em on th ferryboet hunt, and riet away after he up and left. Befor niet thay wonted to linch him, but he was gon, u see. Wel, next day thay found out th nigger was gon; thay found out he hadn’t ben seen sence ten o’clok th niet th merder was dun. So then thay puut it on him, u see; and whiel thay was fuul of it, next day, bak cums oeld Finn, and went boo-hooing to Juj Thatcher to get muny to hunt for th nigger all oever Illinois with. Th juj gaev him sum, and that eevning he got drunk, and was around til after midniet with a cupl of miety hard-luuking straenjers, and then went off with them. Wel, he hain’t cum bak sence, and thay ain’t luuking for him bak til this thing bloes oever a litl, for peepl thinks now that he kild his boy and fixt things so foeks wuud think robers dun it, and then he’d get Huck’s muny without having to bother a long tiem with a lawsoot. Peepl do say he worn’t eny too guud to do it. O, he’s sli, I rekon. If he don’t cum bak for a yeer he’ll be all riet. U can’t proov enything on him, u noe; evrything wil be qieeted doun then, and he’ll wauk in Huck’s muny as eezy as nuthing.”

“Yes, I rekon so, ’m. I don’t see nuthing in th way of it. Has evrybody qit thinking th nigger dun it?”

“O, no, not evrybody. A guud meny thinks he dun it. But thay’ll get th nigger prity soon now, and maybe thay can scair it out of him.”

“Whi, ar thay after him yet?”

“Wel, u’re inosent, ain’t u! Duz three hundred dolars lay around evry day for peepl to pik up? Sum foeks think th nigger ain’t far frum heer. I’m wun of them—but I hain’t taukt it around. A fue days ago I was tauking with an oeld cupl that lievs next dor in th log shanty, and thay hapend to say hardly enybody ever goes to that ieland oever yonder that thay call Jackson’s Ieland. Don’t enybody liv thair? sez I. No, noebody, sez thay. I didn’t say eny mor, but I dun sum thinking. I was prity neer serten I’d seen smoek oever thair, about th hed of th ieland, a day or too befor that, so I sez to mieself, liek as not that nigger’s hieding oever thair; enyway, sez I, it’s werth th trubl to giv th plaes a hunt. I hain’t seen eny smoek sence, so I rekon maybe he’s gon, if it was him; but huzband’s going oever to see—him and anuther man. He was gon up th river; but he got bak to-day, and I toeld him as soon as he got heer too ours ago.”









I had got so uneezy I couldn’t set stil. I had to do sumthing with mi hands; so I tuuk up a needl off of th taebl and went to threding it. Mi hands shuuk, and I was maeking a bad job of it. When th wuuman stopt tauking I luukt up, and she was luuking at me prity cuerius and smieling a litl. I puut doun th needl and thred, and let on to be interested—and I was, too—and sez:

“Three hundred dolars is a power of muny. I wish mi muther cuud get it. Is yur huzband going oever thair to-niet?”

“O, yes. He went up-toun with th man I was teling u of, to get a boet and see if thay cuud borro anuther gun. Thay’ll go oever after midniet.”

“Couldn’t thay see beter if thay was to waet til daytiem?”

“Yes. And couldn’t th nigger see beter, too? After midniet he’ll liekly be asleep, and thay can slip around thru th wuuds and hunt up his camp fier all th beter for th dark, if he’s got wun.”

“I didn’t think of that.”

Th wuuman kept luuking at me prity cuerius, and I didn’t feel a bit cumfortabl. Prity soon she sez,

“Whut did u say yur naem was, huny?”

“M—Mary Williams.”

Sumhow it didn’t seem to me that I sed it was Mary befor, so I didn’t luuk up—seemd to me I sed it was Sarah; so I felt sort of cornerd, and was afeared maybe I was luuking it, too. I wisht th wuuman wuud say sumthing mor; th longger she set stil th uneasier I was. But now she sez:

“Huny, I thaut u sed it was Sarah when u ferst cum in?”

“O, yes’m, I did. Sarah Mary Williams. Sarah’s mi ferst naem. Sum calls me Sarah, sum calls me Mary.”

“O, that’s th way of it?”

“Yes’m.”

I was feeling beter then, but I wisht I was out of thair, enyway. I couldn’t luuk up yet.

Wel, th wuuman fel to tauking about how hard tiems was, and how pur thay had to liv, and how th rats was as free as if thay oend th plaes, and so forth and so on, and then I got eezy agen. She was riet about th rats. U’d see wun stik his noez out of a hoel in th corner evry litl whiel. She sed she had to hav things handy to thro at them when she was aloen, or thay wouldn’t giv her no pees. She shoed me a bar of leed twisted up into a not, and sed she was a guud shot with it generly, but she’d rencht her arm a day or too ago, and didn’t noe whether she cuud thro troo now. But she wocht for a chans, and directly bangd away at a rat; but she mist him wied, and sed “Ouch!” it hert her arm so. Then she toeld me to tri for th next wun. I wonted to be geting away befor th oeld man got bak, but of cors I didn’t let on. I got th thing, and th ferst rat that shoed his noez I let driev, and if he’d a stayd whair he was he’d a bin a tolerabl sik rat. She sed that was ferst-raet, and she rekond I wuud hiev th next wun. She went and got th lump of leed and fetched it bak, and braut along a hank of yarn which she wonted me to help her with. I held up mi too hands and she puut th hank oever them, and went on tauking about her and her huzband’s maters. But she broek off to say:

“Keep yur ie on th rats. U beter hav th leed in yur lap, handy.”

So she dropt th lump into mi lap just at that moement, and I clapt mi legs together on it and she went on tauking. But oenly about a minit. Then she tuuk off th hank and luukt me straet in th faes, and verry plezant, and sez:

“Cum, now, whut’s yur reeal naem?”

“Wh—whut, mum?”

“Whut’s yur reeal naem? Is it Bil, or Tom, or Bob?—or whut is it?”

I rekon I shuuk liek a leef, and I didn’t noe hardly whut to do. But I sez:

“Pleez to don’t poek fun at a pur gerl liek me, mum. If I’m in th way heer, I’ll—”

“No, u wun’t. Set doun and stay whair u ar. I ain’t going to hert u, and I ain’t going to tel on u, nuther. U just tel me yur seecret, and trust me. I’ll keep it; and, whut’s mor, I’ll help u. So’ll mi oeld man if u wont him to. U see, u’re a runaway ’prentice, that’s all. It ain’t enything. Thair ain’t no harm in it. U’ve bin treeted bad, and u maed up yur miend to cut. Bles u, chield, I wouldn’t tel on u. Tel me all about it now, that’s a guud boy.”

So I sed it wouldn’t be no ues to tri to play it eny longger, and I wuud just maek a cleen brest and tel her evrything, but she musn’t go bak on her promis. Then I toeld her mi faather and muther was ded, and th law had bound me out to a meen oeld farmer in th cuntry therty miel bak frum th river, and he treeted me so bad I couldn’t stand it no longger; he went away to be gon a cupl of days, and so I tuuk mi chans and stoel sum of his dauter’s oeld cloeths and cleerd out, and I had bin three niets cuming th therty miels. I traveld niets, and hid daytimes and slept, and th bag of bred and meet I carryd frum hoem lasted me all th way, and I had a-plenty. I sed I beleevd mi unkl Abner Moore wuud taek cair of me, and so that was whi I struk out for this toun of Goshen.

“Goshen, chield? This ain’t Goshen. This is St. Petersburg. Goshen’s ten miel ferther up th river. Hoo toeld u this was Goshen?”

“Whi, a man I met at daybraek this morning, just as I was going to tern into th wuuds for mi reguelar sleep. He toeld me when th roeds forkt I must taek th riet hand, and fiev miel wuud fech me to Goshen.”

“He was drunk, I rekon. He toeld u just exactly rong.”

“Wel, he did act liek he was drunk, but it ain’t no mater now. I got to be mooving along. I’ll fech Goshen befor dayliet.”

“Hoeld on a minit. I’ll puut u up a snak to eet. U miet wont it.”









So she puut me up a snak, and sez:

“Say, when a cow’s laying doun, which end of her gets up ferst? Anser up prompt now—don’t stop to study oever it. Which end gets up ferst?”

“Th hiend end, mum.”

“Wel, then, a hors?”

“Th for’rard end, mum.”

“Which sied of a tree duz th moss gro on?”

“North sied.”

“If fifteen cows is brouzing on a hilsied, how meny of them eets with thair heds pointed th saem direcshun?”

“Th hoel fifteen, mum.”

“Wel, I rekon u hav livd in th cuntry. I thaut maybe u was trieing to hocus me agen. Whut’s yur reeal naem, now?”

“George Peters, mum.”

“Wel, tri to remember it, George. Don’t forget and tel me it’s Elexander befor u go, and then get out bi saying it’s George Elexander when I cach u. And don’t go about wimen in that oeld calico. U do a gerl tolerabl pur, but u miet fool men, maybe. Bles u, chield, when u set out to thred a needl don’t hoeld th thred stil and fech th needl up to it; hoeld th needl stil and poek th thred at it; that’s th way a wuuman moest allways duz, but a man allways duz t’uther way. And when u thro at a rat or enything, hich yurself up a tiptoe and fech yur hand up oever yur hed as aukward as u can, and mis yur rat about six or seven fuut. Thro stif-armd frum th shoelder, liek thair was a pivot thair for it to tern on, liek a gerl; not frum th rist and elbo, with yur arm out to wun sied, liek a boy. And, miend u, when a gerl tries to cach enything in her lap she throes her nees apart; she don’t clap them together, th way u did when u catched th lump of leed. Whi, I spoted u for a boy when u was threding th needl; and I contrievd th uther things just to maek serten. Now trot along to yur unkl, Sarah Mary Williams George Elexander Peters, and if u get into trubl u send werd to Mrs. Judith Loftus, which is me, and I’ll do whut I can to get u out of it. Keep th river roed all th way, and next tiem u tramp taek shoos and soks with u. Th river roed’s a roky wun, and yur feet’ll be in a condishun when u get to Goshen, I rekon.”

I went up th bank about fifty yards, and then I dubld on mi traks and slipt bak to whair mi canoo was, a guud pees belo th hous. I jumpt in, and was off in a hery. I went up-streem far enuf to maek th hed of th ieland, and then started across. I tuuk off th sun-bonet, for I didn’t wont no blinders on then. When I was about th midl I herd th clok begin to striek, so I stops and lisens; th sound cum faent oever th wauter but cleer—eleven. When I struk th hed of th ieland I never waeted to blo, tho I was moest winded, but I shuvd riet into th timber whair mi oeld camp uezd to be, and started a guud fier thair on a hi and dri spot.

Then I jumpt in th canoo and dug out for our plaes, a miel and a haf belo, as hard as I cuud go. I landed, and slopt thru th timber and up th rij and into th cavern. Thair Jim laed, sound asleep on th ground. I rouzd him out and sez:

“Git up and hump yurself, Jim! Thair ain’t a minit to looz. Thay’re after us!”









Jim never askt no qeschuns, he never sed a werd; but th way he werkt for th next haf an our shoed about how he was scaird. Bi that tiem evrything we had in th werld was on our raft, and she was redy to be shuvd out frum th wilo coev whair she was hid. We puut out th camp fier at th cavern th ferst thing, and didn’t sho a candl outsied after that.

I tuuk th canoo out frum th shor a litl pees, and tuuk a luuk; but if thair was a boet around I couldn’t see it, for stars and shadoes ain’t guud to see bi. Then we got out th raft and slipt along doun in th shaed, past th fuut of th ieland ded stil—never saying a werd.












CHAPTER XII.

It must a bin cloez on to wun o’clok when we got belo th ieland at last, and th raft did seem to go miety slo. If a boet was to cum along we was going to taek to th canoo and braek for th Illinois shor; and it was wel a boet didn’t cum, for we hadn’t ever thaut to puut th gun in th canoo, or a fishing-lien, or enything to eet. We was in ruther too much of a swet to think of so meny things. It worn’t guud jujment to puut evrything on th raft.

If th men went to th ieland I just expect thay found th camp fier I bilt, and wocht it all niet for Jim to cum. Enyways, thay stayd away frum us, and if mi bilding th fier never foold them it worn’t no fallt of mien. I playd it as lo doun on them as I cuud.

When th ferst streek of day began to sho we tied up to a toehed in a big bend on th Illinois sied, and hakt off cotonwuud branches with th hachet, and cuverd up th raft with them so she luukt liek thair had bin a caev-in in th bank thair. A toe-hed is a sandbar that has cottonwoods on it as thik as harro-teeth.

We had mountens on th Missouri shor and hevy timber on th Illinois sied, and th chanel was doun th Missouri shor at that plaes, so we worn’t afraed of enybody runing across us. We laed thair all day, and wocht th rafts and steamboats spin doun th Missouri shor, and up-bound steamboats fiet th big river in th midl. I toeld Jim all about th tiem I had jabering with that wuuman; and Jim sed she was a smart wun, and if she was to start after us herself she wouldn’t set doun and woch a camp fier—no, ser, she’d fech a daug. Wel, then, I sed, whi couldn’t she tel her huzband to fech a daug? Jim sed he bet she did think of it bi th tiem th men was redy to start, and he beleevd thay must a gon up-toun to get a daug and so thay lost all that tiem, or els we wouldn’t be heer on a toehed sixteen or seventeen miel belo th vilej—no, indeedy, we wuud be in that saem oeld toun agen. So I sed I didn’t cair whut was th reezon thay didn’t get us as long as thay didn’t.

When it was begining to cum on dark we poekt our heds out of th cotonwuud thiket, and luukt up and doun and across; nuthing in siet; so Jim tuuk up sum of th top planks of th raft and bilt a snug wigwom to get under in blaezing wether and raeny, and to keep th things dri. Jim maed a flor for th wigwom, and raezd it a fuut or mor abuv th level of th raft, so now th blankets and all th traps was out of reech of steemboet waevs. Riet in th midl of th wigwom we maed a layer of dert about fiev or six inches deep with a fraem around it for to hoeld it to its plaes; this was to bild a fier on in slopy wether or chily; th wigwom wuud keep it frum being seen. We maed an extra steering-or, too, becauz wun of th uthers miet get broek on a snag or sumthing. We fixt up a short forkt stik to hang th oeld lantern on, becauz we must allways liet th lantern whenever we see a steemboet cuming doun-streem, to keep frum geting run oever; but we wouldn’t hav to liet it for up-streem boets unles we see we was in whut thay call a “crossing”; for th river was prity hi yet, verry lo banks being stil a litl under wauter; so up-bound boets didn’t allways run th chanel, but hunted eezy wauter.

This second niet we run between seven and aet ours, with a curent that was maeking oever foer miel an our. We catched fish and taukt, and we tuuk a swim now and then to keep off sleepynes. It was kiend of solem, drifting doun th big, stil river, laying on our baks luuking up at th stars, and we didn’t ever feel liek tauking loud, and it worn’t offen that we laft—oenly a litl kiend of a lo chukl. We had miety guud wether as a jeneral thing, and nuthing ever hapend to us at all—that niet, nor th next, nor th next.

Evry niet we past touns, sum of them away up on blak hillsides, nuthing but just a shieny bed of liets; not a hous cuud u see. Th fifth niet we past St. Louis, and it was liek th hoel werld lit up. In St. Petersburg thay uezd to say thair was twenty or therty thouzand peepl in St. Louis, but I never beleevd it til I see that wunderful spred of liets at too o’clok that stil niet. Thair worn’t a sound thair; evrybody was asleep.

Evry niet now I uezd to slip ashor tords ten o’clok at sum litl vilej, and bi ten or fifteen sents’ werth of meel or baecon or uther stuf to eet; and sumtiems I lifted a chiken that worn’t roosting cumfortabl, and tuuk him along. Pap allways sed, taek a chiken when u get a chans, becauz if u don’t wont him yurself u can eezy fiend sumbody that duz, and a guud deed ain’t ever forgot. I never see pap when he didn’t wont th chiken himself, but that is whut he uezd to say, enyway.









Mornings befor dayliet I slipt into cornfields and borroed a wautermelon, or a mushmelon, or a punkin, or sum nue corn, or things of that kiend. Pap allways sed it worn’t no harm to borro things if u was meening to pay them bak sum tiem; but th wido sed it worn’t enything but a sofft naem for steeling, and no deesent body wuud do it. Jim sed he rekond th wido was partly riet and pap was partly riet; so th best way wuud be for us to pik out too or three things frum th list and say we wouldn’t borro them eny mor—then he rekond it wouldn’t be no harm to borro th uthers. So we taukt it oever all wun niet, drifting along doun th river, trieing to maek up our miends whether to drop th watermelons, or th cantelopes, or th mushmelons, or whut. But tords dayliet we got it all setld satisfactory, and conclooded to drop crabapples and p’simmons. We worn’t feeling just riet befor that, but it was all cumfortabl now. I was glad th way it cum out, too, becauz crabapples ain’t ever guud, and th p’simmons wouldn’t be riep for too or three munths yet.

We shot a wauter-foul now and then that got up too erly in th morning or didn’t go to bed erly enuf in th eevning. Taek it all round, we livd prity hi.

Th fifth niet belo St. Louis we had a big storm after midniet, with a power of thunder and lietning, and th raen pord doun in a solid sheet. We stayd in th wigwom and let th raft taek cair of itself. When th lietning glaird out we cuud see a big straet river ahed, and hi, roky blufs on boeth sieds. Bi and bi sez I, “Hel-lo, Jim, luuky yonder!” It was a steemboet that had kild herself on a rok. We was drifting straet doun for her. Th lietning shoed her verry distinkt. She was leening oever, with part of her uper dek abuv wauter, and u cuud see evry litl chimbly-gi cleen and cleer, and a chair bi th big bel, with an oeld slouch hat hanging on th bak of it, when th flashes cum.

Wel, it being away in th niet and stormy, and all so misteerius-liek, I felt just th way eny uther boy wuud a felt when I see that rek laying thair so mornful and loensum in th midl of th river. I wonted to get abord of her and slink around a litl, and see whut thair was thair. So I sez:

“Le’s land on her, Jim.”

But Jim was ded agenst it at ferst. He sez:

“I doan’ wont to go fool’n ’long er no rak. We’s doin’ blaem’ wel, en we beter let blaem’ wel aloen, as de guud buuk sez. Liek as not day’s a wochman on dat rak.”

“Wochman yur grandmuther,” I sez; “thair ain’t nuthing to woch but th texas and th pielot-hous; and do u rekon enybody’s going to resk his lief for a texas and a pielot-hous such a niet as this, when it’s liekly to braek up and wosh off doun th river eny minit?” Jim couldn’t say nuthing to that, so he didn’t tri. “And besieds,” I sez, “we miet borro sumthing werth having out of th capten’s staetroom. Seegars, I bet u—and cost fiev sents apees, solid cash. Steemboet captens is allways rich, and get sixty dolars a munth, and thay don’t cair a sent whut a thing costs, u noe, long as thay wont it. Stik a candl in yur poket; I can’t rest, Jim, til we giv her a rumejing. Do u rekon Tom Sawyer wuud ever go bi this thing? Not for pi, he wouldn’t. He’d call it an advencher—that’s whut he’d call it; and he’d land on that rek if it was his last act. And wouldn’t he thro stiel into it?—wouldn’t he spred himself, nor nuthing? Whi, u’d think it was Christopher C’lumbus discuvering Kingdom-Cum. I wish Tom Sawyer was heer.”

Jim he grumbld a litl, but giv in. He sed we mustn’t tauk eny mor than we cuud help, and then tauk miety lo. Th lietning shoed us th rek agen just in tiem, and we fetched th stabboard derrik, and maed fast thair.

Th dek was hi out heer. We went sneeking doun th sloep of it to labboard, in th dark, tords th texas, feeling our way slo with our feet, and spreding our hands out to fend off th gies, for it was so dark we couldn’t see no sien of them. Prity soon we struk th forward end of th skieliet, and clumb on to it; and th next step fetched us in frunt of th capten’s dor, which was oepen, and bi Jimminy, away doun thru th texas-hall we see a liet! and all in th saem second we seem to heer lo voises in yonder!

Jim whisperd and sed he was feeling powerful sik, and toeld me to cum along. I sez, all riet, and was going to start for th raft; but just then I herd a vois wael out and say:

“O, pleez don’t, boys; I swair I wun’t ever tel!”

Anuther vois sed, prity loud:

“It’s a lie, Jim Terner. U’ve acted this way befor. U allways wont mor’n yur shair of th truk, and u’ve allways got it, too, becauz u’ve swor ’t if u didn’t u’d tel. But this tiem u’ve sed it jest wun tiem too meny. U’re th meenest, treacherousest hound in this cuntry.”

Bi this tiem Jim was gon for th raft. I was just a-biling with cueriosity; and I sez to mieself, Tom Sawyer wouldn’t bak out now, and so I wun’t eether; I’m a-going to see whut’s going on heer. So I dropt on mi hands and nees in th litl pasej, and crept aft in th dark til thair worn’t but wun staetroom betwixt me and th cross-hall of th texas. Then in thair I see a man strecht on th flor and tied hand and fuut, and too men standing oever him, and wun of them had a dim lantern in his hand, and th uther wun had a pistol. This wun kept pointing th pistol at th man’s hed on th flor, and saying:

“I’d liek to! And I orter, too—a meen skunk!”









Th man on th flor wuud shrivel up and say, “O, pleez don’t, Bil; I hain’t ever goin’ to tel.”

And evry tiem he sed that th man with th lantern wuud laf and say:

“’Deed u ain’t! U never sed no trooer thing ’n that, u bet u.” And wuns he sed: “Heer him beg! and yit if we hadn’t got th best of him and tied him he’d a kild us boeth. And whut for? Jist for noth’n. Jist becauz we stuud on our riets—that’s whut for. But I lay u ain’t a-goin’ to threten noebody eny mor, Jim Terner. Puut up that pistol, Bil.”

Bil sez:

“I don’t wont to, Jake Packard. I’m for killin’ him—and didn’t he kil oeld Hatfield jist th saem way—and don’t he dezerv it?”

“But I don’t wont him kild, and I’ve got mi reezons for it.”

“Bles yo’ hart for them werds, Jake Packard! I’ll never forgit u long’s I liv!” sez th man on th flor, sort of blubbering.

Packard didn’t taek no noetis of that, but hung up his lantern on a nael and started tords whair I was thair in th dark, and moeshund Bil to cum. I crawfished as fast as I cuud about too yards, but th boet slanted so that I couldn’t maek verry guud tiem; so to keep frum geting run oever and catched I cralld into a staetroom on th uper sied. Th man caem a-pawing along in th dark, and when Packard got to mi staetroom, he sez:

“Heer—cum in heer.”

And in he cum, and Bil after him. But befor thay got in I was up in th uper berth, cornerd, and sorry I cum. Then thay stuud thair, with thair hands on th lej of th berth, and taukt. I couldn’t see them, but I cuud tel whair thay was bi th whisky thay’d bin having. I was glad I didn’t drink whisky; but it wouldn’t maed much diferens enyway, becauz moest of th tiem thay couldn’t a treed me becauz I didn’t breeth. I was too scaird. And, besieds, a body couldn’t breeth and heer such tauk. Thay taukt lo and ernest. Bil wonted to kil Terner. He sez:

“He’s sed he’ll tel, and he wil. If we was to giv boeth our shairs to him now it wouldn’t maek no diferens after th ro and th way we’ve servd him. Shor’s u’re born, he’ll tern Staet’s evidens; now u heer me. I’m for puuting him out of his trubls.”

“So’m I,” sez Packard, verry qieet.

“Blaem it, I’d sorter begun to think u wasn’t. Wel, then, that’s all riet. Le’s go and do it.”

“Hoeld on a minit; I hain’t had mi say yit. U lisen to me. Shooting’s guud, but thair’s qieeter ways if th thing’s got to be dun. But whut I say is this: it ain’t guud sens to go cort’n around after a hallter if u can git at whut u’re up to in sum way that’s jist as guud and at th saem tiem don’t bring u into no resks. Ain’t that so?”

“U bet it is. But how u goin’ to manej it this tiem?”

“Wel, mi iedeea is this: we’ll rusl around and gather up whutever pickins we’ve oeverluukt in th staterooms, and shuv for shor and hied th truk. Then we’ll waet. Now I say it ain’t a-goin’ to be mor’n too ours befo’ this rak braeks up and woshes off doun th river. See? He’ll be drownded, and wun’t hav noebody to blaem for it but his oen self. I rekon that’s a considerble siet beter ’n killin’ of him. I’m unfaevorabl to killin’ a man as long as u can git aroun’ it; it ain’t guud sens, it ain’t guud morals. Ain’t I riet?”









“Yes, I reck’n u ar. But s’poez she don’t braek up and wosh off?”

“Wel, we can waet th too ours enyway and see, can’t we?”

“All riet, then; cum along.”

So thay started, and I lit out, all in a coeld swet, and scrambld forward. It was dark as pich thair; but I sed, in a kiend of a cors whisper, “Jim!” and he anserd up, riet at mi elbo, with a sort of a moen, and I sez:

“Qik, Jim, it ain’t no tiem for fooling around and moaning; thair’s a gang of merderers in yonder, and if we don’t hunt up thair boet and set her drifting doun th river so thees feloes can’t get away frum th rek thair’s wun of ’em going to be in a bad fix. But if we fiend thair boet we can puut all of ’em in a bad fix—for th sherrif ’ll get ’em. Qik—hery! I’ll hunt th labboard sied, u hunt th stabboard. U start at th raft, and—”

“O, mi lordy, lordy! raf’’? Day ain’ no raf’ no mo’; she dun broek loos en gon I—en heer we is!”



















CHAPTER XIII.

Wel, I catched mi breth and moest faented. Shut up on a rek with such a gang as that! But it worn’t no tiem to be sentimentering. We’d got to fiend that boet now—had to hav it for ourselvs. So we went a-qaeking and shaeking doun th stabboard sied, and slo werk it was, too—seemd a week befor we got to th stern. No sien of a boet. Jim sed he didn’t beleev he cuud go eny ferther—so scaird he hadn’t hardly eny strength left, he sed. But I sed, cum on, if we get left on this rek we ar in a fix, shur. So on we prould agen. We struk for th stern of th texas, and found it, and then scrabbled along forwards on th skieliet, hanging on frum shuter to shuter, for th ej of th skieliet was in th wauter. When we got prity cloez to th cross-hall dor thair was th skif, shur enuf! I cuud just bairly see her. I felt ever so thankful. In anuther second I wuud a bin abord of her, but just then th dor oepend. Wun of th men stuk his hed out oenly about a cupl of fuut frum me, and I thaut I was gon; but he jerkt it in agen, and sez:

“Heev that blaem lantern out o’ siet, Bil!”

He flung a bag of sumthing into th boet, and then got in himself and set doun. It was Packard. Then Bil he cum out and got in. Packard sez, in a lo vois:

“All redy—shuv off!”

I couldn’t hardly hang on to th shuters, I was so weak. But Bil sez:

“Hoeld on—’d u go thru him?”

“No. Didn’t u?”

“No. So he’s got his shair o’ th cash yet.”

“Wel, then, cum along; no ues to taek truk and leev muny.”

“Say, wun’t he suspishun whut we’re up to?”

“Maybe he wun’t. But we got to hav it enyway. Cum along.”

So thay got out and went in.

Th dor slamd to becauz it was on th careend sied; and in a haf second I was in th boet, and Jim cum tumbling after me. I out with mi nief and cut th roep, and away we went!

We didn’t tuch an or, and we didn’t speek nor whisper, nor hardly eeven breeth. We went gliding swift along, ded sielent, past th tip of th padl-box, and past th stern; then in a second or too mor we was a hundred yards belo th rek, and th darknes soekt her up, evry last sien of her, and we was saef, and knowed it.

When we was three or foer hundred yards doun-streem we see th lantern sho liek a litl spark at th texas dor for a second, and we knowed bi that that th rascals had mist thair boet, and was begining to understand that thay was in just as much trubl now as Jim Terner was.

Then Jim mand th ors, and we tuuk out after our raft. Now was th ferst tiem that I begun to wery about th men—I rekon I hadn’t had tiem to befor. I begun to think how dredful it was, eeven for merderers, to be in such a fix. I sez to mieself, thair ain’t no teling but I miet cum to be a merderer mieself yet, and then how wuud I liek it? So sez I to Jim:

“Th ferst liet we see we’ll land a hundred yards belo it or abuv it, in a plaes whair it’s a guud hieding-plaes for u and th skif, and then I’ll go and fix up sum kiend of a yarn, and get sumbody to go for that gang and get them out of thair scraep, so thay can be hung when thair tiem cums.”

But that iedeea was a faeluer; for prity soon it begun to storm agen, and this tiem wers than ever. Th raen pord doun, and never a liet shoed; evrybody in bed, I rekon. We boomd along doun th river, woching for liets and woching for our raft. After a long tiem th raen let up, but th clouds stayd, and th lietning kept whimpering, and bi and bi a flash shoed us a blak thing ahed, floeting, and we maed for it.

It was th raft, and miety glad was we to get abord of it agen. We seen a liet now away doun to th riet, on shor. So I sed I wuud go for it. Th skif was haf fuul of plunder which that gang had stoel thair on th rek. We husld it on to th raft in a piel, and I toeld Jim to floet along doun, and sho a liet when he jujd he had gon about too miel, and keep it berning til I cum; then I mand mi ors and shuvd for th liet. As I got doun tords it three or foer mor shoed—up on a hilsied. It was a vilej. I cloezd in abuv th shor liet, and laed on mi ors and floeted. As I went bi I see it was a lantern hanging on th jackstaff of a dubl-hul ferryboet. I skimd around for th wochman, a-wundering whairabouts he slept; and bi and bi I found him roosting on th bitts forward, with his hed doun between his nees. I gaev his shoelder too or three litl shoves, and begun to cri.

He sterd up in a kiend of a startlish way; but when he see it was oenly me he tuuk a guud gap and strech, and then he sez:

“Helo, whut’s up? Don’t cri, bub. Whut’s th trubl?”









I sez:

“Pap, and mam, and sis, and—”

Then I broek doun. He sez:

“O, dang it now, don’t taek on so; we all has to hav our trubls, and this ’n ’ll cum out all riet. Whut’s th mater with ’em?”

“Thay’re—thay’re—ar u th wochman of th boet?”

“Yes,” he sez, kiend of prity-wel-satisfied liek. “I’m th capten and th oener and th maet and th pielot and wochman and hed dek-hand; and sumtiems I’m th fraet and pasenjers. I ain’t as rich as oeld Jim Hornback, and I can’t be so blaem’ jenerus and guud to Tom, Dick, and Harry as whut he is, and slam around muny th way he duz; but I’ve toeld him a meny a tiem ’t I wouldn’t traed plaeses with him; for, sez I, a saelor’s lief’s th lief for me, and I’m derned if I’d liv too miel out o’ toun, whair thair ain’t nuthing ever goin’ on, not for all his spondulicks and as much mor on top of it. Sez I—”

I broek in and sez:

“Thay’re in an awful pek of trubl, and—”

“Hoo is?”

“Whi, pap and mam and sis and Mis Hooker; and if u’d taek yur ferryboet and go up thair—”

“Up whair? Whair ar thay?”

“On th rek.”

“Whut rek?”

“Whi, thair ain’t but wun.”

“Whut, u don’t meen th Walter Scott?”

“Yes.”

“Guud land! whut ar thay doin’ thair, for graeshus sakes?”

“Wel, thay didn’t go thair a-perpos.”

“I bet thay didn’t! Whi, graet guudnes, thair ain’t no chans for ’em if thay don’t git off miety qik! Whi, how in th naeshun did thay ever git into such a scraep?”

“Eezy enuf. Mis Hooker was a-viziting up thair to th toun—”

“Yes, Booth’s Landing—go on.”

“She was a-viziting thair at Booth’s Landing, and just in th ej of th eevning she started oever with her nigger wuuman in th hors-ferry to stay all niet at her frend’s hous, Mis Whut-u-may-call-her I disremember her naem—and thay lost thair steering-or, and swung around and went a-floeting doun, stern ferst, about too miel, and sadl-baggsed on th rek, and th ferryman and th nigger wuuman and th horses was all lost, but Mis Hooker she maed a grab and got abord th rek. Wel, about an our after dark we cum along doun in our traeding-scow, and it was so dark we didn’t noetis th rek til we was riet on it; and so we sadl-baggsed; but all of us was saevd but Bil Whipl—and o, he was th best cretur!—I moest wish ’t it had bin me, I do.”

“Mi George! It’s th beatenest thing I ever struk. And then whut did u all do?”

“Wel, we holerd and tuuk on, but it’s so wied thair we couldn’t maek noebody heer. So pap sed sumbody got to get ashor and get help sumhow. I was th oenly wun that cuud swim, so I maed a dash for it, and Mis Hooker she sed if I didn’t striek help sooner, cum heer and hunt up her unkl, and he’d fix th thing. I maed th land about a miel belo, and bin fooling along ever sinss, trieing to get peepl to do sumthing, but thay sed, ’Whut, in such a niet and such a curent? Thair ain’t no sens in it; go for th steem ferry.’ Now if u’ll go and—”

“Bi Jackson, I’d liek to, and, blaem it, I don’t noe but I wil; but hoo in th dingnation’s a-going’ to pay for it? Do u rekon yur pap—”

“Whi that’s all riet. Mis Hooker she toel me, particuelar, that her unkl Hornback—”

“Graet guns! is he her unkl? Luuky heer, u braek for that liet oever yonder-way, and tern out west when u git thair, and about a qorter of a miel out u’ll cum to th tavern; tel ’em to dart u out to Jim Hornback’s, and he’ll fuut th bil. And don’t u fool around eny, becauz he’ll wont to noe th nues. Tel him I’ll hav his nees all saef befor he can get to toun. Hump yurself, now; I’m a-going up around th corner heer to roust out mi enjineer.”

I struk for th liet, but as soon as he ternd th corner I went bak and got into mi skif and baeld her out, and then puuld up shor in th eezy wauter about six hundred yards, and tukt mieself in amung sum woodboats; for I couldn’t rest eezy til I cuud see th ferryboet start. But taek it all around, I was feeling ruther cumfortabl on acounts of taeking all this trubl for that gang, for not meny wuud a dun it. I wisht th wido knowed about it. I jujd she wuud be proud of me for helping thees rapscallions, becauz rapscallions and ded beets is th kiend th wido and guud peepl taeks th moest interest in.









Wel, befor long heer cums th rek, dim and dusky, slieding along doun! A kiend of coeld shiver went thru me, and then I struk out for her. She was verry deep, and I see in a minit thair worn’t much chans for enybody being aliev in her. I puuld all around her and holerd a litl, but thair wasn’t eny anser; all ded stil. I felt a litl bit hevy-hearted about th gang, but not much, for I rekond if thay cuud stand it I cuud.

Then heer cums th ferryboet; so I shuvd for th midl of th river on a long doun-streem slant; and when I jujd I was out of ie-reech I laed on mi ors, and luukt bak and see her go and smel around th rek for Mis Hooker’s remainders, becauz th capten wuud noe her unkl Hornback wuud wont them; and then prity soon th ferryboet giv it up and went for th shor, and I laed into mi werk and went a-booming doun th river.

It did seem a powerful long tiem befor Jim’s liet shoed up; and when it did sho it luukt liek it was a thouzand miel off. Bi th tiem I got thair th skie was begining to get a litl gray in th eest; so we struk for an ieland, and hid th raft, and sunk th skif, and ternd in and slept liek ded peepl.

















CHAPTER XIV.

Bi and bi, when we got up, we ternd oever th truk th gang had stoel off of th rek, and found boots, and blankets, and cloeths, and all sorts of uther things, and a lot of buuks, and a spieglas, and three boxes of seegars. We hadn’t ever bin this rich befor in neether of our lievs. Th seegars was priem. We laed off all th afternoon in th wuuds tauking, and me reeding th buuks, and having a jeneral guud tiem. I toeld Jim all about whut hapend insied th rek and at th ferryboet, and I sed thees kiends of things was advenchers; but he sed he didn’t wont no mor advenchers. He sed that when I went in th texas and he cralld bak to get on th raft and found her gon he neerly died, becauz he jujd it was all up with him enyway it cuud be fixt; for if he didn’t get saevd he wuud get drownded; and if he did get saevd, hooever saevd him wuud send him bak hoem so as to get th reword, and then Mis Watson wuud sel him South, shur. Wel, he was riet; he was moest allways riet; he had an uncomon level hed for a nigger.

I red considerabl to Jim about kings and dueks and earls and such, and how gaudy thay drest, and how much stiel thay puut on, and calld eech uther yur majesty, and yur graes, and yur lordship, and so on, ’sted of mister; and Jim’s ies bugd out, and he was interested. He sez:

“I didn’ noe day was so meny un um. I hain’t hearn ’bout nun un um, skasely, but oelay King Sollermun, onless u counts dem kings dat’s in a pak er k’yards. How much do a king git?”

“Get?” I sez; “whi, thay get a thouzand dolars a munth if thay wont it; thay can hav just as much as thay wont; evrything belongs to them.”

“Ain’’ dat gay? En whut day got to do, Huck?”

“Thay don’t do nuthing! Whi, how u tauk! Thay just set around.”

“No; is dat so?”

“Of cors it is. Thay just set around—exsept, maybe, when thair’s a wor; then thay go to th wor. But uther tiems thay just laezy around; or go hawking—just hawking and sp—Sh!—d’ u heer a noiz?”

We skipt out and luukt; but it worn’t nuthing but th fluter of a steemboet’s wheel away doun, cuming around th point; so we cum bak.

“Yes,” sez I, “and uther tiems, when things is dul, thay fus with th parlyment; and if evrybody don’t go just so he whacks thair heds off. But moestly thay hang round th hairem.”

“Roun’ de which?”

“Hairem.”

“Whut’s de hairem?”









“Th plaes whair he keeps his wievs. Don’t u noe about th hairem? Solomon had wun; he had about a milyon wievs.”

“Whi, yes, dat’s so; I—I’d dun forgot it. A hairem’s a bo’d’n-hous, I reck’n. Mos’ liekly day has rakety tiems in de nussery. En I reck’n de wievs qorrels considable; en dat ’crees de raket. Yit day say Sollermun de wises’ man dat ever liv’. I doan’ taek no stok in dat. Bekase whi: wuud a wiez man wont to liv in de mids’ er sich a blim-blammin’ all de tiem? No—’deed he wouldn’t. A wiez man ’ud taek en buil’ a biler-factry; en den he cuud shet doun de biler-factry when he wont to res’.”

“Wel, but he was th wiezest man, enyway; becauz th wido she toeld me so, her oen self.”

“I doan k’yer whut de widder say, he worn’t no wiez man nuther. He had sum er de dad-fetchedes’ ways I ever see. Duz u noe ’bout dat chile dat he ’uz gwyne to chop in too?”

“Yes, th wido toeld me all about it.”

“Wel, den! Worn’ dat de beatenes’ noeshun in de worl’? U jes’ taek en luuk at it a minit. Dah’s de stump, dah—dat’s wun er de wimen; heah’s u—dat’s de yuther wun; I’s Sollermun; en dish yer dolar bil’s de chile. Bofe un u claems it. Whut duz I do? Duz I shin aroun’ mongs’ de naebors en fien out which un u de bil do b’long to, en han’ it oever to de riet wun, all saef en soun’, de way dat enybody dat had eny gumpshun wuud? No; I taek en whak de bil in too, en giv haf un it to u, en de yuther haf to de yuther wuuman. Dat’s de way Sollermun was gwyne to do wid de chile. Now I wont to ast u: whut’s de ues er dat haf a bil?—can’t bi noth’n wid it. En whut ues is a haf a chile? I wouldn’ giv a dern for a milyon un um.”

“But hang it, Jim, u’ve cleen mist th point—blaem it, u’ve mist it a thouzand miel.”

“Hoo? Me? Go ’long. Doan’ tauk to me ’bout yo’ pints. I reck’n I noes sens when I sees it; en day ain’ no sens in sich doin’s as dat. De ’spute worn’t ’bout a haf a chile, de ’spute was ’bout a hoel chile; en de man dat think he kin setl a ’spute ’bout a hoel chile wid a haf a chile doan’ noe enuf to cum in out’n de raen. Doan’ tauk to me ’bout Sollermun, Huck, I noes him bi de bak.”









“But I tel u u don’t get th point.”

“Blaem de point! I reck’n I noes whut I noes. En mien u, de reeal pient is doun furder—it’s doun deeper. It lays in de way Sollermun was raezd. U taek a man dat’s got on’y wun or too chillen; is dat man gwyne to be waseful o’ chillen? No, he ain’t; he can’t ’ford it. He noe how to value ’em. But u taek a man dat’s got ’bout fiev milyon chillen runnin’ roun’ de hous, en it’s diffunt. He as soon chop a chile in too as a cat. Day’s plenty mo’. A chile er too, mo’ er les, worn’t no consekens to Sollermun, dad fatch him!”

I never see such a nigger. If he got a noeshun in his hed wuns, thair worn’t no geting it out agen. He was th moest doun on Solomon of eny nigger I ever see. So I went to tauking about uther kings, and let Solomon slied. I toeld about Louis Sixteenth that got his hed cut off in France long tiem ago; and about his litl boy th dolfin, that wuud a bin a king, but thay tuuk and shut him up in jael, and sum say he died thair.

“Po’ litl chap.”

“But sum sez he got out and got away, and cum to America.”

“Dat’s guud! But he’ll be pooty loensum—day ain’ no kings heer, is day, Huck?”

“No.”

“Den he cain’t git no sichuaeshun. Whut he gwyne to do?”

“Wel, I don’t noe. Sum of them gets on th polees, and sum of them lerns peepl how to tauk French.”

“Whi, Huck, doan’ de French peepl tauk de saem way we duz?”

“No, Jim; u couldn’t understand a werd thay sed—not a singgl werd.”

“Wel, now, I be ding-busted! How do dat cum?”

“I don’t noe; but it’s so. I got sum of thair jaber out of a buuk. S’poez a man was to cum to u and say Polly-voo-franzy—whut wuud u think?”

“I wouldn’ think nuff’n; I’d taek en bust him oever de hed—dat is, if he worn’t whiet. I wouldn’t ’lo no nigger to call me dat.”

“Shuks, it ain’t calling u enything. It’s oenly saying, do u noe how to tauk French?”

“Wel, den, whi couldn’t he say it?”

“Whi, he is a-saying it. That’s a Frenchman’s way of saying it.”

“Wel, it’s a blaem ridicklous way, en I doan’ wont to heer no mo’ ’bout it. Day ain’ no sens in it.”

“Luuky heer, Jim; duz a cat tauk liek we do?”

“No, a cat don’t.”

“Wel, duz a cow?”

“No, a cow don’t, nuther.”

“Duz a cat tauk liek a cow, or a cow tauk liek a cat?”

“No, day don’t.”

“It’s nacheral and riet for ’em to tauk diferent frum eech uther, ain’t it?”

“Cors.”

“And ain’t it nacheral and riet for a cat and a cow to tauk diferent frum us?”

“Whi, mos’ sholy it is.”

“Wel, then, whi ain’t it nacheral and riet for a Frenchman to tauk diferent frum us? U anser me that.”

“Is a cat a man, Huck?”

“No.”

“Wel, den, day ain’t no sens in a cat talkin’ liek a man. Is a cow a man?—er is a cow a cat?”

“No, she ain’t eether of them.”

“Wel, den, she ain’t got no biznes to tauk liek eether wun er th yuther of ’em. Is a Frenchman a man?”

“Yes.”

“Wel, den! Dad blaem it, whi doan’ he tauk liek a man? U anser me dat!”

I see it worn’t no ues waesting werds—u can’t lern a nigger to argue. So I qit.










CHAPTER XV.

We jujd that three niets mor wuud fech us to Cairo, at th botom of Illinois, whair th Ohio River cums in, and that was whut we was after. We wuud sel th raft and get on a steemboet and go way up th Ohio amungst th free Staets, and then be out of trubl.

Wel, th second niet a fog begun to cum on, and we maed for a toehed to tee to, for it wouldn’t do to tri to run in a fog; but when I paddled ahed in th canoo, with th lien to maek fast, thair worn’t enything but litl saplings to tee to. I past th lien around wun of them riet on th ej of th cut bank, but thair was a stif curent, and th raft cum booming doun so lievly she tore it out bi th roots and away she went. I see th fog cloezing doun, and it maed me so sik and scaird I couldn’t buj for moest a haf a minit it seemd to me—and then thair worn’t no raft in siet; u couldn’t see twenty yards. I jumpt into th canoo and run bak to th stern, and grabd th padl and set her bak a stroek. But she didn’t cum. I was in such a hery I hadn’t untied her. I got up and tried to unti her, but I was so exsieted mi hands shuuk so I couldn’t hardly do enything with them.

As soon as I got started I tuuk out after th raft, hot and hevy, riet doun th toehed. That was all riet as far as it went, but th toehed worn’t sixty yards long, and th minit I floo bi th fuut of it I shot out into th solid whiet fog, and hadn’t no mor iedeea which way I was going than a ded man.

Thinks I, it wun’t do to padl; ferst I noe I’ll run into th bank or a toehed or sumthing; I got to set stil and floet, and yet it’s miety fijety biznes to hav to hoeld yur hands stil at such a tiem. I whooped and lisend. Away doun thair somewheres I heers a small hoop, and up cums mi spirits. I went tairing after it, lisening sharp to heer it agen. Th next tiem it cum I see I worn’t heding for it, but heding away to th riet of it. And th next tiem I was heding away to th left of it—and not gaening on it much eether, for I was flieing around, this way and that and t’uther, but it was going straet ahed all th tiem.

I did wish th fool wuud think to beet a tin pan, and beet it all th tiem, but he never did, and it was th stil plaeses between th whoops that was maeking th trubl for me. Wel, I faut along, and directly I heers th hoop behiend me. I was tanggld guud now. That was sumbody els’s hoop, or els I was ternd around.

I throwed th padl doun. I herd th hoop agen; it was behiend me yet, but in a diferent plaes; it kept cuming, and kept chaenjing its plaes, and I kept ansering, til bi and bi it was in frunt of me agen, and I knowed th curent had swung th canoo’s hed doun-streem, and I was all riet if that was Jim and not sum uther raftsman holering. I couldn’t tel nuthing about voises in a fog, for nuthing don’t luuk nacheral nor sound nacheral in a fog.

Th hooping went on, and in about a minit I cum a-booming doun on a cut bank with smoeky goests of big trees on it, and th curent throwed me off to th left and shot bi, amungst a lot of snags that fairly rord, th currrent was tairing bi them so swift.

In anuther second or too it was solid whiet and stil agen. I set perfectly stil then, lisening to mi hart thump, and I rekon I didn’t draw a breth whiel it thumpt a hundred.

I just giv up then. I knowed whut th mater was. That cut bank was an ieland, and Jim had gon doun t’uther sied of it. It worn’t no toehed that u cuud floet bi in ten minits. It had th big timber of a reguelar ieland; it miet be fiev or six miels long and mor than haf a miel wied.

I kept qieet, with mi eers cokt, about fifteen minits, I rekon. I was floeting along, of cors, foer or fiev miels an our; but u don’t ever think of that. No, u feel liek u ar laying ded stil on th wauter; and if a litl glimps of a snag slips bi u don’t think to yurself how fast u’re going, but u cach yur breth and think, mi! how that snag’s tairing along. If u think it ain’t dizmal and loensum out in a fog that way bi yurself in th niet, u tri it wuns—u’ll see.









Next, for about a haf an our, I whoops now and then; at last I heers th anser a long ways off, and tries to folo it, but I couldn’t do it, and directly I jujd I’d got into a nest of toeheds, for I had litl dim glimpses of them on boeth sieds of me—sumtiems just a narro chanel between, and sum that I couldn’t see I knowed was thair becauz I’d heer th wosh of th curent agenst th oeld ded brush and trash that hung oever th banks. Wel, I worn’t long loosing th whoops doun amungst th toeheds; and I oenly tried to chaes them a litl whiel, enyway, becauz it was wers than chaesing a Jak-o’-lantern. U never knowed a sound doj around so, and swop plaeses so qik and so much.

I had to claw away frum th bank prity lievly foer or fiev tiems, to keep frum noking th ielands out of th river; and so I jujd th raft must be buting into th bank evry now and then, or els it wuud get ferther ahed and cleer out of heering—it was floeting a litl faster than whut I was.

Wel, I seemd to be in th oepen river agen bi and bi, but I couldn’t heer no sien of a hoop nowheres. I rekond Jim had fetched up on a snag, maybe, and it was all up with him. I was guud and tierd, so I laed doun in th canoo and sed I wouldn’t bother no mor. I didn’t wont to go to sleep, of cors; but I was so sleepy I couldn’t help it; so I thaut I wuud taek jest wun litl cat-nap.









But I rekon it was mor than a cat-nap, for when I waekt up th stars was shiening briet, th fog was all gon, and I was spining doun a big bend stern ferst. Ferst I didn’t noe whair I was; I thaut I was dreeming; and when things began to cum bak to me thay seemd to cum up dim out of last week.

It was a monstrus big river heer, with th tallest and th thikest kiend of timber on boeth banks; just a solid wall, as wel as I cuud see bi th stars. I luukt away doun-streem, and seen a blak spek on th wauter. I tuuk after it; but when I got to it it worn’t nuthing but a cupl of sawlogs maed fast together. Then I see anuther spek, and chaest that; then anuther, and this tiem I was riet. It was th raft.

When I got to it Jim was seting thair with his hed doun between his nees, asleep, with his riet arm hanging oever th steering-or. Th uther or was smasht off, and th raft was literd up with leevs and branches and dert. So she’d had a ruf tiem.

I maed fast and laed doun under Jim’s noez on th raft, and began to gap, and strech mi fists out agenst Jim, and sez:

“Helo, Jim, hav I bin asleep? Whi didn’t u ster me up?”

“Guudnes graeshus, is dat u, Huck? En u ain’ ded—u ain’ drownded—u’s bak agin? It’s too guud for troo, huny, it’s too guud for troo. Lemme luuk at u chile, lemme feel o’ u. No, u ain’ ded! u’s bak agin, ’liv en soun’, jis de saem oelay Huck—de saem oelay Huck, thanks to guudnes!”

“Whut’s th mater with u, Jim? U bin a-drinking?”

“Drinkin’? Has I ben a-drinkin’? Has I had a chans to be a-drinkin’?”

“Wel, then, whut maeks u tauk so wield?”

“How duz I tauk wield?”

“How? Whi, hain’t u bin tauking about mi cuming bak, and all that stuf, as if I’d bin gon away?”

“Huck—Huck Finn, u luuk me in de ie; luuk me in de ie. Hain’t u ben gon away?”

“Gon away? Whi, whut in th naeshun do u meen? I hain’t bin gon anywheres. Whair wuud I go to?”

“Wel, luuky heer, boss, day’s sumf’n rong, day is. Is I me, or hoo is I? Is I heah, or whah is I? Now dat’s whut I wonts to noe.”

“Wel, I think u’re heer, plaen enuf, but I think u’re a tanggl-heded oeld fool, Jim.”

“I is, is I? Wel, u anser me dis: Didn’t u toet out de lien in de canoo fer to maek fas’ to de toe-hed?”

“No, I didn’t. Whut toe-hed? I hain’t see no toe-hed.”

“U hain’t seen no toehed? Luuky heer, didn’t de lien puul loos en de raf’ go a-hummin’ doun de river, en leev u en de canoo behine in de fog?”

“Whut fog?”

“Whi, de fog!—de fog dat’s bin aroun’ all niet. En didn’t u hoop, en didn’t I hoop, tel we got mix’ up in de ielands en wun un us got los’ en t’uther wun was jis’ as guud as los’, ’kase he didn’ noe whah he wuz? En didn’t I bust up agin a lot er dem ielands en hav a turrible tiem en mos’ git drownded? Now ain’ dat so, boss—ain’t it so? U anser me dat.”

“Wel, this is too meny for me, Jim. I hain’t seen no fog, nor no ielands, nor no trubls, nor nuthing. I bin seting heer tauking with u all niet til u went to sleep about ten minits ago, and I rekon I dun th saem. U couldn’t a got drunk in that tiem, so of cors u’ve bin dreeming.”

“Dad fech it, how is I gwyne to dreem all dat in ten minits?”

“Wel, hang it all, u did dreem it, becauz thair didn’t eny of it hapen.”

“But, Huck, it’s all jis’ as plaen to me as—”

“It don’t maek no diferens how plaen it is; thair ain’t nuthing in it. I noe, becauz I’ve bin heer all th tiem.”

Jim didn’t say nuthing for about fiev minits, but set thair studying oever it. Then he sez:

“Wel, den, I reck’n I did dreem it, Huck; but daug mi cats ef it ain’t de powerfullest dreem I ever see. En I hain’t ever had no dreem b’fo’ dat’s tierd me liek dis wun.”

“O, wel, that’s all riet, becauz a dreem duz tier a body liek evrything sumtiems. But this wun was a staving dreem; tel me all about it, Jim.”

So Jim went to werk and toeld me th hoel thing riet thru, just as it hapend, oenly he paented it up considerabl. Then he sed he must start in and “’terpret” it, becauz it was sent for a worning. He sed th ferst toehed stuud for a man that wuud tri to do us sum guud, but th curent was anuther man that wuud get us away frum him. Th whoops was wornings that wuud cum to us evry now and then, and if we didn’t tri hard to maek out to understand them thay’d just taek us into bad luk, ’sted of keeping us out of it. Th lot of toeheds was trubls we was going to get into with qorrelsum peepl and all kiends of meen foeks, but if we miended our biznes and didn’t tauk bak and agravaet them, we wuud puul thru and get out of th fog and into th big cleer river, which was th free Staets, and wouldn’t hav no mor trubl.

It had clouded up prity dark just after I got on to th raft, but it was cleering up agen now.

“O, wel, that’s all interpreted wel enuf as far as it goes, Jim,” I sez; “but whut duz thees things stand for?”

It was th leevs and rubish on th raft and th smasht or. U cuud see them ferst-raet now.

Jim luukt at th trash, and then luukt at me, and bak at th trash agen. He had got th dreem fixt so strong in his hed that he couldn’t seem to shaek it loos and get th facts bak into its plaes agen riet away. But when he did get th thing straetend around he luukt at me stedy without ever smieling, and sez:

“Whut do day stan’ for? I’se gwyne to tel u.
