“I’m in, up to th hub, for enything that wil pay, Bilgewater; but, u see, I don’t noe nuthing about play-actin’, and hain’t ever seen much of it. I was too small when pap uezd to hav ’em at th palas. Do u rekon u can lern me?”

“Eezy!”

“All riet. I’m jist a-freezn’ for sumthing fresh, enyway. Le’s comens riet away.”

So th duek he toeld him all about hoo Romeo was and hoo Juliet was, and sed he was uezd to being Romeo, so th king cuud be Juliet.

“But if Juliet’s such a yung gal, duek, mi peeld hed and mi whiet whiskers is goin’ to luuk oncommon od on her, maybe.”

“No, don’t u wery; thees cuntry jakes wun’t ever think of that. Besieds, u noe, u’ll be in costoom, and that maeks all th diferens in th werld; Juliet’s in a balcony, enjoying th moonliet befor she goes to bed, and she’s got on her niet-goun and her rufld nightcap. Heer ar th costooms for th parts.”











He got out too or three curten-calico soots, which he sed was meedyevil armor for Richard III. and t’uther chap, and a long whiet coton nietshert and a rufld nightcap to mach. Th king was satisfied; so th duek got out his buuk and red th parts oever in th moest splendid spred-eegl way, pransing around and acting at th saem tiem, to sho how it had got to be dun; then he giv th buuk to th king and toeld him to get his part bi hart.

Thair was a litl wun-hors toun about three miel doun th bend, and after diner th duek sed he had ciphered out his iedeea about how to run in dayliet without it being dangersome for Jim; so he alowd he wuud go doun to th toun and fix that thing. Th king alowd he wuud go, too, and see if he couldn’t striek sumthing. We was out of coffy, so Jim sed I beter go along with them in th canoo and get sum.

When we got thair thair worn’t noebody stering; streets empty, and perfectly ded and stil, liek Sunday. We found a sik nigger suning himself in a bak yard, and he sed evrybody that worn’t too yung or too sik or too oeld was gon to camp-meeting, about too miel bak in th wuuds. Th king got th direcshuns, and alowd he’d go and werk that camp-meeting for all it was werth, and I miet go, too.

Th duek sed whut he was after was a printing-offis. We found it; a litl bit of a consern, up oever a carpenter shop—carpenters and printers all gon to th meeting, and no dors lokt. It was a derty, literd-up plaes, and had ink marks, and handbills with pikchers of horses and runaway niggers on them, all oever th walls. Th duek shed his coet and sed he was all riet now. So me and th king lit out for th camp-meeting.

We got thair in about a haf an our fairly driping, for it was a moest awful hot day. Thair was as much as a thouzand peepl thair frum twenty miel around. Th wuuds was fuul of teems and wagons, hicht everywheres, feeding out of th wagon-traufs and stomping to keep off th flies. Thair was sheds maed out of poels and rooft oever with branches, whair thay had lemonaed and jinjerbred to sel, and piels of watermelons and green corn and such-liek truk.

Th preeching was going on under th saem kiends of sheds, oenly thay was biger and held crouds of peepl. Th benches was maed out of outsied slabs of logs, with hoels bord in th round sied to driev stiks into for legs. Thay didn’t hav no baks. Th preechers had hi platforms to stand on at wun end of th sheds. Th wimen had on sun-bonnets; and sum had linsey-woolsey froks, sum gingam wuns, and a fue of th yung wuns had on calico. Sum of th yung men was bairfuuted, and sum of th children didn’t hav on eny cloeths but just a toe-linen shert. Sum of th oeld wimen was niting, and sum of th yung foeks was corting on th sli.











Th ferst shed we cum to th preecher was liening out a him. He liend out too liens, evrybody sung it, and it was kiend of grand to heer it, thair was so meny of them and thay dun it in such a rouzing way; then he liend out too mor for them to sing—and so on. Th peepl woek up mor and mor, and sung louder and louder; and tords th end sum begun to groen, and sum begun to shout. Then th preecher begun to preech, and begun in ernest, too; and went weeving ferst to wun sied of th platform and then th uther, and then a-leening doun oever th frunt of it, with his arms and his body going all th tiem, and shouting his werds out with all his miet; and evry now and then he wuud hoeld up his Biebl and spred it oepen, and kiend of pas it around this way and that, shouting, “It’s th braezen serpent in th wildernes! Luuk upon it and liv!” And peepl wuud shout out, “Glory!—A-a-men!” And so he went on, and th peepl groening and crieing and saying aamen:

“O, cum to th morners’ bench! cum, blak with sin! (Aamen!) cum, sik and sor! (Aamen!) cum, laem and hallt and bliend! (Aamen!) cum, por and needy, sunk in shaem! (A-A-Men!) cum, all that’s worn and soild and sufering!—cum with a broeken spirit! cum with a contriet hart! cum in yur rags and sin and dert! th wauters that clenz is free, th dor of heven stands oepen—o, enter in and be at rest!” (A-A-Men! Glory, Glory Halelooya!)

And so on. U couldn’t maek out whut th preecher sed eny mor, on acount of th shouting and crieing. Foeks got up everywheres in th croud, and werkt thair way just bi maen strength to th morners’ bench, with th teers runing doun thair faeses; and when all th morners had got up thair to th frunt benches in a croud, thay sung and shouted and flung themselvs doun on th straw, just craezy and wield.

Wel, th ferst I knowed th king got a-going, and u cuud heer him oever evrybody; and next he went a-charjing up on to th platform, and th preecher he begd him to speek to th peepl, and he dun it. He toeld them he was a pieret—bin a pieret for therty yeers out in th Indian Oeshan—and his croo was thind out considerabl last spring in a fiet, and he was hoem now to taek out sum fresh men, and thanks to guudnes he’d bin robd last niet and puut ashor off of a steemboet without a sent, and he was glad of it; it was th blessedest thing that ever hapend to him, becauz he was a chaenjd man now, and hapy for th ferst tiem in his lief; and, pur as he was, he was going to start riet off and werk his way bak to th Indian Oeshan, and puut in th rest of his lief trieing to tern th pierets into th troo path; for he cuud do it beter than enybody els, being aqaented with all pieret croos in that oeshan; and tho it wuud taek him a long tiem to get thair without muny, he wuud get thair enyway, and evry tiem he convinst a pieret he wuud say to him, “Don’t u thank me, don’t u giv me no credit; it all belongs to them deer peepl in Pokeville camp-meeting, nacheral bruthers and benefactors of th raes, and that deer preecher thair, th trooest frend a pieret ever had!”











And then he busted into teers, and so did evrybody. Then sumbody sings out, “Taek up a colecshun for him, taek up a colecshun!” Wel, a haf a duzen maed a jump to do it, but sumbody sings out, “Let him pas th hat around!” Then evrybody sed it, th preecher too.

So th king went all thru th croud with his hat swobing his ies, and blesing th peepl and praezing them and thanking them for being so guud to th pur pierets away off thair; and evry litl whiel th prityest kiend of gerls, with th teers runing doun thair cheeks, wuud up and ask him wuud he let them kis him for to remember him bi; and he allways dun it; and sum of them he hugd and kist as meny as fiev or six tiems—and he was invieted to stay a week; and evrybody wonted him to liv in thair houses, and sed thay’d think it was an onor; but he sed as this was th last day of th camp-meeting he couldn’t do no guud, and besieds he was in a swet to get to th Indian Oeshan riet off and go to werk on th pierets.

When we got bak to th raft and he cum to count up he found he had colected aety-seven dolars and seventy-fiev sents. And then he had fetched away a three-galon jug of whisky, too, that he found under a wagon when he was starting hoem thru th wuuds. Th king sed, taek it all around, it laed oever eny day he’d ever puut in in th missionarying lien. He sed it worn’t no ues tauking, heathens don’t amount to shuks alongsied of pierets to werk a camp-meeting with.

Th duek was thinking he’d bin doing prity wel til th king cum to sho up, but after that he didn’t think so so much. He had set up and printed off too litl jobs for farmers in that printing-offis—hors bils—and tuuk th muny, foer dolars. And he had got in ten dolars’ werth of advertiezments for th paeper, which he sed he wuud puut in for foer dolars if thay wuud pay in advans—so thay dun it. Th pries of th paeper was too dolars a yeer, but he tuuk in three subscriptions for haf a dolar apees on condishun of them paying him in advans; thay wer going to pay in cordwood and unyons as uezhual, but he sed he had just baut th consern and nokt doun th pries as lo as he cuud aford it, and was going to run it for cash. He set up a litl pees of poeetry, which he maed, himself, out of his oen hed—three verses—kiend of sweet and saddish—th naem of it was, “Yes, crush, coeld werld, this braeking hart”—and he left that all set up and redy to print in th paeper, and didn’t charj nuthing for it. Wel, he tuuk in nien dolars and a haf, and sed he’d dun a prity sqair day’s werk for it.

Then he shoed us anuther litl job he’d printed and hadn’t charjd for, becauz it was for us. It had a pikcher of a runaway nigger with a bundl on a stik oever his shoelder, and “$200 reword” under it. Th reeding was all about Jim, and just descriebd him to a dot. It sed he run away frum St. Jacques’ plantaeshun, forty miel belo Nue Orleans, last winter, and liekly went north, and hooever wuud cach him and send him bak he cuud hav th reword and expenses.











“Now,” sez th duek, “after to-niet we can run in th daytiem if we wont to. Whenever we see enybody cuming we can tee Jim hand and fuut with a roep, and lay him in th wigwom and sho this handbil and say we capcherd him up th river, and wer too pur to travel on a steemboet, so we got this litl raft on credit frum our frends and ar going doun to get th reword. Handcufs and chaens wuud luuk stil beter on Jim, but it wouldn’t go wel with th story of us being so pur. Too much liek jooelry. Roeps ar th corect thing—we must prezerv th uenitys, as we say on th bords.”

We all sed th duek was prity smart, and thair couldn’t be no trubl about runing daytimes. We jujd we cuud maek miels enuf that niet to get out of th reech of th powwow we rekond th duek’s werk in th printing offis was going to maek in that litl toun; then we cuud boom riet along if we wonted to.

We laed lo and kept stil, and never shuvd out til neerly ten o’clok; then we slid bi, prity wied away frum th toun, and didn’t hoist our lantern til we was cleer out of siet of it.

When Jim calld me to taek th woch at foer in th morning, he sez:

“Huck, duz u reck’n we gwyne to run acrost eny mo’ kings on dis trip?”

“No,” I sez, “I rekon not.”

“Wel,” sez he, “dat’s all riet, den. I doan’ mien wun er too kings, but dat’s enuf. Dis wun’s powerful drunk, en de duek ain’ much beter.”

I found Jim had bin trieing to get him to tauk French, so he cuud heer whut it was liek; but he sed he had bin in this cuntry so long, and had so much trubl, he’d forgot it.














CHAPTER XXI.

It was after sun-up now, but we went riet on and didn’t tee up. Th king and th duek ternd out bi and bi luuking prity rusty; but after thay’d jumpt oeverbord and tuuk a swim it chippered them up a guud deel. After brekfast th king he tuuk a seet on th corner of th raft, and puuld off his boots and roeld up his briches, and let his legs danggl in th wauter, so as to be cumfortabl, and lit his piep, and went to geting his Romeo and Juliet bi hart. When he had got it prity guud him and th duek begun to practis it together. Th duek had to lern him oever and oever agen how to say evry speech; and he maed him si, and puut his hand on his hart, and after a whiel he sed he dun it prity wel; “oenly,” he sez, “u mustn’t belo out Romeo! that way, liek a buul—u must say it sofft and sik and languishy, so—R-o-o-meo! that is th iedeea; for Juliet’s a deer sweet meer chield of a gerl, u noe, and she doesn’t bray liek a jakas.”

Wel, next thay got out a cupl of long sords that th duek maed out of oek laths, and begun to practis th sord fiet—th duek calld himself Richard III.; and th way thay laed on and pranced around th raft was grand to see. But bi and bi th king tript and fel oeverbord, and after that thay tuuk a rest, and had a tauk about all kiends of advenchers thay’d had in uther tiems along th river.

After diner th duek sez:

“Wel, Capet, we’ll wont to maek this a ferst-clas sho, u noe, so I ges we’ll ad a litl mor to it. We wont a litl sumthing to anser oncors with, enyway.”

“Whut’s onkores, Bilgewater?”

Th duek toeld him, and then sez:

“I’ll anser bi doing th Hieland fling or th saelor’s hornpiep; and u—wel, let me see—o, I’ve got it—u can do Hamlet’s soliloqy.”

“Hamlet’s which?”

“Hamlet’s soliloqy, u noe; th moest selebraeted thing in Shakespeare. Aa, it’s subliem, subliem! Allways fetches th hous. I haeven’t got it in th buuk—I’ve oenly got wun voluem—but I rekon I can pees it out frum memory. I’ll just wauk up and doun a minit, and see if I can call it bak frum recolecshun’s vallts.”











So he went to marching up and doun, thinking, and frouning horribl evry now and then; then he wuud hoist up his iebrows; next he wuud sqeez his hand on his forhed and stager bak and kiend of moen; next he wuud si, and next he’d let on to drop a teer. It was buetiful to see him. Bi and bi he got it. He toeld us to giv atenshun. Then he strieks a moest noebl atitued, with wun leg shuvd forwards, and his arms strecht away up, and his hed tilted bak, luuking up at th skie; and then he begins to rip and rave and grit his teeth; and after that, all thru his speech, he hould, and spred around, and sweld up his chest, and just nokt th spots out of eny acting ever I see befor. This is th speech—I lernd it, eezy enuf, whiel he was lerning it to th king:









To be, or not to be; that is th bair bodkin
That maeks calamity of so long lief;
For hoo wuud fardels bair, til Birnam Wuud do cum to Dunsinane,
But that th feer of sumthing after deth Merders th inosent sleep,
Graet naecher’s second cors,
And maeks us rather sling th arroes of outraejus forchun
Than fli to uthers that we noe not of.
Thair’s th respect must giv us pauz:
Waek Duncan with thi noking! I wuud thow couldst;
For hoo wuud bair th whips and scorns of tiem,
Th opresor’s rong, th proud man’s contuumely,
Th law’s delay, and th qieeetus which his pangs miet taek.
In th ded waest and midl of th niet, when churchyards yaun
In customairy soots of solem blak,
But that th undiscovered cuntry frum hoos bourne no traveler reterns,
Breeths forth contaejon on th werld,
And thus th naetiv hue of rezolooshun, liek th pur cat i’ th adej,
Is sicklied o’er with cair.
And all th clouds that loeerd o’er our houstops,
With this regard thair curents tern ari,
And looz th naem of acshun.
’Tis a consumaeshun devoutly to be wisht.
But sofft u, th fair Ophelia:
Ope not thi ponderus and marbl jaws.
But get thee to a nunery—go!

Wel, th oeld man he liekt that speech, and he miety soon got it so he cuud do it ferst raet. It seemd liek he was just born for it; and when he had his hand in and was exsieted, it was perfectly luvly th way he wuud rip and teer and rair up behiend when he was geting it off.

Th ferst chans we got, th duek he had sum sho bils printed; and after that, for too or three days as we floeted along, th raft was a moest uncomon lievly plaes, for thair worn’t nuthing but sord-fieting and rehersing—as th duek calld it—going on all th tiem. Wun morning, when we was prity wel doun th Staet of Arkansaw, we cum in siet of a litl wun-hors toun in a big bend; so we tied up about three-qorters of a miel abuv it, in th mouth of a crik which was shut in liek a tunel bi th siepres trees, and all of us but Jim tuuk th canoo and went doun thair to see if thair was eny chans in that plaes for our sho.

We struk it miety luky; thair was going to be a sercus thair that afternoon, and th cuntry peepl was allredy begining to cum in, in all kiends of oeld shackly wagons, and on horses. Th sercus wuud leev befor niet, so our sho wuud hav a prity guud chans. Th duek he hierd th cort hous, and we went around and stuk up our bils. Thay red liek this: 

  Shaksperean Revieval!!!

  Wunderful Atracshun!

  For Wun Niet Oenly! Th werld renound trajeedians,

  David Garrick th yungger, of Drury Laen Theeater, London,

  and

  Edmund Kean th elder, of th Royal Haymarket Theeater, Whitechapel,
  Puuding Laen, Piccadilly, London, and th Royal Continental Theatres, in
  thair subliem Shaksperean Spectacl entietld Th Balcony Seen in

  Romeo and Juliet!!!

  Romeo...................................... Mr. Garrick.

  Juliet..................................... Mr. Kean.

  Asisted bi th hoel strength of th cumpany!

  Nue costooms, nue seenery, nue apointments!

  Allso:

  Th thriling, masterly, and blud-curdling Braud-sord conflict In
  Richard III.!!!

  Richard III................................ Mr. Garrick.

  Richmond................................... Mr. Kean.

  allso:

  (bi speshal reqest,)

  Hamlet’s Imortal Soliloqy!!

  Bi th Ilustrius Kean!

  Dun bi him 300 consecuetiv niets in Paris!

  For Wun Niet Oenly,

  On acount of imperrativ European engaejments!

  Admishun 25 sents; children and servants, 10 sents.

Then we went loafing around th toun. Th stors and houses was moest all oeld shackly dried-up fraem conserns that hadn’t ever bin paented; thay was set up three or foer fuut abuv ground on stilts, so as to be out of reech of th wauter when th river was oeverfloed. Th houses had litl gardens around them, but thay didn’t seem to raez hardly enything in them but jimpson weeds, and sunflowers, and ash-piels, and oeld curld-up boots and shoos, and peeses of botls, and rags, and playd-out tin-wair. Th fenses was maed of diferent kiends of bords, naeld on at diferent tiems; and thay leend evry which-way, and had gaets that didn’t generly hav but wun hinj—a lether wun. Sum of th fenses had bin whietwosht, sum tiem or anuther, but th duek sed it was in Clumbus’s tiem, liek enuf. Thair was generly hogs in th garden, and peepl drieving them out.

All th stors was along wun street. Thay had whiet domestic aunings in frunt, and th cuntry peepl hicht thair horses to th auning-poests. Thair was empty drygoods boxes under th aunings, and loefers roosting on them all day long, whittling them with thair Barlow nievs; and chawing tobaco, and gaeping and yauning and streching—a miety ornery lot. Thay generly had on yelo straw hats moest as wied as an umbrela, but didn’t wair no coets nor waistcoats, thay calld wun anuther Bil, and Buk, and Hank, and Joe, and Andy, and taukt laezy and drawly, and uezd considerabl meny cuss werds. Thair was as meny as wun loefer leening up agenst evry auning-poest, and he moest allways had his hands in his briches-pokets, exsept when he fetched them out to lend a chaw of tobaco or scrach. Whut a body was heering amungst them all th tiem was:

“Gimme a chaw ’v tobacker, Hank.”

“Cain’t; I hain’t got but wun chaw left. Ask Bil.”











Maybe Bil he givs him a chaw; maybe he lies and sez he ain’t got nun. Sum of them kiends of loefers never has a sent in th werld, nor a chaw of tobaco of thair oen. Thay get all thair chawing bi borroeing; thay say to a felo, “I wisht u’d len’ me a chaw, Jak, I jist this minit giv Ben Thompson th last chaw I had”—which is a lie prity much everytime; it don’t fool noebody but a straenjer; but Jak ain’t no straenjer, so he sez:

“U giv him a chaw, did u? So did yur sister’s cat’s grandmuther. U pay me bak th chaws u’ve awready borry’d off’n me, Lafe Buckner, then I’ll loen u wun or too tun of it, and wun’t charj u no bak intrust, nuther.”

“Wel, I did pay u bak sum of it wunst.”

“Yes, u did—’bout six chaws. U borry’d stor tobacker and paed bak nigger-hed.”

Stor tobaco is flat blak plug, but thees feloes moestly chaws th nacheral leef twisted. When thay borro a chaw thay don’t generly cut it off with a nief, but set th plug in between thair teeth, and naw with thair teeth and tug at th plug with thair hands til thay get it in too; then sumtiems th wun that oens th tobaco luuks mornful at it when it’s handed bak, and sez, sarcastic:

“Heer, gimme th chaw, and u taek th plug.”

All th streets and laens was just mud; thay worn’t nuthing els but mud—mud as blak as tar and ni about a fuut deep in sum plaeses, and too or three inches deep in all th plaeses. Th hogs loeft and grunted around everywheres. U’d see a mudy soe and a liter of pigs cum lazying along th street and whollop herself riet doun in th way, whair foeks had to wauk around her, and she’d strech out and shut her ies and waev her eers whilst th pigs was milking her, and luuk as hapy as if she was on salary. And prity soon u’d heer a loefer sing out, “Hi! so boy! sik him, Tige!” and away th soe wuud go, sqeeling moest horribl, with a daug or too swinging to eech eer, and three or foer duzen mor a-cuming; and then u wuud see all th loefers get up and woch th thing out of siet, and laf at th fun and luuk graetful for th noiz. Then thay’d setl bak agen til thair was a daug fiet. Thair couldn’t enything waek them up all oever, and maek them hapy all oever, liek a daug fiet—unles it miet be puuting terpentien on a stray daug and seting fier to him, or tieing a tin pan to his tael and see him run himself to deth.

On th river frunt sum of th houses was stiking out oever th bank, and thay was boed and bent, and about redy to tumbl in. Th peepl had moovd out of them. Th bank was caevd away under wun corner of sum uthers, and that corner was hanging oever. Peepl livd in them yet, but it was dangersome, becauz sumtiems a strip of land as wied as a hous caevs in at a tiem. Sumtiems a belt of land a qorter of a miel deep wil start in and caev along and caev along til it all caevs into th river in wun sumer. Such a toun as that has to be allways mooving bak, and bak, and bak, becauz th river’s allways nawing at it.

Th neerer it got to noon that day th thiker and thiker was th wagons and horses in th streets, and mor cuming all th tiem. Familys fetched thair diners with them frum th cuntry, and eet them in th wagons. Thair was considerabl whisky drinking going on, and I seen three fiets. Bi and bi sumbody sings out:

“Heer cums oeld Boggs!—in frum th cuntry for his litl oeld munthly drunk; heer he cums, boys!”

All th loefers luukt glad; I rekond thay was uezd to having fun out of Boggs. Wun of them sez:

“Wunder hoo he’s a-gwyne to chaw up this tiem. If he’d a-chawed up all th men he’s ben a-gwyne to chaw up in th last twenty yeer he’d hav considerabl ruputation now.”

Anuther wun sez, “I wisht oeld Boggs ’d threten me, ’cuz then I’d noe I worn’t gwyne to die for a thousan’ yeer.”

Boggs cums a-tairing along on his hors, hooping and yeling liek an Injun, and singing out:

“Cler th trak, thar. I’m on th waw-path, and th pries uv coffins is a-gwyne to raez.”











He was drunk, and weeving about in his sadl; he was oever fifty yeer oeld, and had a verry red faes. Evrybody yeld at him and laft at him and sassed him, and he sassed bak, and sed he’d atend to them and lay them out in thair reguelar terns, but he couldn’t waet now becauz he’d cum to toun to kil oeld Curnel Sherburn, and his moto was, “Meet ferst, and spoon vittles to top off on.”

He see me, and roed up and sez:

“Whar’d u cum f’m, boy? U prepaird to die?”

Then he roed on. I was scaird, but a man sez:

“He don’t meen nuthing; he’s allways a-carryin’ on liek that when he’s drunk. He’s th best naturedest oeld fool in Arkansaw—never hert noebody, drunk nor soeber.”

Boggs roed up befor th bigest stor in toun, and bent his hed doun so he cuud see under th curten of th auning and yels:

“Cum out heer, Sherburn! Cum out and meet th man u’ve swindld. U’re th houn’ I’m after, and I’m a-gwyne to hav u, too!”

And so he went on, calling Sherburn evrything he cuud lay his tung to, and th hoel street pakt with peepl lisening and lafing and going on. Bi and bi a proud-luuking man about fifty-fiev—and he was a heep th best drest man in that toun, too—steps out of th stor, and th croud drops bak on eech sied to let him cum. He sez to Boggs, miety ca’m and slo—he sez:

“I’m tierd of this, but I’ll endur it til wun o’clok. Til wun o’clok, miend—no longger. If u oepen yur mouth agenst me oenly wuns after that tiem u can’t travel so far but I wil fiend u.”

Then he terns and goes in. Th croud luukt miety soeber; noebody sterd, and thair worn’t no mor lafing. Boggs roed off blackguarding Sherburn as loud as he cuud yel, all doun th street; and prity soon bak he cums and stops befor th stor, stil keeping it up. Sum men crouded around him and tried to get him to shut up, but he wouldn’t; thay toeld him it wuud be wun o’clok in about fifteen minits, and so he must go hoem—he must go riet away. But it didn’t do no guud. He cussed away with all his miet, and throwed his hat doun in th mud and roed oever it, and prity soon away he went a-raejing doun th street agen, with his gray hair a-flieing. Evrybody that cuud get a chans at him tried thair best to coex him off of his hors so thay cuud lok him up and get him soeber; but it worn’t no ues—up th street he wuud teer agen, and giv Sherburn anuther cussing. Bi and bi sumbody sez:

“Go for his dauter!—qik, go for his dauter; sumtiems he’ll lisen to her. If enybody can perswaed him, she can.”

So sumbody started on a run. I waukt doun street a ways and stopt. In about fiev or ten minits heer cums Boggs agen, but not on his hors. He was a-reeling across th street tords me, bair-heded, with a frend on boeth sieds of him a-holt of his arms and herying him along. He was qieet, and luukt uneezy; and he worn’t hanging bak eny, but was doing sum of th herying himself. Sumbody sings out:

“Boggs!”

I luukt oever thair to see hoo sed it, and it was that Curnel Sherburn. He was standing perfectly stil in th street, and had a pistol raezd in his riet hand—not aeming it, but hoelding it out with th barrel tilted up tords th skie. Th saem second I see a yung gerl cuming on th run, and too men with her. Boggs and th men ternd round to see hoo calld him, and when thay see th pistol th men jumpt to wun sied, and th pistol-barrel cum doun slo and stedy to a level—boeth barrels cokt. Boggs throes up boeth of his hands and sez, “O Lord, don’t shoot!” Bang! goes th ferst shot, and he stagers bak, clawing at th air—bang! goes th second wun, and he tumbls bakwards on to th ground, hevy and solid, with his arms spred out. That yung gerl screemd out and cums rushing, and doun she throes herself on her faather, crieing, and saying, “O, he’s kild him, he’s kild him!” Th croud cloezd up around them, and shoelderd and jamd wun anuther, with thair neks strecht, trieing to see, and peepl on th insied trieing to shuv them bak and shouting, “Bak, bak! giv him air, giv him air!”











Curnel Sherburn he tosst his pistol on to th ground, and ternd around on his heels and waukt off.

Thay tuuk Boggs to a litl drug stor, th croud presing around just th saem, and th hoel toun foloeing, and I rusht and got a guud plaes at th windo, whair I was cloez to him and cuud see in. Thay laed him on th flor and puut wun larj Biebl under his hed, and oepend anuther wun and spred it on his brest; but thay tore oepen his shert ferst, and I seen whair wun of th buulets went in. He maed about a duzen long gasps, his brest lifting th Biebl up when he drawed in his breth, and leting it doun agen when he breethd it out—and after that he laed stil; he was ded. Then thay puuld his dauter away frum him, screeming and crieing, and tuuk her off. She was about sixteen, and verry sweet and jentl luuking, but awful pael and scaird.

Wel, prity soon th hoel toun was thair, sqerming and scrouging and puushing and shuving to get at th windo and hav a luuk, but peepl that had th plaeses wouldn’t giv them up, and foeks behiend them was saying all th tiem, “Say, now, u’ve luukt enuf, u feloes; ’tain’t riet and ’tain’t fair for u to stay thar all th tiem, and never giv noebody a chans; uther foeks has thair riets as wel as u.”

Thair was considerabl jawing bak, so I slid out, thinking maybe thair was going to be trubl. Th streets was fuul, and evrybody was exsieted. Evrybody that seen th shooting was teling how it hapend, and thair was a big croud pakt around eech wun of thees feloes, streching thair neks and lisening. Wun long, lanky man, with long hair and a big whiet fer stoevpiep hat on th bak of his hed, and a cruuked-handld caen, markt out th plaeses on th ground whair Boggs stuud and whair Sherburn stuud, and th peepl foloeing him around frum wun plaes to t’uther and woching evrything he dun, and bobing thair heds to sho thay understuud, and stooping a litl and resting thair hands on thair thies to woch him mark th plaeses on th ground with his caen; and then he stuud up straet and stif whair Sherburn had stuud, frouning and having his hat-brim doun oever his ies, and sung out, “Boggs!” and then fetched his caen doun slo to a level, and sez “Bang!” stagerd bakwards, sez “Bang!” agen, and fel doun flat on his bak. Th peepl that had seen th thing sed he dun it perfect; sed it was just exactly th way it all hapend. Then as much as a duzen peepl got out thair botls and treeted him.

Wel, bi and bi sumbody sed Sherburn aut to be lincht. In about a minit evrybody was saying it; so away thay went, mad and yeling, and snaching doun evry cloeths-lien thay cum to to do th hanging with.














CHAPTER XXII.

Thay swormd up tords Sherburn’s hous, a-hooping and raejing liek Injuns, and evrything had to cleer th way or get run oever and tromped to mush, and it was awful to see. Children was heeling it ahed of th mob, screeming and trieing to get out of th way; and evry windo along th roed was fuul of wimen’s heds, and thair was nigger boys in evry tree, and buks and wenches luuking oever evry fens; and as soon as th mob wuud get neerly to them thay wuud braek and skaddle bak out of reech. Lots of th wimen and gerls was crieing and taeking on, scaird moest to deth.

Thay swormd up in frunt of Sherburn’s palings as thik as thay cuud jam together, and u couldn’t heer yurself think for th noiz. It was a litl twenty-fuut yard. Sum sung out “Teer doun th fens! teer doun th fens!” Then thair was a raket of riping and tairing and smashing, and doun she goes, and th frunt wall of th croud begins to roel in liek a waev.

Just then Sherburn steps out on to th roof of his litl frunt porch, with a dubl-barrel gun in his hand, and taeks his stand, perfectly ca’m and deliberaet, not saying a werd. Th raket stopt, and th waev sukt bak.

Sherburn never sed a werd—just stuud thair, luuking doun. Th stilnes was awful creepy and uncumfortabl. Sherburn run his ie slo along th croud; and whairever it struk th peepl tried a litl to out-gaez him, but thay couldn’t; thay dropt thair ies and luukt sneeky. Then prity soon Sherburn sort of laft; not th plezant kiend, but th kiend that maeks u feel liek when u ar eeting bred that’s got sand in it.

Then he sez, slo and scornful:

“Th iedeea of u lynching enybody! It’s amuezing. Th iedeea of u thinking u had pluk enuf to linch a man! Becauz u’re braev enuf to tar and fether pur frendles cast-out wimen that cum along heer, did that maek u think u had grit enuf to lay yur hands on a man? Whi, a man’s saef in th hands of ten thouzand of yur kiend—as long as it’s daytiem and u’re not behiend him.

“Do I noe u? I noe u cleer thru. I was born and raezd in th South, and I’ve livd in th North; so I noe th averej all around. Th averej man’s a coward. In th North he lets enybody wauk oever him that wonts to, and goes hoem and prays for a humbl spirit to bair it. In th South wun man all bi himself, has stopt a staej fuul of men in th daytiem, and robd th lot. Yur nuespaepers call u a braev peepl so much that u think u ar braever than eny uther peepl—whairas u’re just as braev, and no braever. Whi don’t yur jurys hang merderers? Becauz thay’re afraed th man’s frends wil shoot them in th bak, in th dark—and it’s just whut thay wuud do.

“So thay allways aqit; and then a man goes in th niet, with a hundred maskt cowards at his bak and lynches th rascal. Yur mistaek is, that u didn’t bring a man with u; that’s wun mistaek, and th uther is that u didn’t cum in th dark and fech yur masks. U braut part of a man—Buk Harkness, thair—and if u hadn’t had him to start u, u’d a taeken it out in bloeing.

“U didn’t wont to cum. Th averej man don’t liek trubl and daenjer. U don’t liek trubl and daenjer. But if oenly haf a man—liek Buk Harkness, thair—shouts ’Linch him! linch him!’ u’re afraed to bak doun—afraed u’ll be found out to be whut u ar—cowards—and so u raez a yel, and hang yurselvs on to that haf-a-man’s coet-tael, and cum raejing up heer, swairing whut big things u’re going to do. Th pitifulest thing out is a mob; that’s whut an army is—a mob; thay don’t fiet with curej that’s born in them, but with curej that’s borroed frum thair mas, and frum thair offisers. But a mob without eny man at th hed of it is beneeth pitifulness. Now th thing for u to do is to droop yur taels and go hoem and crall in a hoel. If eny reeal lynching’s going to be dun it wil be dun in th dark, Suthern fashun; and when thay cum thay’ll bring thair masks, and fech a man along. Now leev—and taek yur haf-a-man with u”—tossing his gun up across his left arm and cocking it when he sez this.

Th croud wosht bak suden, and then broek all apart, and went tairing off evry which way, and Buk Harkness he heeled it after them, luuking tolerabl cheep. I cuud a stayd if I wonted to, but I didn’t wont to.

I went to th sercus and loeft around th bak sied til th wochman went bi, and then dievd in under th tent. I had mi twenty-dolar goeld pees and sum uther muny, but I rekond I beter saev it, becauz thair ain’t no teling how soon u ar going to need it, away frum hoem and amungst straenjers that way. U can’t be too cairful. I ain’t opoezd to spending muny on circuses when thair ain’t no uther way, but thair ain’t no ues in waesting it on them.











It was a reeal buuly sercus. It was th splendidest siet that ever was when thay all cum rieding in, too and too, a jentlman and laedy, sied bi sied, th men just in thair drors and undersherts, and no shoos nor stirrups, and resting thair hands on thair thies eezy and cumfortabl—thair must a bin twenty of them—and evry laedy with a luvly complexshun, and perfectly buetiful, and luuking just liek a gang of reeal shur-enuf qeens, and drest in cloeths that cost milyons of dolars, and just literd with diemonds. It was a powerful fien siet; I never see enything so luvly. And then wun bi wun thay got up and stuud, and went a-weeving around th ring so jentl and waevy and graesful, th men luuking ever so tall and airy and straet, with thair heds bobing and skiming along, away up thair under th tent-roof, and evry laedy’s roez-leefy dres flaping sofft and silky around her hips, and she luuking liek th moest luvlyest parrasol.

And then faster and faster thay went, all of them dansing, ferst wun fuut out in th air and then th uther, th horses leening mor and mor, and th ringmaster going round and round th senter-poel, craking his whip and shouting “Hi!—hi!” and th cloun craking joeks behiend him; and bi and bi all hands dropt th raens, and evry laedy puut her nukls on her hips and evry jentlman foelded his arms, and then how th horses did leen oever and hump themselvs! And so wun after th uther thay all skipt off into th ring, and maed th sweetest bo I ever see, and then scamperd out, and evrybody clapt thair hands and went just about wield.

Wel, all thru th sercus thay dun th moest astonishing things; and all th tiem that cloun carryd on so it moest kild th peepl. Th ringmaster couldn’t ever say a werd to him but he was bak at him qik as a wink with th funyest things a body ever sed; and how he ever cuud think of so meny of them, and so suden and so pat, was whut I couldn’t noeway understand. Whi, I couldn’t a thaut of them in a yeer. And bi and bi a drunk man tried to get into th ring—sed he wonted to ried; sed he cuud ried as wel as enybody that ever was. Thay argued and tried to keep him out, but he wouldn’t lisen, and th hoel sho cum to a standstil. Then th peepl begun to holler at him and maek fun of him, and that maed him mad, and he begun to rip and teer; so that sterd up th peepl, and a lot of men begun to piel doun off of th benches and sworm tords th ring, saying, “Nok him doun! thro him out!” and wun or too wimen begun to screem. So, then, th ringmaster he maed a litl speech, and sed he hoept thair wouldn’t be no disterbans, and if th man wuud promis he wouldn’t maek no mor trubl he wuud let him ried if he thaut he cuud stay on th hors. So evrybody laft and sed all riet, and th man got on. Th minit he was on, th hors begun to rip and teer and jump and cavort around, with too sercus men hanging on to his briedl trieing to hoeld him, and th drunk man hanging on to his nek, and his heels flieing in th air evry jump, and th hoel croud of peepl standing up shouting and lafing til teers roeld doun. And at last, shur enuf, all th sercus men cuud do, th hors broek loos, and away he went liek th verry naeshun, round and round th ring, with that sot laying doun on him and hanging to his nek, with ferst wun leg hanging moest to th ground on wun sied, and then t’uther wun on t’uther sied, and th peepl just craezy. It worn’t funy to me, tho; I was all of a trembl to see his daenjer. But prity soon he strugld up astraddle and grabd th briedl, a-reeling this way and that; and th next minit he sprung up and dropt th briedl and stuud! and th hors a-going liek a hous afier too. He just stuud up thair, a-saeling around as eezy and cumfortabl as if he worn’t ever drunk in his lief—and then he begun to puul off his cloeths and sling them. He shed them so thik thay kiend of clogd up th air, and alltogether he shed seventeen soots. And, then, thair he was, slim and hansum, and drest th gaudiest and prityest u ever saw, and he lit into that hors with his whip and maed him fairly hum—and fienaly skipt off, and maed his bo and danst off to th dresing-room, and evrybody just a-houling with plezher and astonishment.











Then th ringmaster he see how he had bin foold, and he was th sickest ringmaster u ever see, I rekon. Whi, it was wun of his oen men! He had got up that joek all out of his oen hed, and never let on to noebody. Wel, I felt sheepish enuf to be tuuk in so, but I wouldn’t a bin in that ringmaster’s plaes, not for a thouzand dolars. I don’t noe; thair may be bullier circuses than whut that wun was, but I never struk them yet. Enyways, it was plenty guud enuf for me; and whairever I run across it, it can hav all of mi custom evry tiem.

Wel, that niet we had our sho; but thair worn’t oenly about twelv peepl thair—just enuf to pay expenses. And thay laft all th tiem, and that maed th duek mad; and evrybody left, enyway, befor th sho was oever, but wun boy which was asleep. So th duek sed thees Arkansaw lunkheads couldn’t cum up to Shakespeare; whut thay wonted was lo comedy—and maybe sumthing ruther wers than lo comedy, he rekond. He sed he cuud siez thair stiel. So next morning he got sum big sheets of raping paeper and sum blak paent, and drawed off sum handbills, and stuk them up all oever th vilej. Th bils sed:
















CHAPTER XXIII.

Wel, all day him and th king was hard at it, riging up a staej and a curten and a ro of candls for fuutliets; and that niet th hous was jam fuul of men in no tiem. When th plaes couldn’t hoeld no mor, th duek he qit tending dor and went around th bak way and cum on to th staej and stuud up befor th curten and maed a litl speech, and praezd up this trajedy, and sed it was th moest thrillingest wun that ever was; and so he went on a-braging about th trajedy, and about Edmund Kean th Elder, which was to play th maen prinsipal part in it; and at last when he’d got evrybody’s expectaeshuns up hi enuf, he roeld up th curten, and th next minit th king cum a-pransing out on all foers, naeked; and he was paented all oever, ring-streekt-and-striept, all sorts of culors, as splendid as a raenbo. And—but never miend th rest of his outfit; it was just wield, but it was awful funy. Th peepl moest kild themselvs lafing; and when th king got dun caepering and capered off behiend th seens, thay rord and clapt and stormd and haw-hawed til he cum bak and dun it oever agen, and after that thay maed him do it anuther tiem. Wel, it wuud maek a cow laf to see th shiens that oeld idiot cut.

Then th duek he lets th curten doun, and boes to th peepl, and sez th graet trajedy wil be performd oenly too niets mor, on acounts of presing London engaejments, whair th seets is all soeld allredy for it in Drury Laen; and then he maeks them anuther bo, and sez if he has sucseeded in pleezing them and instructing them, he wil be deeply obleeged if thay wil menshun it to thair frends and get them to cum and see it.

Twenty peepl sings out:

“Whut, is it oever? Is that all?”

Th duek sez yes. Then thair was a fien tiem. Evrybody sings out, “Soeld!” and roez up mad, and was a-going for that staej and them trajeedians. But a big, fien luuking man jumps up on a bench and shouts:

“Hoeld on! Just a werd, jentlmen.” Thay stopt to lisen. “We ar soeld—miety badly soeld. But we don’t wont to be th lafing stok of this hoel toun, I rekon, and never heer th last of this thing as long as we liv. No. Whut we wont is to go out of heer qieet, and tauk this sho up, and sel th rest of th toun! Then we’ll all be in th saem boet. Ain’t that sensibl?” (“U bet it is!—th jedge is riet!” evrybody sings out.) “All riet, then—not a werd about eny sel. Go along hoem, and adviez evrybody to cum and see th trajedy.”

Next day u couldn’t heer nuthing around that toun but how splendid that sho was. Hous was jamd agen that niet, and we soeld this croud th saem way. When me and th king and th duek got hoem to th raft we all had a super; and bi and bi, about midniet, thay maed Jim and me bak her out and floet her doun th midl of th river, and fech her in and hied her about too miel belo toun.

Th therd niet th hous was cramd agen—and thay worn’t nue-comers this tiem, but peepl that was at th sho th uther too niets. I stuud bi th duek at th dor, and I see that evry man that went in had his pokets buljing, or sumthing mufld up under his coet—and I see it worn’t no perfuemery, neether, not bi a long siet. I smelt sikly egs bi th barrel, and roten cabbages, and such things; and if I noe th siens of a ded cat being around, and I bet I do, thair was sixty-foer of them went in. I shuvd in thair for a minit, but it was too vairius for me; I couldn’t stand it. Wel, when th plaes couldn’t hoeld no mor peepl th duek he giv a felo a qorter and toeld him to tend dor for him a minit, and then he started around for th staej dor, I after him; but th minit we ternd th corner and was in th dark he sez:

“Wauk fast now til u get away frum th houses, and then shin for th raft liek th dickens was after u!”

I dun it, and he dun th saem. We struk th raft at th saem tiem, and in les than too seconds we was gliding doun streem, all dark and stil, and ejing tords th midl of th river, noebody saying a werd. I rekond th pur king was in for a gaudy tiem of it with th audyens, but nuthing of th sort; prity soon he cralls out frum under th wigwom, and sez:

“Wel, how’d th oeld thing pan out this tiem, duek?” He hadn’t bin up-toun at all.

We never shoed a liet til we was about ten miel belo th vilej. Then we lit up and had a super, and th king and th duek fairly laft thair boens loos oever th way thay’d servd them peepl. Th duek sez:

“Greenhorns, flatheads! I nue th ferst hous wuud keep mum and let th rest of th toun get roept in; and I nue thay’d lay for us th therd niet, and consider it was thair tern now. Wel, it is thair tern, and I’d giv sumthing to noe how much thay’d taek for it. I wuud just liek to noe how thay’re puuting in thair oportuenity. Thay can tern it into a picnik if thay wont to—thay braut plenty provizhuns.”

Them rapscallions tuuk in foer hundred and sixty-fiev dolars in that three niets. I never see muny halld in bi th wagon-loed liek that befor. Bi and bi, when thay was asleep and snoring, Jim sez:











“Don’t it s’prise u de way dem kings carrys on, Huck?”

“No,” I sez, “it don’t.”

“Whi don’t it, Huck?”

“Wel, it don’t, becauz it’s in th breed. I rekon thay’re all aliek.”

“But, Huck, dese kings o’ ourn is reglar rapscallions; dat’s jist whut day is; day’s reglar rapscallions.”

“Wel, that’s whut I’m a-saying; all kings is moestly rapscallions, as fer as I can maek out.”

“Is dat so?”

“U red about them wuns—u’ll see. Luuk at Henry th Aet; this ’n ’s a Sunday-scool Superintendent to him. And luuk at Charles Second, and Louis Forteen, and Louis Fifteen, and James Second, and Edward Second, and Richard Therd, and forty mor; besieds all them Saxon heptarchies that uezd to rip around so in oeld tiems and raez Cain. Mi, u aut to seen oeld Henry th Aet when he was in bloom. He was a blosom. He uezd to marry a nue wief evry day, and chop off her hed next morning. And he wuud do it just as indiferent as if he was ordering up egs. ‘Fech up Nell Gwynn,’ he sez. Thay fech her up. Next morning, ‘Chop off her hed!’ And thay chop it off. ‘Fech up Jane Shor,’ he sez; and up she cums, Next morning, ‘Chop off her hed’—and thay chop it off. ‘Ring up Fair Rosamun.’ Fair Rosamun ansers th bel. Next morning, ‘Chop off her hed.’ And he maed evry wun of them tel him a tael evry niet; and he kept that up til he had hogged a thouzand and wun taels that way, and then he puut them all in a buuk, and calld it Domesday Buuk—which was a guud naem and staeted th caes. U don’t noe kings, Jim, but I noe them; and this oeld rip of ourn is wun of th cleanest I’ve struk in history. Wel, Henry he taeks a noeshun he wonts to get up sum trubl with this cuntry. How duz he go at it—giv noetis?—giv th cuntry a sho? No. All of a suden he heevs all th tee in Boston Harbor oeverbord, and whacks out a declaraeshun of independens, and dairs them to cum on. That was his stiel—he never giv enybody a chans. He had suspishuns of his faather, th Duek of Wellington. Wel, whut did he do? Ask him to sho up? No—drownded him in a but of mamsey, liek a cat. S’poez peepl left muny laying around whair he was—whut did he do? He colard it. S’poez he contracted to do a thing, and u paed him, and didn’t set doun thair and see that he dun it—whut did he do? He allways dun th uther thing. S’poez he oepend his mouth—whut then? If he didn’t shut it up powerful qik he’d looz a lie evry tiem. That’s th kiend of a bug Henry was; and if we’d a had him along ’sted of our kings he’d a foold that toun a heep wers than ourn dun. I don’t say that ourn is lams, becauz thay ain’t, when u cum riet doun to th coeld facts; but thay ain’t nuthing to that oeld ram, enyway. All I say is, kings is kings, and u got to maek alowanses. Taek them all around, thay’re a miety ornery lot. It’s th way thay’re raezd.”











“But dis wun do smel so liek de naeshun, Huck.”

“Wel, thay all do, Jim. We can’t help th way a king smels; history don’t tel no way.”

“Now de duek, he’s a tolerble liekly man in sum ways.”

“Yes, a duek’s diferent. But not verry diferent. This wun’s a midling hard lot for a duek. When he’s drunk thair ain’t no neer-sieted man cuud tel him frum a king.”

“Wel, enyways, I doan’ hanker for no mo’ un um, Huck. Dese is all I kin stan’.”

“It’s th way I feel, too, Jim. But we’ve got them on our hands, and we got to remember whut thay ar, and maek alowanses. Sumtiems I wish we cuud heer of a cuntry that’s out of kings.”

Whut was th ues to tel Jim thees worn’t reeal kings and dueks? It wouldn’t a dun no guud; and, besieds, it was just as I sed: u couldn’t tel them frum th reeal kiend.

I went to sleep, and Jim didn’t call me when it was mi tern. He offen dun that. When I waekt up just at daybraek he was siting thair with his hed doun betwixt his nees, moaning and morning to himself. I didn’t taek noetis nor let on. I knowed whut it was about. He was thinking about his wief and his children, away up yonder, and he was lo and hoemsik; becauz he hadn’t ever bin away frum hoem befor in his lief; and I do beleev he caird just as much for his peepl as whiet foeks duz for thair’n. It don’t seem nacheral, but I rekon it’s so. He was offen moaning and morning that way niets, when he jujd I was asleep, and saying, “Po’ litl ’Lizabeth! po’ litl Johnny! it’s miety hard; I spec’ I ain’t ever gwyne to see u no mo’, no mo’!” He was a miety guud nigger, Jim was.

But this tiem I sumhow got to tauking to him about his wief and yung wuns; and bi and bi he sez:

“Whut maeks me feel so bad dis tiem ’uz bekase I heer sumpn oever yonder on de bank liek a whak, er a slam, whiel ago, en it mien me er de tiem I treet mi litl ’Lizabeth so ornery. She worn’t on’y ’bout fo’ yeer oelay, en she tuk de sk’yarlet feever, en had a powful ruf spel; but she got wel, en wun day she was a-stannin’ aroun’, en I sez to her, I sez:

“‘Shet de do’.’

“She never dun it; jis’ stuud dah, kiner smilin’ up at me. It maek me mad; en I sez agin, miety loud, I sez:

“‘Doan’ u heer me? Shet de do’!’

“She jis stuud de saem way, kiner smilin’ up. I was a-bilin’! I sez:

“‘I lay I maek u mien!’

“En wid dat I fech’ her a slap sied de hed dat sont her a-sprawlin’. Den I went into de yuther room, en ’uz gon ’bout ten minits; en when I cum bak dah was dat do’ a-stannin’ oepen yit, en dat chile stannin’ mos’ riet in it, a-lookin’ doun and mournin’, en de teers runnin’ doun. Mi, but I wuz mad! I was a-gwyne for de chile, but jis’ den—it was a do’ dat oepen innerds—jis’ den, ’long cum de wiend en slam it to, behine de chile, ker-BLAM!—en mi lan’, de chile never moov’! Mi breff mos’ hop outer me; en I feel so—so—I doan’ noe HOW I feel. I crope out, all a-tremblin’, en crope aroun’ en oepen de do’ eezy en slo, en poek mi hed in behine de chile, sof’ en stil, en all uv a suden I sez POW! jis’ as loud as I cuud yel. She never buj! O, Huck, I bust out a-cryin’ en grab her up in mi arms, en say, ‘O, de po’ litl thing! De Lord God Amighty fogive po’ oelay Jim, kaze he never gwyne to fogive hisself as long’s he liv!’ O, she was plum deef en dum, Huck, plum deef en dum—en I’d ben a-treet’n her so!”














CHAPTER XXIV.

Next day, tords niet, we laed up under a litl wilo toehed out in th midl, whair thair was a vilej on eech sied of th river, and th duek and th king begun to lay out a plan for werking them touns. Jim he spoek to th duek, and sed he hoept it wouldn’t taek but a fue ours, becauz it got miety hevy and tiersum to him when he had to lay all day in th wigwom tied with th roep. U see, when we left him all aloen we had to tee him, becauz if enybody hapend on to him all bi himself and not tied it wouldn’t luuk much liek he was a runaway nigger, u noe. So th duek sed it was kiend of hard to hav to lay roept all day, and he’d siefer out sum way to get around it.

He was uncomon briet, th duek was, and he soon struk it. He drest Jim up in King Lear’s outfit—it was a long curten-calico goun, and a whiet hors-hair wig and whiskers; and then he tuuk his theeater paent and paented Jim’s faes and hands and eers and nek all oever a ded, dul, solid bloo, liek a man that’s bin drownded nien days. Blaemd if he worn’t th horriblest luuking outraej I ever see. Then th duek tuuk and roet out a sien on a shinggl so:

Sik Arab—but harmles when not out of his hed.

And he naeld that shinggl to a lath, and stuud th lath up foer or fiev fuut in frunt of th wigwom. Jim was satisfied. He sed it was a siet beter than lieing tied a cupl of yeers evry day, and trembling all oever evry tiem thair was a sound. Th duek toeld him to maek himself free and eezy, and if enybody ever cum medling around, he must hop out of th wigwom, and carry on a litl, and fech a houl or too liek a wield beest, and he rekond thay wuud liet out and leev him aloen. Which was sound enuf jujment; but u taek th averej man, and he wouldn’t waet for him to houl. Whi, he didn’t oenly luuk liek he was ded, he luukt considerabl mor than that.

Thees rapscallions wonted to tri th Nonesuch agen, becauz thair was so much muny in it, but thay jujd it wouldn’t be saef, becauz maybe th nues miet a werkt along doun bi this tiem. Thay couldn’t hit no project that sooted exactly; so at last th duek sed he rekond he’d lay off and werk his braens an our or too and see if he couldn’t puut up sumthing on th Arkansaw vilej; and th king he alowd he wuud drop oever to t’uther vilej without eny plan, but just trust in Providens to leed him th profitabl way—meening th devil, I rekon. We had all baut stor cloeths whair we stopt last; and now th king puut his’n on, and he toeld me to puut mien on. I dun it, of cors. Th king’s duds was all blak, and he did luuk reeal swel and starchy. I never knowed how cloeths cuud chaenj a body befor. Whi, befor, he luukt liek th orneriest oeld rip that ever was; but now, when he’d taek off his nue whiet beever and maek a bo and do a smiel, he luukt that grand and guud and pieus that u’d say he had waukt riet out of th ark, and maybe was oeld Leviticus himself. Jim cleend up th canoo, and I got mi padl redy. Thair was a big steemboet laying at th shor away up under th point, about three miel abuv th toun—bin thair a cupl of ours, taeking on fraet. Sez th king:

“Seein’ how I’m drest, I rekon maybe I beter ariev doun frum St. Louis or Cincinnati, or sum uther big plaes. Go for th steemboet, Huklberry; we’ll cum doun to th vilej on her.”

I didn’t hav to be orderd twies to go and taek a steemboet ried. I fetched th shor a haf a miel abuv th vilej, and then went scooting along th bluf bank in th eezy wauter. Prity soon we cum to a nies inosent-luuking yung cuntry jake seting on a log swobing th swet off of his faes, for it was powerful worm wether; and he had a cupl of big carpet-bags bi him.

“Run her noez in shor,” sez th king. I dun it. “Wher’ u bound for, yung man?”

“For th steemboet; going to Orleans.”

“Git abord,” sez th king. “Hoeld on a minit, mi servant ’ll he’p u with them bags. Jump out and he’p th jentlman, Adolphus”—meening me, I see.











I dun so, and then we all three started on agen. Th yung chap was miety thankful; sed it was tuf werk toeting his bagej such wether. He askt th king whair he was going, and th king toeld him he’d cum doun th river and landed at th uther vilej this morning, and now he was going up a fue miel to see an oeld frend on a farm up thair. Th yung felo sez:

“When I ferst see u I sez to mieself, ‘It’s Mr. Wilks, shur, and he cum miety neer geting heer in tiem.’ But then I sez agen, ‘No, I rekon it ain’t him, or els he wouldn’t be padling up th river.’ U ain’t him, ar u?”

“No, mi naem’s Blodgett—Elexander Blodgett—Reverend Elexander Blodgett, I s’poez I must say, as I’m wun o’ th Lord’s pur servants. But stil I’m jist as aebl to be sorry for Mr. Wilks for not arieving in tiem, all th saem, if he’s mist enything bi it—which I hoep he hasn’t.”

“Wel, he don’t mis eny property bi it, becauz he’ll get that all riet; but he’s mist seeing his bruther Peeter die—which he mayn’t miend, noebody can tel as to that—but his bruther wuud a giv enything in this werld to see him befor he died; never taukt about nuthing els all thees three weeks; hadn’t seen him sinss thay was boys together—and hadn’t ever seen his bruther William at all—that’s th deef and dum wun—William ain’t mor than therty or therty-fiev. Peeter and George wer th oenly wuns that cum out heer; George was th marryd bruther; him and his wief boeth died last yeer. Harvey and William’s th oenly wuns that’s left now; and, as I was saying, thay haeven’t got heer in tiem.”

“Did enybody send ’em werd?”

“O, yes; a munth or too ago, when Peeter was ferst tuuk; becauz Peeter sed then that he sorter felt liek he worn’t going to get wel this tiem. U see, he was prity oeld, and George’s g’yirls was too yung to be much cumpany for him, exsept Mary Jane, th red-heded wun; and so he was kiender loensum after George and his wief died, and didn’t seem to cair much to liv. He moest desperetly wonted to see Harvey—and William, too, for that mater—becauz he was wun of them kiend that can’t bair to maek a wil. He left a leter behiend for Harvey, and sed he’d toeld in it whair his muny was hid, and how he wonted th rest of th property divieded up so George’s g’yirls wuud be all riet—for George didn’t leev nuthing. And that leter was all thay cuud get him to puut a pen to.”

“Whi do u rekon Harvey don’t cum? Wher’ duz he liv?”

“O, he lievs in England—Sheffield—preeches thair—hasn’t ever bin in this cuntry. He hasn’t had eny too much tiem—and besieds he mightn’t a got th leter at all, u noe.”

“Too bad, too bad he couldn’t a livd to see his bruthers, pur soel. U going to Orleans, u say?”

“Yes, but that ain’t oenly a part of it. I’m going in a ship, next Wednesday, for Ryo Janeero, whair mi unkl lievs.”

“It’s a prity long jerny. But it’ll be luvly; wisht I was a-going. Is Mary Jane th oeldest? How oeld is th uthers?”

“Mary Jane’s nienteen, Susan’s fifteen, and Joanna’s about forteen—that’s th wun that givs herself to guud werks and has a hair-lip.”

“Pur things! to be left aloen in th coeld werld so.”

“Wel, thay cuud be wers off. Oeld Peeter had frends, and thay ain’t going to let them cum to no harm. Thair’s Hobson, th Babtis’ preecher; and Deecon Lot Hovey, and Ben Rucker, and Abner Shackleford, and Levi Bel, th lawyer; and Dr. Robinson, and thair wievs, and th wido Bartley, and—wel, thair’s a lot of them; but thees ar th wuns that Peeter was thikest with, and uezd to riet about sumtiems, when he roet hoem; so Harvey ’ll noe whair to luuk for frends when he gets heer.”











Wel, th oeld man went on asking qeschuns til he just fairly emptyd that yung felo. Blaemd if he didn’t inqier about evrybody and evrything in that blest toun, and all about th Wilkses; and about Peeter’s biznes—which was a tanner; and about George’s—which was a carpenter; and about Harvey’s—which was a dissentering minister; and so on, and so on. Then he sez:

“Whut did u wont to wauk all th way up to th steemboet for?”

“Becauz she’s a big Orleans boet, and I was afeard she mightn’t stop thair. When thay’re deep thay wun’t stop for a hael. A Cincinnati boet wil, but this is a St. Louis wun.”

“Was Peeter Wilks wel off?”

“O, yes, prity wel off. He had houses and land, and it’s rekond he left three or foer thouzand in cash hid up som’ers.”

“When did u say he died?”

“I didn’t say, but it was last niet.”

“Fueneral to-morro, liekly?”

“Yes, ’bout th midl of th day.”

“Wel, it’s all terribl sad; but we’ve all got to go, wun tiem or anuther. So whut we wont to do is to be prepaird; then we’re all riet.”

“Yes, ser, it’s th best way. Maa uezd to allways say that.”

When we struk th boet she was about dun loeding, and prity soon she got off. Th king never sed nuthing about going abord, so I lost mi ried, after all. When th boet was gon th king maed me padl up anuther miel to a loensum plaes, and then he got ashor and sez:

“Now husl bak, riet off, and fech th duek up heer, and th nue carpet-bags. And if he’s gon oever to t’uther sied, go oever thair and git him. And tel him to git himself up regardles. Shuv along, now.”

I see whut he was up to; but I never sed nuthing, of cors. When I got bak with th duek we hid th canoo, and then thay set doun on a log, and th king toeld him evrything, just liek th yung felo had sed it—evry last werd of it. And all th tiem he was a-doing it he tried to tauk liek an Englishman; and he dun it prity wel, too, for a slouch. I can’t imitaet him, and so I ain’t a-going to tri to; but he reealy dun it prity guud. Then he sez:

“How ar u on th deef and dum, Bilgewater?”

Th duek sed, leev him aloen for that; sed he had playd a deef and dum person on th histronic bords. So then thay waeted for a steemboet.

About th midl of th afternoon a cupl of litl boets cum along, but thay didn’t cum frum hi enuf up th river; but at last thair was a big wun, and thay haeld her. She sent out her yall, and we went abord, and she was frum Cincinnati; and when thay found we oenly wonted to go foer or fiev miel thay was booming mad, and gaev us a cussing, and sed thay wouldn’t land us. But th king was ca’m. He sez:

“If jentlmen kin aford to pay a dolar a miel apees to be tuuk on and puut off in a yall, a steemboet kin aford to carry ’em, can’t it?”

So thay soffend doun and sed it was all riet; and when we got to th vilej thay yawled us ashor. About too duzen men flokt doun when thay see th yall a-cuming, and when th king sez:

“Kin eny of u jentlmen tel me wher’ Mr. Peeter Wilks lievs?” thay giv a glans at wun anuther, and noded thair heds, as much as to say, “Whut d’ I tel u?” Then wun of them sez, kiend of sofft and jentl:

“I’m sorry ser, but th best we can do is to tel u whair he did liv yesterday eevning.”

Suden as winking th ornery oeld cretur went an to smash, and fel up agenst th man, and puut his chin on his shoelder, and cried doun his bak, and sez:

“Alas, alas, our pur bruther—gon, and we never got to see him; o, it’s too, too hard!”











Then he terns around, blubbering, and maeks a lot of idiotic siens to th duek on his hands, and blaemd if he didn’t drop a carpet-bag and bust out a-crieing. If thay worn’t th beatenest lot, them too frauds, that ever I struk.

Wel, th men gatherd around and simpathiezd with them, and sed all sorts of kiend things to them, and carryd thair carpet-bags up th hil for them, and let them leen on them and cri, and toeld th king all about his bruther’s last moements, and th king he toeld it all oever agen on his hands to th duek, and boeth of them tuuk on about that ded tanner liek thay’d lost th twelv disiepls. Wel, if ever I struk enything liek it, I’m a nigger. It was enuf to maek a body ashaemd of th hueman raes.














CHAPTER XXV.

Th nues was all oever toun in too minits, and u cuud see th peepl tairing doun on th run frum evry which way, sum of them puuting on thair coets as thay cum. Prity soon we was in th midl of a croud, and th noiz of th tramping was liek a soeljer march. Th windoes and dooryards was fuul; and evry minit sumbody wuud say, oever a fens:

“Is it them?”

And sumbody troting along with th gang wuud anser bak and say:

“U bet it is.”

When we got to th hous th street in frunt of it was pakt, and th three gerls was standing in th dor. Mary Jane was red-heded, but that don’t maek no diferens, she was moest awful buetiful, and her faes and her ies was all lit up liek glory, she was so glad her unkls was cum. Th king he spred his arms, and Mary Jane she jumpt for them, and th hair-lip jumpt for th duek, and thair thay had it! Evrybody moest, leastways wimen, cried for joy to see them meet agen at last and hav such guud tiems.

Then th king he huncht th duek prievet—I see him do it—and then he luukt around and see th coffin, oever in th corner on too chairs; so then him and th duek, with a hand across eech uther’s shoelder, and t’uther hand to thair ies, waukt slo and solem oever thair, evrybody droping bak to giv them room, and all th tauk and noiz stoping, peepl saying “Sh!” and all th men taeking thair hats off and drooping thair heds, so u cuud a herd a pin fall. And when thay got thair thay bent oever and luukt in th coffin, and tuuk wun siet, and then thay bust out a-crieing so u cuud a herd them to Orleans, moest; and then thay puut thair arms around eech uther’s neks, and hung thair chins oever eech uther’s shoelders; and then for three minits, or maybe foer, I never see too men leek th way thay dun. And, miend u, evrybody was doing th saem; and th plaes was that damp I never see enything liek it. Then wun of them got on wun sied of th coffin, and t’uther on t’uther sied, and thay neeld doun and rested thair forheds on th coffin, and let on to pray all to themselvs. Wel, when it cum to that it werkt th croud liek u never see enything liek it, and evrybody broek doun and went to sobing riet out loud—th pur gerls, too; and evry wuuman, neerly, went up to th gerls, without saying a werd, and kist them, solem, on th forhed, and then puut thair hand on thair hed, and luukt up tords th skie, with th teers runing doun, and then busted out and went off sobing and swobing, and giv th next wuuman a sho. I never see enything so disgusting.











Wel, bi and bi th king he gets up and cums forward a litl, and werks himself up and slobbers out a speech, all fuul of teers and flapdoodle about its being a sor trieal for him and his pur bruther to looz th dizeezd, and to mis seeing dizeezd aliev after th long jerny of foer thouzand miel, but it’s a trieal that’s sweetened and sanktified to us bi this deer simpathy and thees hoely teers, and so he thanks them out of his hart and out of his bruther’s hart, becauz out of thair mouths thay can’t, werds being too weak and coeld, and all that kiend of rot and slush, til it was just sikening; and then he blubbers out a pieus guudy-guudy Aamen, and terns himself loos and goes to crieing fit to bust.

And th minit th werds wer out of his mouth sumbody oever in th croud struk up th doxolojer, and evrybody joind in with all thair miet, and it just wormd u up and maed u feel as guud as cherch leting out. Muezic is a guud thing; and after all that soel-buter and hogwosh I never see it freshen up things so, and sound so onest and buuly.

Then th king begins to werk his jaw agen, and sez how him and his neeses wuud be glad if a fue of th maen prinsipal frends of th family wuud taek super heer with them this eevning, and help set up with th ashes of th dizeezd; and sez if his pur bruther laying yonder cuud speek he noes hoo he wuud naem, for thay was naems that was verry deer to him, and menshund offen in his leters; and so he wil naem th saem, to wit, as foloes, vizz.:—Rev. Mr. Hobson, and Deecon Lot Hovey, and Mr. Ben Rucker, and Abner Shackleford, and Levi Bel, and Dr. Robinson, and thair wievs, and th wido Bartley.

Rev. Hobson and Dr. Robinson was doun to th end of th toun a-hunting together—that is, I meen th doctor was shiping a sik man to t’uther werld, and th preecher was pinting him riet. Lawyer Bel was away up to Louisville on biznes. But th rest was on hand, and so thay all cum and shuuk hands with th king and thankt him and taukt to him; and then thay shuuk hands with th duek and didn’t say nuthing, but just kept a-smieling and bobing thair heds liek a passel of sapheads whilst he maed all sorts of siens with his hands and sed “Goo-goo—goo-goo-goo” all th tiem, liek a baeby that can’t tauk.

So th king he blattered along, and manejd to inqier about prity much evrybody and daug in toun, bi his naem, and menshund all sorts of litl things that hapend wun tiem or anuther in th toun, or to George’s family, or to Peeter. And he allways let on that Peeter roet him th things; but that was a lie: he got evry blest wun of them out of that yung flat-hed that we canoed up to th steemboet.

Then Mary Jane she fetched th leter her faather left behiend, and th king he red it out loud and cried oever it. It giv th dweling-hous and three thouzand dolars, goeld, to th gerls; and it giv th tanyard (which was doing a guud biznes), along with sum uther houses and land (werth about seven thouzand), and three thouzand dolars in goeld to Harvey and William, and toeld whair th six thouzand cash was hid doun selar. So thees too frauds sed thay’d go and fech it up, and hav evrything sqair and abuv-bord; and toeld me to cum with a candl. We shut th selar dor behiend us, and when thay found th bag thay spilt it out on th flor, and it was a luvly siet, all them yaller-boys. Mi, th way th king’s ies did shien! He slaps th duek on th shoelder and sez:

“O, this ain’t buuly nor noth’n! O, no, I rekon not! Whi, buuly, it beets th Nonesuch, don’t it?”

Th duek alowd it did. Thay pawed th yaller-boys, and sifted them thru thair finggers and let them jinggl doun on th flor; and th king sez:

“It ain’t no ues talkin’; bein’ bruthers to a rich ded man and representatives of furrin errs that’s got left is th lien for u and me, Bilj. Thish yer cums of trust’n to Providens. It’s th best way, in th long run. I’ve tried ’em all, and ther’ ain’t no beter way.”

Moest evrybody wuud a bin satisfied with th piel, and tuuk it on trust; but no, thay must count it. So thay counts it, and it cums out foer hundred and fifteen dolars short. Sez th king:

“Dern him, I wunder whut he dun with that foer hundred and fifteen dolars?”

Thay weryd oever that awhiel, and ransakt all around for it. Then th duek sez:

“Wel, he was a prity sik man, and liekly he maed a mistaek—I rekon that’s th way of it. Th best way’s to let it go, and keep stil about it. We can spair it.”

“O, shuks, yes, we can spair it. I don’t k’yer noth’n ’bout that—it’s th count I’m thinkin’ about. We wont to be awful sqair and oepen and abuv-bord heer, u noe. We wont to lug this h-yer muny up stairs and count it befor evrybody—then ther’ ain’t noth’n suspishus. But when th ded man sez ther’s six thous’n dolars, u noe, we don’t wont to—”

“Hoeld on,” sez th duek. “Le’s maek up th deffisit,” and he begun to hall out yaller-boys out of his poket.











“It’s a moest amaz’n’ guud iedeea, duek—u hav got a rattlin’ clever hed on u,” sez th king. “Blest if th oeld Nonesuch ain’t a heppin’ us out agin,” and he begun to hall out yaller-jakets and stak them up.

It moest busted them, but thay maed up th six thouzand cleen and cleer.

“Say,” sez th duek, “I got anuther iedeea. Le’s go up stairs and count this muny, and then taek and giv it to th gerls.”

“Guud land, duek, lemme hug u! It’s th moest dazling iedeea ’at ever a man struk. U hav cert’nly got th moest astonishin’ hed I ever see. O, this is th boss doj, ther’ ain’t no mistaek ’bout it. Let ’em fech along thair suspishuns now if thay wont to—this ’ll lay ’em out.”

When we got up-stairs evrybody gethered around th taebl, and th king he counted it and stakt it up, three hundred dolars in a piel—twenty elegant litl piels. Evrybody luukt hunggry at it, and likt thair chops. Then thay raekt it into th bag agen, and I see th king begin to swel himself up for anuther speech. He sez:

“Frends all, mi pur bruther that lays yonder has dun jenerus bi them that’s left behiend in th vael of sorrers. He has dun jenerus bi thees yer pur litl lams that he luvd and shelterd, and that’s left faatherles and mutherles. Yes, and we that knowed him noes that he wuud a dun mor jenerus bi ’em if he hadn’t ben afeard o’ woundin’ his deer William and me. Now, wouldn’t he? Ther’ ain’t no qeschun ’bout it in mi miend. Wel, then, whut kiend o’ bruthers wuud it be that ’d stand in his way at sech a tiem? And whut kiend o’ unkls wuud it be that ’d rob—yes, rob—sech pur sweet lams as thees ’at he luvd so at sech a tiem? If I noe William—and I think I do—he—wel, I’ll jest ask him.” He terns around and begins to maek a lot of siens to th duek with his hands, and th duek he luuks at him stoopid and lether-heded a whiel; then all of a suden he seems to cach his meening, and jumps for th king, goo-gooing with all his miet for joy, and hugs him about fifteen tiems befor he lets up. Then th king sez, “I knowed it; I rekon that ’ll convins enybody th way he feels about it. Heer, Mary Jane, Susan, Joanner, taek th muny—taek it all. It’s th gift of him that lays yonder, coeld but joyful.”











Mary Jane she went for him, Susan and th hair-lip went for th duek, and then such anuther huging and kising I never see yet. And evrybody crouded up with th teers in thair ies, and moest shuuk th hands off of them frauds, saying all th tiem:

“U deer guud soels!—how luvly!—how cuud u!”

Wel, then, prity soon all hands got to tauking about th dizeezd agen, and how guud he was, and whut a loss he was, and all that; and befor long a big ieern-jawed man werkt himself in thair frum outsied, and stuud a-lisening and luuking, and not saying enything; and noebody saying enything to him eether, becauz th king was tauking and thay was all bizy lisening. Th king was saying—in th midl of sumthing he’d started in on—

“—thay bein’ partickler frends o’ th dizeezd. That’s whi thay’re invieted heer this evenin’; but tomorro we wont all to cum—evrybody; for he respected evrybody, he liekt evrybody, and so it’s fitten that his fueneral orjys sh’d be public.”

And so he went a-mooning on and on, lieking to heer himself tauk, and evry litl whiel he fetched in his fueneral orjys agen, til th duek he couldn’t stand it no mor; so he riets on a litl scrap of paeper, “Obseqys, u oeld fool,” and foelds it up, and goes to goo-gooing and reeching it oever peepl’s heds to him. Th king he reeds it and puuts it in his poket, and sez:

“Pur William, aflicted as he is, his hart’s aluz riet. Asks me to inviet evrybody to cum to th fueneral—wonts me to maek ’em all welcum. But he needn’t a weryd—it was jest whut I was at.”

Then he weevs along agen, perfectly ca’m, and goes to droping in his fueneral orjys agen evry now and then, just liek he dun befor. And when he dun it th therd tiem he sez:

“I say orjys, not becauz it’s th comon term, becauz it ain’t—obseqys bein’ th comon term—but becauz orjys is th riet term. Obseqys ain’t uezd in England no mor now—it’s gon out. We say orjys now in England. Orjys is beter, becauz it meens th thing u’re after mor exact. It’s a werd that’s maed up out’n th Greek orgo, outsied, oepen, abraud; and th Hebrew jeesum, to plant, cuver up; hens inter. So, u see, fueneral orjys is an oepen er public fueneral.”

He was th werst I ever struk. Wel, th ieern-jawed man he laft riet in his faes. Evrybody was shokt. Evrybody sez, “Whi, doctor!” and Abner Shackleford sez:

“Whi, Robinson, hain’t u herd th nues? This is Harvey Wilks.”

Th king he smield eeger, and shuvd out his flaper, and sez:

“Is it mi pur bruther’s deer guud frend and fizishan? I—”

“Keep yur hands off of me!” sez th doctor. “U tauk liek an Englishman, don’t u? It’s th werst imitaeshun I ever herd. U Peeter Wilks’s bruther! U’re a fraud, that’s whut u ar!”











Wel, how thay all tuuk on! Thay crouded around th doctor and tried to qieet him doun, and tried to explaen to him and tel him how Harvey ’d shoed in forty ways that he was Harvey, and knowed evrybody bi naem, and th naems of th verry daugs, and begd and begd him not to hert Harvey’s feelings and th pur gerl’s feelings, and all that. But it worn’t no ues; he stormd riet along, and sed eny man that pretended to be an Englishman and couldn’t imitaet th linggo no beter than whut he did was a fraud and a lieer. Th pur gerls was hanging to th king and crieing; and all of a suden th doctor ups and terns on them. He sez:

“I was yur faather’s frend, and I’m yur frend; and I worn u as a frend, and an onest wun that wonts to protect u and keep u out of harm and trubl, to tern yur baks on that scoundrel and hav nuthing to do with him, th ignorant tramp, with his idiotic Greek and Hebrew, as he calls it. He is th thinnest kiend of an impostor—has cum heer with a lot of empty naems and facts which he pikt up somewheres, and u taek them for proofs, and ar helpt to fool yurselvs bi thees foolish frends heer, hoo aut to noe beter. Mary Jane Wilks, u noe me for yur frend, and for yur unselfish frend, too. Now lisen to me; tern this pityful rascal out—I beg u to do it. Wil u?”

Mary Jane straetend herself up, and mi, but she was hansum! She sez:

“Heer is mi anser.” She hoev up th bag of muny and puut it in th king’s hands, and sez, “Taek this six thouzand dolars, and invest for me and mi sisters eny way u wont to, and don’t giv us no reseet for it.”

Then she puut her arm around th king on wun sied, and Susan and th hair-lip dun th saem on th uther. Evrybody clapt thair hands and stompt on th flor liek a perfect storm, whilst th king held up his hed and smield proud. Th doctor sez:

“All riet; I wosh mi hands of th mater. But I worn u all that a tiem ’s cuming when u’re going to feel sik whenever u think of this day.” And away he went.

“All riet, doctor,” sez th king, kiender moking him; “we’ll tri and get ’em to send for u;” which maed them all laf, and thay sed it was a priem guud hit.




















CHAPTER XXVI.

Wel, when thay was all gon th king he asks Mary Jane how thay was off for spair rooms, and she sed she had wun spair room, which wuud do for Unkl William, and she’d giv her oen room to Unkl Harvey, which was a litl biger, and she wuud tern into th room with her sisters and sleep on a cot; and up garret was a litl cubby, with a palet in it. Th king sed th cubby wuud do for his valy—meening me.

So Mary Jane tuuk us up, and she shoed them thair rooms, which was plaen but nies. She sed she’d hav her froks and a lot of uther traps tuuk out of her room if thay was in Unkl Harvey’s way, but he sed thay worn’t. Th froks was hung along th wall, and befor them was a curten maed out of calico that hung doun to th flor. Thair was an oeld hair trunk in wun corner, and a gitar-box in anuther, and all sorts of litl knickknacks and jimcracks around, liek gerls brisken up a room with. Th king sed it was all th mor hoemly and mor pleasanter for thees fixings, and so don’t disterb them. Th duek’s room was prity small, but plenty guud enuf, and so was mi cubby.

That niet thay had a big super, and all them men and wimen was thair, and I stuud behiend th king and th duek’s chairs and waeted on them, and th niggers waeted on th rest. Mary Jane she set at th hed of th taebl, with Susan alongsied of her, and sed how bad th biskits was, and how meen th prezervs was, and how ornery and tuf th fried chikens was—and all that kiend of rot, th way wimen allways do for to fors out compliments; and th peepl all knowed evrything was tiptop, and sed so—sed “How do u get biskits to broun so nies?” and “Whair, for th land’s saek, did u get thees amaz’n pikls?” and all that kiend of humbug tauky-tauk, just th way peepl allways duz at a super, u noe.











And when it was all dun me and th hair-lip had super in th kichen off of th leevings, whilst th uthers was helping th niggers cleen up th things. Th hair-lip she got to pumping me about England, and blest if I didn’t think th ies was geting miety thin sumtiems. She sez:

“Did u ever see th king?”

“Hoo? William Foerth? Wel, I bet I hav—he goes to our cherch.” I knowed he was ded yeers ago, but I never let on. So when I sez he goes to our cherch, she sez:

“Whut—reguelar?”

“Yes—reguelar. His pue’s riet oever opozit ourn—on t’uther sied th puulpit.”

“I thaut he livd in London?”

“Wel, he duz. Whair wuud he liv?”

“But I thaut u livd in Sheffield?”

I see I was up a stump. I had to let on to get choekt with a chiken boen, so as to get tiem to think how to get doun agen. Then I sez:

“I meen he goes to our cherch reguelar when he’s in Sheffield. That’s oenly in th sumer tiem, when he cums thair to taek th see baths.”

“Whi, how u tauk—Sheffield ain’t on th see.”

“Wel, hoo sed it was?”

“Whi, u did.”

“I didn’t nuther.”

“U did!”

“I didn’t.”

“U did.”

“I never sed nuthing of th kiend.”

“Wel, whut did u say, then?”

“Sed he cum to taek th see baths—that’s whut I sed.”

“Wel, then, how’s he going to taek th see baths if it ain’t on th see?”

“Luuky heer,” I sez; “did u ever see eny Conggres-wauter?”

“Yes.”

“Wel, did u hav to go to Conggres to get it?”

“Whi, no.”

“Wel, neether duz William Foerth hav to go to th see to get a see bath.”

“How duz he get it, then?”
