“Gets it th way peepl doun heer gets Conggres-wauter—in barrels. Thair in th palas at Sheffield thay’ve got fernises, and he wonts his wauter hot. Thay can’t biel that amount of wauter away off thair at th see. Thay haeven’t got no conveenyunses for it.”

“O, I see, now. U miet a sed that in th ferst plaes and saevd tiem.”

When she sed that I see I was out of th wuuds agen, and so I was cumfortabl and glad. Next, she sez:

“Do u go to cherch, too?”

“Yes—reguelar.”

“Whair do u set?”

“Whi, in our pue.”

“Hoos pue?”

“Whi, ourn—yur Unkl Harvey’s.”

“His’n? Whut duz he wont with a pue?”

“Wonts it to set in. Whut did u rekon he wonted with it?”

“Whi, I thaut he’d be in th puulpit.”

Rot him, I forgot he was a preecher. I see I was up a stump agen, so I playd anuther chiken boen and got anuther think. Then I sez:

“Blaem it, do u supoez thair ain’t but wun preecher to a cherch?”

“Whi, whut do thay wont with mor?”

“Whut!—to preech befor a king? I never did see such a gerl as u. Thay don’t hav no les than seventeen.”

“Seventeen! Mi land! Whi, I wouldn’t set out such a string as that, not if I never got to glory. It must taek ’em a week.”

“Shuks, thay don’t all of ’em preech th saem day—oenly wun of ’em.”

“Wel, then, whut duz th rest of ’em do?”

“O, nuthing much. Lol around, pas th plaet—and wun thing or anuther. But maenly thay don’t do nuthing.”

“Wel, then, whut ar thay for?”

“Whi, thay’re for stiel. Don’t u noe nuthing?”

“Wel, I don’t wont to noe no such foolishnes as that. How is servants treeted in England? Do thay treet ’em beter ’n we treet our niggers?”

“No! A servant ain’t noebody thair. Thay treet them wers than daugs.”

“Don’t thay giv ’em holidays, th way we do, Christmas and Nue Yeer’s week, and Foerth of July?”

“O, just lisen! A body cuud tel u hain’t ever bin to England bi that. Whi, Hair-l—whi, Joanna, thay never see a holiday frum yeer’s end to yeer’s end; never go to th sercus, nor theeater, nor nigger shoes, nor nowheres.”

“Nor cherch?”

“Nor cherch.”

“But u allways went to cherch.”

Wel, I was gon up agen. I forgot I was th oeld man’s servant. But next minit I wherld in on a kiend of an explanaeshun how a valy was diferent frum a comon servant and had to go to cherch whether he wonted to or not, and set with th family, on acount of its being th law. But I didn’t do it prity guud, and when I got dun I see she worn’t satisfied. She sez:

“Onest injun, now, hain’t u bin teling me a lot of lies?”











“Onest injun,” sez I.

“Nun of it at all?”

“Nun of it at all. Not a lie in it,” sez I.

“Lay yur hand on this buuk and say it.”

I see it worn’t nuthing but a dicshunairy, so I laed mi hand on it and sed it. So then she luukt a litl beter satisfied, and sez:

“Wel, then, I’ll beleev sum of it; but I hoep to graeshus if I’ll beleev th rest.”

“Whut is it u wun’t beleev, Joe?” sez Mary Jane, steping in with Susan behiend her. “It ain’t riet nor kiend for u to tauk so to him, and him a straenjer and so far frum his peepl. How wuud u liek to be treeted so?”

“That’s allways yur way, Maim—allways saeling in to help sumbody befor thay’re hert. I hain’t dun nuthing to him. He’s toeld sum stretchers, I rekon, and I sed I wouldn’t swolo it all; and that’s evry bit and graen I did say. I rekon he can stand a litl thing liek that, can’t he?”

“I don’t cair whether ’twas litl or whether ’twas big; he’s heer in our hous and a straenjer, and it wasn’t guud of u to say it. If u was in his plaes it wuud maek u feel ashaemd; and so u oughtn’t to say a thing to anuther person that wil maek them feel ashaemd.”

“Whi, Mam, he sed—”

“It don’t maek no diferens whut he sed—that ain’t th thing. Th thing is for u to treet him kiend, and not be saying things to maek him remember he ain’t in his oen cuntry and amungst his oen foeks.”

I sez to mieself, this is a gerl that I’m leting that oeld reptiel rob her of her muny!

Then Susan she waltzed in; and if u’ll beleev me, she did giv Hair-lip hark frum th toom!

Sez I to mieself, and this is anuther wun that I’m leting him rob her of her muny!

Then Mary Jane she tuuk anuther ining, and went in sweet and luvly agen—which was her way; but when she got dun thair worn’t hardly enything left o’ pur Hair-lip. So she holerd.

“All riet, then,” sez th uther gerls; “u just ask his pardon.”

She dun it, too; and she dun it buetiful. She dun it so buetiful it was guud to heer; and I wisht I cuud tel her a thouzand lies, so she cuud do it agen.

I sez to mieself, this is anuther wun that I’m leting him rob her of her muny. And when she got thru thay all jest laed theirselves out to maek me feel at hoem and noe I was amungst frends. I felt so ornery and lo doun and meen that I sez to mieself, mi miend’s maed up; I’ll hiev that muny for them or bust.

So then I lit out—for bed, I sed, meening sum tiem or anuther. When I got bi mieself I went to thinking th thing oever. I sez to mieself, shal I go to that doctor, prievet, and blo on thees frauds? No—that wun’t do. He miet tel hoo toeld him; then th king and th duek wuud maek it worm for me. Shal I go, prievet, and tel Mary Jane? No—I dasn’t do it. Her faes wuud giv them a hint, shur; thay’ve got th muny, and thay’d slied riet out and get away with it. If she was to fech in help I’d get mixt up in th biznes befor it was dun with, I juj. No; thair ain’t no guud way but wun. I got to steel that muny, sumhow; and I got to steel it sum way that thay wun’t suspishun that I dun it. Thay’ve got a guud thing heer, and thay ain’t a-going to leev til thay’ve playd this family and this toun for all thay’re werth, so I’ll fiend a chans tiem enuf. I’ll steel it and hied it; and bi and bi, when I’m away doun th river, I’ll riet a leter and tel Mary Jane whair it’s hid. But I beter hiev it toniet if I can, becauz th doctor maybe hasn’t let up as much as he lets on he has; he miet scair them out of heer yet.

So, thinks I, I’ll go and serch them rooms. Upstairs th hall was dark, but I found th duek’s room, and started to paw around it with mi hands; but I recolected it wouldn’t be much liek th king to let enybody els taek cair of that muny but his oen self; so then I went to his room and begun to paw around thair. But I see I couldn’t do nuthing without a candl, and I dasn’t liet wun, of cors. So I jujd I’d got to do th uther thing—lay for them and eevzdrop. About that tiem I heers thair fuutsteps cuming, and was going to skip under th bed; I reecht for it, but it wasn’t whair I thaut it wuud be; but I tucht th curten that hid Mary Jane’s froks, so I jumpt in behiend that and snugld in amungst th gouns, and stuud thair perfectly stil.











Thay cum in and shut th dor; and th ferst thing th duek dun was to get doun and luuk under th bed. Then I was glad I hadn’t found th bed when I wonted it. And yet, u noe, it’s kiend of nacheral to hied under th bed when u ar up to enything prievet. Thay sets doun then, and th king sez:

“Wel, whut is it? And cut it middlin’ short, becauz it’s beter for us to be doun thair a-whoopin’ up th mournin’ than up heer givin’ ’em a chans to tauk us oever.”

“Wel, this is it, Capet. I ain’t eezy; I ain’t cumfortabl. That doctor lays on mi miend. I wonted to noe yur plans. I’ve got a noeshun, and I think it’s a sound wun.”

“Whut is it, duek?”

“That we beter glied out of this befor three in th morning, and clip it doun th river with whut we’ve got. Speshaly, seeing we got it so eezy—given bak to us, flung at our heds, as u may say, when of cors we alowd to hav to steel it bak. I’m for noking off and lieting out.”

That maed me feel prity bad. About an our or too ago it wuud a bin a litl diferent, but now it maed me feel bad and disapointed, Th king rips out and sez:

“Whut! And not sel out th rest o’ th property? March off liek a passel of fools and leev aet or nien thous’n’ dolars’ werth o’ property layin’ around jest sufferin’ to be scoopt in?—and all guud, saelabl stuf, too.”

Th duek he grumbld; sed th bag of goeld was enuf, and he didn’t wont to go no deeper—didn’t wont to rob a lot of orfans of evrything thay had.

“Whi, how u tauk!” sez th king. “We sha’n’t rob ’em of nuthing at all but jest this muny. Th peepl that bies th property is th suff’rers; becauz as soon ’s it’s found out ’at we didn’t oen it—which wun’t be long after we’ve slid—th sael wun’t be valid, and it ’ll all go bak to th estaet. Thees yer orfans ’ll git thair hous bak agin, and that’s enuf for them; thay’re yung and spri, and k’n eezy ern a livin’. thay ain’t a-goin to sufer. Whi, jest think—thair’s thous’n’s and thous’n’s that ain’t ni so wel off. Bles u, thay ain’t got noth’n’ to complaen of.”

Wel, th king he taukt him bliend; so at last he giv in, and sed all riet, but sed he beleevd it was blaemd foolishnes to stay, and that doctor hanging oever them. But th king sez:

“Cuss th doctor! Whut do we k’yer for him? Hain’t we got all th fools in toun on our sied? And ain’t that a big enuf majority in eny toun?”

So thay got redy to go doun stairs agen. Th duek sez:

“I don’t think we puut that muny in a guud plaes.”

That cheerd me up. I’d begun to think I worn’t going to get a hint of no kiend to help me. Th king sez:

“Whi?”

“Becauz Mary Jane ’ll be in morning frum this out; and ferst u noe th nigger that duz up th rooms wil get an order to box thees duds up and puut ’em away; and do u rekon a nigger can run across muny and not borro sum of it?”

“Yur hed’s level agin, duek,” sez th king; and he cums a-fumbling under th curten too or three fuut frum whair I was. I stuk tiet to th wall and kept miety stil, tho quivery; and I wunderd whut them feloes wuud say to me if thay catched me; and I tried to think whut I’d beter do if thay did cach me. But th king he got th bag befor I cuud think mor than about a haf a thaut, and he never suspicioned I was around. Thay tuuk and shuvd th bag thru a rip in th straw tik that was under th fether-bed, and cramd it in a fuut or too amungst th straw and sed it was all riet now, becauz a nigger oenly maeks up th fether-bed, and don’t tern oever th straw tik oenly about twies a yeer, and so it worn’t in no daenjer of geting stoel now.











But I knowed beter. I had it out of thair befor thay was haf-way doun stairs. I groept along up to mi cubby, and hid it thair til I cuud get a chans to do beter. I jujd I beter hied it outsied of th hous somewheres, becauz if thay mist it thay wuud giv th hous a guud ransaking: I knowed that verry wel. Then I ternd in, with mi cloeths all on; but I couldn’t a gon to sleep if I’d a wonted to, I was in such a swet to get thru with th biznes. Bi and bi I herd th king and th duek cum up; so I roeld off mi palet and laed with mi chin at th top of mi lader, and waeted to see if enything was going to hapen. But nuthing did.

So I held on til all th laet sounds had qit and th erly wuns hadn’t begun yet; and then I slipt doun th lader.














CHAPTER XXVII.

I crept to thair dors and lisend; thay was snoring. So I tiptoed along, and got doun stairs all riet. Thair worn’t a sound anywheres. I peeped thru a crak of th diening-room dor, and see th men that was woching th corps all sound asleep on thair chairs. Th dor was oepen into th parlor, whair th corps was laying, and thair was a candl in boeth rooms. I past along, and th parlor dor was oepen; but I see thair worn’t noebody in thair but th remainders of Peeter; so I shuvd on bi; but th frunt dor was lokt, and th kee wasn’t thair. Just then I herd sumbody cuming doun th stairs, bak behiend me. I run in th parlor and tuuk a swift luuk around, and th oenly plaes I see to hied th bag was in th coffin. Th lid was shuvd along about a fuut, shoeing th ded man’s faes doun in thair, with a wet clauth oever it, and his shroud on. I tukt th muny-bag in under th lid, just doun beyond whair his hands was crosst, which maed me creep, thay was so coeld, and then I run bak across th room and in behiend th dor.

Th person cuming was Mary Jane. She went to th coffin, verry sofft, and neeld doun and luukt in; then she puut up her hankerchif, and I see she begun to cri, tho I couldn’t heer her, and her bak was to me. I slid out, and as I past th diening-room I thaut I’d maek shur them wochers hadn’t seen me; so I luukt thru th crak, and evrything was all riet. Thay hadn’t sterd.

I slipt up to bed, feeling ruther bloo, on acounts of th thing playing out that way after I had tuuk so much trubl and run so much resk about it. Sez I, if it cuud stay whair it is, all riet; becauz when we get doun th river a hundred miel or too I cuud riet bak to Mary Jane, and she cuud dig him up agen and get it; but that ain’t th thing that’s going to hapen; th thing that’s going to hapen is, th muny ’ll be found when thay cum to scroo on th lid. Then th king ’ll get it agen, and it ’ll be a long day befor he givs enybody anuther chans to smouch it frum him. Of cors I wonted to slied doun and get it out of thair, but I dasn’t tri it. Evry minit it was geting erlyer now, and prity soon sum of them wochers wuud begin to ster, and I miet get catched—catched with six thouzand dolars in mi hands that noebody hadn’t hierd me to taek cair of. I don’t wish to be mixt up in no such biznes as that, I sez to mieself.

When I got doun stairs in th morning th parlor was shut up, and th wochers was gon. Thair worn’t noebody around but th family and th wido Bartley and our trieb. I wocht thair faeses to see if enything had bin hapening, but I couldn’t tel.

Tords th midl of th day th undertaeker cum with his man, and thay set th coffin in th midl of th room on a cupl of chairs, and then set all our chairs in roes, and borroed mor frum th naebors til th hall and th parlor and th diening-room was fuul. I see th coffin lid was th way it was befor, but I dasn’t go to luuk in under it, with foeks around.

Then th peepl begun to flok in, and th beets and th gerls tuuk seets in th frunt ro at th hed of th coffin, and for a haf an our th peepl field around slo, in singgl rank, and luukt doun at th ded man’s faes a minit, and sum dropt in a teer, and it was all verry stil and solem, oenly th gerls and th beets hoelding hankerchifs to thair ies and keeping thair heds bent, and sobing a litl. Thair worn’t no uther sound but th scraeping of th feet on th flor and bloeing noezes—becauz peepl allways bloes them mor at a fueneral than thay do at uther plaeses exsept cherch.

When th plaes was pakt fuul th undertaeker he slid around in his blak gluvs with his softy soothering ways, puuting on th last tuches, and geting peepl and things all ship-shaep and cumfortabl, and maeking no mor sound than a cat. He never spoek; he moovd peepl around, he sqeezd in laet wuns, he oepend up pasejways, and dun it with nods, and siens with his hands. Then he tuuk his plaes oever agenst th wall. He was th sofftest, glidingest, stealthiest man I ever see; and thair worn’t no mor smiel to him than thair is to a ham.











Thay had borroed a melodeum—a sik wun; and when evrything was redy a yung wuuman set doun and werkt it, and it was prity skreeky and coliky, and evrybody joind in and sung, and Peeter was th oenly wun that had a guud thing, acording to mi noeshun. Then th Reverend Hobson oepend up, slo and solem, and begun to tauk; and straet off th moest outraejus ro busted out in th selar a body ever herd; it was oenly wun daug, but he maed a moest powerful raket, and he kept it up riet along; th parson he had to stand thair, oever th coffin, and waet—u couldn’t heer yurself think. It was riet doun aukward, and noebody didn’t seem to noe whut to do. But prity soon thay see that long-legd undertaeker maek a sien to th preecher as much as to say, “Don’t u wery—just depend on me.” Then he stoopt doun and begun to glied along th wall, just his shoelders shoeing oever th peepl’s heds. So he glieded along, and th powwow and raket geting mor and mor outraejus all th tiem; and at last, when he had gon around too sieds of th room, he disapeers doun selar. Then in about too seconds we herd a whak, and th daug he finisht up with a moest amaezing houl or too, and then evrything was ded stil, and th parson begun his solem tauk whair he left off. In a minit or too heer cums this undertaeker’s bak and shoelders gliding along th wall agen; and so he glieded and glieded around three sieds of th room, and then roez up, and shaeded his mouth with his hands, and strecht his nek out tords th preecher, oever th peepl’s heds, and sez, in a kiend of a cors whisper, “He had a rat!” Then he droopt doun and glieded along th wall agen to his plaes. U cuud see it was a graet satisfacshun to th peepl, becauz nacheraly thay wonted to noe. A litl thing liek that don’t cost nuthing, and it’s just th litl things that maeks a man to be luukt up to and liekt. Thair worn’t no mor popuelar man in toun than whut that undertaeker was.











Wel, th fueneral sermon was verry guud, but pison long and tiersum; and then th king he shuvd in and got off sum of his uezhual rubbage, and at last th job was thru, and th undertaeker begun to sneek up on th coffin with his scroo-driever. I was in a swet then, and wocht him prity keen. But he never meddled at all; just slid th lid along as sofft as mush, and scrood it doun tiet and fast. So thair I was! I didn’t noe whether th muny was in thair or not. So, sez I, s’poez sumbody has hogged that bag on th sli?—now how do I noe whether to riet to Mary Jane or not? S’poez she dug him up and didn’t fiend nuthing, whut wuud she think of me? Blaem it, I sez, I miet get hunted up and jaeld; I’d beter lay lo and keep dark, and not riet at all; th thing’s awful mixt now; trieing to beter it, I’ve wersend it a hundred tiems, and I wish to guudnes I’d just let it aloen, dad fech th hoel biznes!

Thay berryd him, and we cum bak hoem, and I went to woching faeses agen—I couldn’t help it, and I couldn’t rest eezy. But nuthing cum of it; th faeses didn’t tel me nuthing.

Th king he vizited around in th eevning, and sweetened evrybody up, and maed himself ever so frendly; and he giv out th iedeea that his conggregaeshun oever in England wuud be in a swet about him, so he must hery and setl up th estaet riet away and leev for hoem. He was verry sorry he was so puusht, and so was evrybody; thay wisht he cuud stay longger, but thay sed thay cuud see it couldn’t be dun. And he sed of cors him and William wuud taek th gerls hoem with them; and that pleezd evrybody too, becauz then th gerls wuud be wel fixt and amungst thair oen relaeshuns; and it pleezd th gerls, too—tikld them so thay cleen forgot thay ever had a trubl in th werld; and toeld him to sel out as qik as he wonted to, thay wuud be redy. Them pur things was that glad and hapy it maed mi hart aek to see them geting foold and lied to so, but I didn’t see no saef way for me to chip in and chaenj th jeneral tuen.

Wel, blaemd if th king didn’t bil th hous and th niggers and all th property for aucshun straet off—sael too days after th fueneral; but enybody cuud bi prievet beforhand if thay wonted to.

So th next day after th fueneral, along about noon-tiem, th gerls’ joy got th ferst joelt. A cupl of nigger traeders cum along, and th king soeld them th niggers reezonabl, for three-day drafts as thay calld it, and away thay went, th too suns up th river to Memphis, and thair muther doun th river to Orleans. I thaut them pur gerls and them niggers wuud braek thair harts for greef; thay cried around eech uther, and tuuk on so it moest maed me doun sik to see it. Th gerls sed thay hadn’t ever dreemd of seeing th family separaeted or soeld away frum th toun. I can’t ever get it out of mi memory, th siet of them pur mizerabl gerls and niggers hanging around eech uther’s neks and crieing; and I rekon I couldn’t a stuud it all, but wuud a had to bust out and tel on our gang if I hadn’t knowed th sael worn’t no acount and th niggers wuud be bak hoem in a week or too.

Th thing maed a big ster in th toun, too, and a guud meny cum out flatfuuted and sed it was scandalus to separaet th muther and th children that way. It injerd th frauds sum; but th oeld fool he bulled riet along, spiet of all th duek cuud say or do, and I tel u th duek was powerful uneezy.

Next day was aucshun day. About braud day in th morning th king and th duek cum up in th garret and woek me up, and I see bi thair luuk that thair was trubl. Th king sez:

“Was u in mi room niet befor last?”

“No, yur majesty”—which was th way I allways calld him when noebody but our gang worn’t around.











“Was u in thair yisterday er last niet?”

“No, yur majesty.”

“Onor briet, now—no lies.”

“Onor briet, yur majesty, I’m teling u th trooth. I hain’t bin a-neer yur room sinss Mis Mary Jane tuuk u and th duek and shoed it to u.”

Th duek sez:

“Hav u seen enybody els go in thair?”

“No, yur graes, not as I remember, I beleev.”

“Stop and think.”

I studyd awhiel and see mi chans; then I sez:

“Wel, I see th niggers go in thair several tiems.”

Boeth of them gaev a litl jump, and luukt liek thay hadn’t ever expected it, and then liek thay had. Then th duek sez:

“Whut, all of them?”

“No—leastways, not all at wuns—that is, I don’t think I ever see them all cum out at wuns but just wun tiem.”

“Helo! When was that?”

“It was th day we had th fueneral. In th morning. It worn’t erly, becauz I oeverslept. I was just starting doun th lader, and I see them.”

“Wel, go on, go on! Whut did thay do? How’d thay act?”

“Thay didn’t do nuthing. And thay didn’t act enyway much, as fer as I see. Thay tiptoed away; so I seen, eezy enuf, that thay’d shuvd in thair to do up yur majesty’s room, or sumthing, s’poezing u was up; and found u worn’t up, and so thay was hoeping to slied out of th way of trubl without waeking u up, if thay hadn’t allredy waekt u up.”

“Graet guns, this is a go!” sez th king; and boeth of them luukt prity sik and tolerabl sily. Thay stuud thair a-thinking and scraching thair heds a minit, and th duek he bust into a kiend of a litl raspy chukl, and sez:

“It duz beet all how neet th niggers playd thair hand. Thay let on to be sorry thay was going out of this reejon! And I beleevd thay was sorry, and so did u, and so did evrybody. Don’t ever tel me eny mor that a nigger ain’t got eny histrionic talent. Whi, th way thay playd that thing it wuud fool enybody. In mi opinyon, thair’s a forchun in ’em. If I had capital and a theeater, I wouldn’t wont a beter lay-out than that—and heer we’ve gon and soeld ’em for a song. Yes, and ain’t privilejd to sing th song yet. Say, whair is that song—that draft?”

“In th bank for to be colected. Whair wuud it be?”

“Wel, that’s all riet then, thank guudnes.”

Sez I, kiend of timid-liek:

“Is sumthing gon rong?”

Th king wherls on me and rips out:

“Nun o’ yur biznes! U keep yur hed shet, and miend y’r oen afairs—if u got eny. Long as u’re in this toun don’t u forgit that—u heer?” Then he sez to th duek, “We got to jest swaller it and say noth’n’: mum’s th werd for us.”

As thay was starting doun th lader th duek he chukls agen, and sez:

“Qik saels and small profits! It’s a guud biznes—yes.”











Th king snarls around on him and sez:

“I was trieing to do for th best in sellin’ ’em out so qik. If th profits has ternd out to be nun, lackin’ considable, and nun to carry, is it mi fallt eny mor’n it’s yourn?”

“Wel, thay’d be in this hous yet and we wouldn’t if I cuud a got mi advies lisend to.”

Th king sassed bak as much as was saef for him, and then swapped around and lit into me agen. He giv me doun th banks for not cuming and teling him I see th niggers cum out of his room acting that way—sed eny fool wuud a knowed sumthing was up. And then waltzed in and cussed himself awhiel, and sed it all cum of him not laying laet and taeking his nacheral rest that morning, and he’d be blaemd if he’d ever do it agen. So thay went off a-jawing; and I felt dredful glad I’d werkt it all off on to th niggers, and yet hadn’t dun th niggers no harm bi it.














CHAPTER XXVIII.

Bi and bi it was geting-up tiem. So I cum doun th lader and started for doun-stairs; but as I cum to th gerls’ room th dor was oepen, and I see Mary Jane seting bi her oeld hair trunk, which was oepen and she’d bin paking things in it—geting redy to go to England. But she had stopt now with a foelded goun in her lap, and had her faes in her hands, crieing. I felt awful bad to see it; of cors enybody wuud. I went in thair and sez:

“Mis Mary Jane, u can’t a-bair to see peepl in trubl, and I can’t—moest allways. Tel me about it.”

So she dun it. And it was th niggers—I just expected it. She sed th buetiful trip to England was moest about spoild for her; she didn’t noe how she was ever going to be hapy thair, noeing th muther and th children worn’t ever going to see eech uther no mor—and then busted out bitterer than ever, and flung up her hands, and sez:

“O, deer, deer, to think thay ain’t ever going to see eech uther eny mor!”

“But thay wil—and insied of too weeks—and I noe it!” sez I.

Laws, it was out befor I cuud think! And befor I cuud buj she throes her arms around mi nek and toeld me to say it agen, say it agen, say it agen!

I see I had spoek too suden and sed too much, and was in a cloez plaes. I askt her to let me think a minit; and she set thair, verry impaeshent and exsieted and hansum, but luuking kiend of hapy and eezd-up, liek a person that’s had a tooth puuld out. So I went to studying it out. I sez to mieself, I rekon a body that ups and tels th trooth when he is in a tiet plaes is taeking considerabl meny resks, tho I ain’t had no expeeryens, and can’t say for serten; but it luuks so to me, enyway; and yet heer’s a caes whair I’m blest if it don’t luuk to me liek th trooth is beter and actuly saefer than a lie. I must lay it bi in mi miend, and think it oever sum tiem or uther, it’s so kiend of straenj and unregular. I never see nuthing liek it. Wel, I sez to mieself at last, I’m a-going to chans it; I’ll up and tel th trooth this tiem, tho it duz seem moest liek seting doun on a kag of pouder and tuching it off just to see whair u’ll go to. Then I sez:

“Mis Mary Jane, is thair eny plaes out of toun a litl ways whair u cuud go and stay three or foer days?”

“Yes; Mr. Lothrop’s. Whi?”

“Never miend whi yet. If I’ll tel u how I noe th niggers wil see eech uther agen insied of too weeks—heer in this hous—and proov how I noe it—wil u go to Mr. Lothrop’s and stay foer days?”

“Foer days!” she sez; “I’ll stay a yeer!”

“All riet,” I sez, “I don’t wont nuthing mor out of u than just yur werd—I druther hav it than anuther man’s kis-th-Biebl.” She smield and redend up verry sweet, and I sez, “If u don’t miend it, I’ll shut th dor—and boelt it.”

Then I cum bak and set doun agen, and sez:

“Don’t u holler. Just set stil and taek it liek a man. I got to tel th trooth, and u wont to braes up, Mis Mary, becauz it’s a bad kiend, and going to be hard to taek, but thair ain’t no help for it. Thees unkls of yourn ain’t no unkls at all; thay’re a cupl of frauds—reguelar ded-beets. Thair, now we’re oever th werst of it, u can stand th rest midling eezy.”

It jolted her up liek evrything, of cors; but I was oever th shoel wauter now, so I went riet along, her ies a-blaezing hieer and hieer all th tiem, and toeld her evry blaem thing, frum whair we ferst struk that yung fool going up to th steemboet, cleer thru to whair she flung herself on to th king’s brest at th frunt dor and he kist her sixteen or seventeen tiems—and then up she jumps, with her faes afier liek sunset, and sez:

“Th broot! Cum, don’t waest a minit—not a second—we’ll hav them tard and fetherd, and flung in th river!”











Sez I:

“Cert’nly. But do u meen befor u go to Mr. Lothrop’s, or—”

“O,” she sez, “whut am I thinking about!” she sez, and set riet doun agen. “Don’t miend whut I sed—pleez don’t—u wun’t, now, wil u?” Laying her silky hand on mien in that kiend of a way that I sed I wuud die ferst. “I never thaut, I was so sterd up,” she sez; “now go on, and I wun’t do so eny mor. U tel me whut to do, and whutever u say I’ll do it.”

“Wel,” I sez, “it’s a ruf gang, them too frauds, and I’m fixt so I got to travel with them a whiel longger, whether I wont to or not—I druther not tel u whi; and if u was to blo on them this toun wuud get me out of thair claws, and I’d be all riet; but thair’d be anuther person that u don’t noe about hoo’d be in big trubl. Wel, we got to saev him, hain’t we? Of cors. Wel, then, we wun’t blo on them.”

Saying them werds puut a guud iedeea in mi hed. I see how maybe I cuud get me and Jim rid of th frauds; get them jaeld heer, and then leev. But I didn’t wont to run th raft in th daytiem without enybody abord to anser qeschuns but me; so I didn’t wont th plan to begin werking til prity laet to-niet. I sez:

“Mis Mary Jane, I’ll tel u whut we’ll do, and u wun’t hav to stay at Mr. Lothrop’s so long, nuther. How fer is it?”

“A litl short of foer miels—riet out in th cuntry, bak heer.”

“Wel, that ’ll anser. Now u go along out thair, and lay lo til nien or haf-past to-niet, and then get them to fech u hoem agen—tel them u’ve thaut of sumthing. If u get heer befor eleven puut a candl in this windo, and if I don’t tern up waet til eleven, and then if I don’t tern up it meens I’m gon, and out of th way, and saef. Then u cum out and spred th nues around, and get thees beets jaeld.”

“Guud,” she sez, “I’ll do it.”

“And if it just hapens so that I don’t get away, but get tuuk up along with them, u must up and say I toeld u th hoel thing beforhand, and u must stand bi me all u can.”

“Stand bi u! indeed I wil. Thay sha’n’t tuch a hair of yur hed!” she sez, and I see her nostrils spred and her ies snap when she sed it, too.

“If I get away I sha’n’t be heer,” I sez, “to proov thees rapscallions ain’t yur unkls, and I couldn’t do it if I was heer. I cuud swair thay was beets and bummers, that’s all, tho that’s werth sumthing. Wel, thair’s uthers can do that beter than whut I can, and thay’re peepl that ain’t going to be douted as qik as I’d be. I’ll tel u how to fiend them. Gimme a pensil and a pees of paeper. Thair—‘Royal Nonesuch, Bricksville.’ Puut it away, and don’t looz it. When th cort wonts to fiend out sumthing about thees too, let them send up to Bricksville and say thay’ve got th men that playd th Royal Nonesuch, and ask for sum witneses—whi, u’ll hav that entier toun doun heer befor u can hardly wink, Mis Mary. And thay’ll cum a-biling, too.”











I jujd we had got evrything fixt about riet now. So I sez:

“Just let th aucshun go riet along, and don’t wery. Noebody don’t hav to pay for th things thay bi til a hoel day after th aucshun on acounts of th short noetis, and thay ain’t going out of this til thay get that muny; and th way we’ve fixt it th sael ain’t going to count, and thay ain’t going to get no muny. It’s just liek th way it was with th niggers—it worn’t no sael, and th niggers wil be bak befor long. Whi, thay can’t colect th muny for th niggers yet—thay’re in th werst kiend of a fix, Mis Mary.”

“Wel,” she sez, “I’ll run doun to brekfast now, and then I’ll start straet for Mr. Lothrop’s.”

“’Deed, that ain’t th tiket, Mis Mary Jane,” I sez, “bi no maner of meens; go befor brekfast.”

“Whi?”

“Whut did u rekon I wonted u to go at all for, Mis Mary?”

“Wel, I never thaut—and cum to think, I don’t noe. Whut was it?”

“Whi, it’s becauz u ain’t wun of thees lether-faes peepl. I don’t wont no beter buuk than whut yur faes is. A body can set doun and red it off liek cors print. Do u rekon u can go and faes yur unkls when thay cum to kis u guud-morning, and never—”

“Thair, thair, don’t! Yes, I’ll go befor brekfast—I’ll be glad to. And leev mi sisters with them?”

“Yes; never miend about them. Thay’ve got to stand it yet a whiel. Thay miet suspishun sumthing if all of u was to go. I don’t wont u to see them, nor yur sisters, nor noebody in this toun; if a naebor was to ask how is yur unkls this morning yur faes wuud tel sumthing. No, u go riet along, Mis Mary Jane, and I’ll fix it with all of them. I’ll tel Mis Susan to giv yur luv to yur unkls and say u’ve went away for a fue ours for to get a litl rest and chaenj, or to see a frend, and u’ll be bak to-niet or erly in th morning.”

“Gon to see a frend is all riet, but I wun’t hav mi luv given to them.”

“Wel, then, it sha’n’t be.” It was wel enuf to tel her so—no harm in it. It was oenly a litl thing to do, and no trubl; and it’s th litl things that smooths peepl’s roeds th moest, doun heer belo; it wuud maek Mary Jane cumfortabl, and it wouldn’t cost nuthing. Then I sez: “Thair’s wun mor thing—that bag of muny.”

“Wel, thay’ve got that; and it maeks me feel prity sily to think how thay got it.”

“No, u’re out, thair. Thay hain’t got it.”

“Whi, hoo’s got it?”

“I wish I knowed, but I don’t. I had it, becauz I stoel it frum them; and I stoel it to giv to u; and I noe whair I hid it, but I’m afraed it ain’t thair no mor. I’m awful sorry, Mis Mary Jane, I’m just as sorry as I can be; but I dun th best I cuud; I did onest. I cum ni geting caut, and I had to shuv it into th ferst plaes I cum to, and run—and it worn’t a guud plaes.”

“O, stop blaeming yurself—it’s too bad to do it, and I wun’t alow it—u couldn’t help it; it wasn’t yur fallt. Whair did u hied it?”

I didn’t wont to set her to thinking about her trubls agen; and I couldn’t seem to get mi mouth to tel her whut wuud maek her see that corps laying in th coffin with that bag of muny on his stumac. So for a minit I didn’t say nuthing; then I sez:

“I’d ruther not tel u whair I puut it, Mis Mary Jane, if u don’t miend leting me off; but I’ll riet it for u on a pees of paeper, and u can red it along th roed to Mr. Lothrop’s, if u wont to. Do u rekon that ’ll do?”

“O, yes.”

So I roet: “I puut it in th coffin. It was in thair when u was crieing thair, away in th niet. I was behiend th dor, and I was miety sorry for u, Mis Mary Jane.”











It maed mi ies wauter a litl to remember her crieing thair all bi herself in th niet, and them devils laying thair riet under her oen roof, shaming her and robing her; and when I foelded it up and giv it to her I see th wauter cum into her ies, too; and she shuuk me bi th hand, hard, and sez:

“Guud-bi. I’m going to do evrything just as u’ve toeld me; and if I don’t ever see u agen, I sha’n’t ever forget u and I’ll think of u a meny and a meny a tiem, and I’ll pray for u, too!”—and she was gon.

Pray for me! I rekond if she knowed me she’d taek a job that was mor neerer her siez. But I bet she dun it, just th saem—she was just that kiend. She had th grit to pray for Judus if she tuuk th noeshun—thair worn’t no bak-doun to her, I juj. U may say whut u wont to, but in mi opinyon she had mor sand in her than eny gerl I ever see; in mi opinyon she was just fuul of sand. It sounds liek flatery, but it ain’t no flatery. And when it cums to buety—and guudnes, too—she lays oever them all. I hain’t ever seen her sinss that tiem that I see her go out of that dor; no, I hain’t ever seen her sinss, but I rekon I’ve thaut of her a meny and a meny a milyon tiems, and of her saying she wuud pray for me; and if ever I’d a thaut it wuud do eny guud for me to pray for her, blaemd if I wouldn’t a dun it or bust.

Wel, Mary Jane she lit out th bak way, I rekon; becauz noebody see her go. When I struk Susan and th hair-lip, I sez:

“Whut’s th naem of them peepl oever on t’uther sied of th river that u all goes to see sumtiems?”

Thay sez:

“Thair’s several; but it’s th Proctors, maenly.”

“That’s th naem,” I sez; “I moest forgot it. Wel, Mis Mary Jane she toeld me to tel u she’s gon oever thair in a dredful hery—wun of them’s sik.”

“Which wun?”

“I don’t noe; leastways, I kiender forget; but I thinks it’s—”

“Sakes aliev, I hoep it ain’t Hanner?”

“I’m sorry to say it,” I sez, “but Hanner’s th verry wun.”

“Mi guudnes, and she so wel oenly last week! Is she tuuk bad?”

“It ain’t no naem for it. Thay set up with her all niet, Mis Mary Jane sed, and thay don’t think she’ll last meny ours.”

“Oenly think of that, now! Whut’s th mater with her?”

I couldn’t think of enything reezonabl, riet off that way, so I sez:

“Mumps.”

“Mumps yur grany! Thay don’t set up with peepl that’s got th mumps.”

“Thay don’t, don’t thay? U beter bet thay do with thees mumps. Thees mumps is diferent. It’s a nue kiend, Mis Mary Jane sed.”











“How’s it a nue kiend?”

“Becauz it’s mixt up with uther things.”

“Whut uther things?”

“Wel, meezls, and hooping-cauf, and erysiplas, and consumpshun, and yaller janders, and braen-feever, and I don’t noe whut all.”

“Mi land! And thay call it th mumps?”

“That’s whut Mis Mary Jane sed.”

“Wel, whut in th naeshun do thay call it th mumps for?”

“Whi, becauz it is th mumps. That’s whut it starts with.”

“Wel, ther’ ain’t no sens in it. A body miet stump his toe, and taek pison, and fall doun th wel, and braek his nek, and bust his braens out, and sumbody cum along and ask whut kild him, and sum numskul up and say, ‘Whi, he stumpt his toe.’ Wuud ther’ be eny sens in that? No. And ther’ ain’t no sens in this, nuther. Is it ketching?”

“Is it ketching? Whi, how u tauk. Is a harro caching—in th dark? If u don’t hich on to wun tooth, u’re bound to on anuther, ain’t u? And u can’t get away with that tooth without feching th hoel harro along, can u? Wel, thees kiend of mumps is a kiend of a harro, as u may say—and it ain’t no slouch of a harro, nuther, u cum to get it hicht on guud.”

“Wel, it’s awful, I think,” sez th hair-lip. “I’ll go to Unkl Harvey and—”

“O, yes,” I sez, “I wuud. Of cors I wuud. I wouldn’t looz no tiem.”

“Wel, whi wouldn’t u?”

“Just luuk at it a minit, and maybe u can see. Hain’t yur unkls obleegd to get along hoem to England as fast as thay can? And do u rekon thay’d be meen enuf to go off and leev u to go all that jerny bi yurselvs? u noe thay’ll waet for u. So fer, so guud. Yur unkl Harvey’s a preecher, ain’t he? Verry wel, then; is a preecher going to deseev a steemboet clerk? is he going to deseev a ship clerk?—so as to get them to let Mis Mary Jane go abord? Now u noe he ain’t. Whut wil he do, then? Whi, he’ll say, ‘It’s a graet pity, but mi cherch maters has got to get along th best way thay can; for mi nees has bin expoezd to th dredful pluribus-unum mumps, and so it’s mi bounden duety to set doun heer and waet th three munths it taeks to sho on her if she’s got it.’ But never miend, if u think it’s best to tel yur unkl Harvey—”

“Shuks, and stay fooling around heer when we cuud all be having guud tiems in England whilst we was waeting to fiend out whether Mary Jane’s got it or not? Whi, u tauk liek a muggins.”

“Wel, enyway, maybe u’d beter tel sum of th naebors.”

“Lisen at that, now. U do beet all for nacheral stupidness. Can’t u see that thay’d go and tel? Ther’ ain’t no way but just to not tel enybody at all.”

“Wel, maybe u’re riet—yes, I juj u ar riet.”

“But I rekon we aut to tel Unkl Harvey she’s gon out a whiel, enyway, so he wun’t be uneezy about her?”

“Yes, Mis Mary Jane she wonted u to do that. She sez, ‘Tel them to giv Unkl Harvey and William mi luv and a kis, and say I’ve run oever th river to see Mr.’—Mr.—whut is th naem of that rich family yur unkl Peeter uezd to think so much of?—I meen th wun that—”

“Whi, u must meen th Apthorps, ain’t it?”

“Of cors; bother them kiend of naems, a body can’t ever seem to remember them, haf th tiem, sumhow. Yes, she sed, say she has run oever for to ask th Apthorps to be shur and cum to th aucshun and bi this hous, becauz she alowd her unkl Peeter wuud ruther thay had it than enybody els; and she’s going to stik to them til thay say thay’ll cum, and then, if she ain’t too tierd, she’s cuming hoem; and if she is, she’ll be hoem in th morning enyway. She sed, don’t say nuthing about th Proctors, but oenly about th Apthorps—which ’ll be perfectly troo, becauz she is going thair to speek about thair bieing th hous; I noe it, becauz she toeld me so herself.”

“All riet,” thay sed, and cleerd out to lay for thair unkls, and giv them th luv and th kises, and tel them th mesej.

Evrything was all riet now. Th gerls wouldn’t say nuthing becauz thay wonted to go to England; and th king and th duek wuud ruther Mary Jane was off werking for th aucshun than around in reech of Doctor Robinson. I felt verry guud; I jujd I had dun it prity neet—I rekond Tom Sawyer couldn’t a dun it no neeter himself. Of cors he wuud a throwed mor stiel into it, but I can’t do that verry handy, not being brung up to it.

Wel, thay held th aucshun in th public sqair, along tords th end of th afternoon, and it strung along, and strung along, and th oeld man he was on hand and luuking his level pisonest, up thair longside of th aucshuneer, and chiping in a litl Scripcher now and then, or a litl guudy-guudy saying of sum kiend, and th duek he was around goo-gooing for simpathy all he knowed how, and just spreding himself generly.











But bi and bi th thing dragd thru, and evrything was soeld—evrything but a litl oeld triefling lot in th graev-yard. So thay’d got to werk that off—I never see such a girafft as th king was for wonting to swolo evrything. Wel, whilst thay was at it a steemboet landed, and in about too minits up cums a croud a-hooping and yeling and lafing and carrying on, and singing out:

“Heer’s yur opozishun lien! heer’s yur too sets o’ errs to oeld Peeter Wilks—and u pays yur muny and u taeks yur chois!”














CHAPTER XXIX.

Thay was feching a verry nies-luuking oeld jentlman along, and a nies-luuking yungger wun, with his riet arm in a sling. And, mi soels, how th peepl yeld and laft, and kept it up. But I didn’t see no joek about it, and I jujd it wuud straen th duek and th king sum to see eny. I rekond thay’d tern pael. But no, nairy a pael did thay tern. Th duek he never let on he suspicioned whut was up, but just went a goo-gooing around, hapy and satisfied, liek a jug that’s googling out butermilk; and as for th king, he just gaezd and gaezd doun sorroeful on them nue-comers liek it giv him th stumac-aek in his verry hart to think thair cuud be such frauds and rascals in th werld. O, he dun it admerabl. Lots of th prinsipal peepl gethered around th king, to let him see thay was on his sied. That oeld jentlman that had just cum luukt all puzld to deth. Prity soon he begun to speek, and I see straet off he pronounst liek an Englishman—not th king’s way, tho th king’s was prity guud for an imitaeshun. I can’t giv th oeld gent’s werds, nor I can’t imitaet him; but he ternd around to th croud, and sez, about liek this:

“This is a serpriez to me which I wasn’t luuking for; and I’ll aknolej, candid and frank, I ain’t verry wel fixt to meet it and anser it; for mi bruther and me has had misforchens; he’s broek his arm, and our bagej got puut off at a toun abuv heer last niet in th niet bi a mistaek. I am Peeter Wilks’ bruther Harvey, and this is his bruther William, which can’t heer nor speek—and can’t eeven maek siens to amount to much, now’t he’s oenly got wun hand to werk them with. We ar hoo we say we ar; and in a day or too, when I get th bagej, I can proov it. But up til then I wun’t say nuthing mor, but go to th hoetel and waet.”

So him and th nue dumy started off; and th king he lafs, and blethers out:

“Broek his arm—verry liekly, ain’t it?—and verry conveenyunt, too, for a fraud that’s got to maek siens, and ain’t learnt how. Lost thair bagej! That’s miety guud!—and miety injeenius—under th sercumstanses!”

So he laft agen; and so did evrybody els, exsept three or foer, or maybe haf a duzen. Wun of thees was that doctor; anuther wun was a sharp-luuking jentlman, with a carpet-bag of th oeld-fashund kiend maed out of carpet-stuf, that had just cum off of th steemboet and was tauking to him in a lo vois, and glansing tords th king now and then and noding thair heds—it was Levi Bel, th lawyer that was gon up to Louisville; and anuther wun was a big ruf husky that cum along and lisend to all th oeld jentlman sed, and was lisening to th king now. And when th king got dun this husky up and sez:

“Say, luuky heer; if u ar Harvey Wilks, when’d u cum to this toun?”

“Th day befor th fueneral, frend,” sez th king.

“But whut tiem o’ day?”

“In th evenin’—’bout an our er too befor sundoun.”

“How’d u cum?”

“I cum doun on th Susan Powell frum Cincinnati.”

“Wel, then, how’d u cum to be up at th Pient in th mornin’—in a canoo?”

“I worn’t up at th Pient in th mornin’.”

“It’s a lie.”

Several of them jumpt for him and begd him not to tauk that way to an oeld man and a preecher.

“Preecher be hangd, he’s a fraud and a lieer. He was up at th Pient that mornin’. I liv up thair, don’t I? Wel, I was up thair, and he was up thair. I see him thair. He cum in a canoo, along with Tim Collins and a boy.”

Th doctor he up and sez:

“Wuud u noe th boy agen if u was to see him, Hines?”

“I rekon I wuud, but I don’t noe. Whi, yonder he is, now. I noe him perfectly eezy.”

It was me he pointed at. Th doctor sez:

“Naebors, I don’t noe whether th nue cupl is frauds or not; but if thees too ain’t frauds, I am an idiot, that’s all. I think it’s our duety to see that thay don’t get away frum heer til we’ve luukt into this thing. Cum along, Hines; cum along, th rest of u. We’ll taek thees feloes to th tavern and afrunt them with t’uther cupl, and I rekon we’ll fiend out sumthing befor we get thru.”

It was nuts for th croud, tho maybe not for th king’s frends; so we all started. It was about sundoun. Th doctor he led me along bi th hand, and was plenty kiend enuf, but he never let go mi hand.











We all got in a big room in th hoetel, and lit up sum candls, and fetched in th nue cupl. Ferst, th doctor sez:

“I don’t wish to be too hard on thees too men, but I think thay’re frauds, and thay may hav complices that we don’t noe nuthing about. If thay hav, wun’t th complices get away with that bag of goeld Peeter Wilks left? It ain’t unliekly. If thees men ain’t frauds, thay wun’t object to sending for that muny and leting us keep it til thay proov thay’re all riet—ain’t that so?”

Evrybody agreed to that. So I jujd thay had our gang in a prity tiet plaes riet at th outstart. But th king he oenly luukt sorroeful, and sez:

“Jentlmen, I wish th muny was thair, for I ain’t got no dispozishun to thro enything in th way of a fair, oepen, out-and-out investigaeshun o’ this misable biznes; but, alas, th muny ain’t thair; u k’n send and see, if u wont to.”

“Whair is it, then?”

“Wel, when mi nees giv it to me to keep for her I tuuk and hid it insied o’ th straw tik o’ mi bed, not wishin’ to bank it for th fue days we’d be heer, and considerin’ th bed a saef plaes, we not bein’ uezd to niggers, and suppos’n’ ’em onest, liek servants in England. Th niggers stoel it th verry next mornin’ after I had went doun stairs; and when I soeld ’em I hadn’t mist th muny yit, so thay got cleen away with it. Mi servant heer k’n tel u ’bout it, jentlmen.”

Th doctor and several sed “Shuks!” and I see noebody didn’t alltogether beleev him. Wun man askt me if I see th niggers steel it. I sed no, but I see them sneeking out of th room and husling away, and I never thaut nuthing, oenly I rekond thay was afraed thay had waekt up mi master and was trieing to get away befor he maed trubl with them. That was all thay askt me. Then th doctor wherls on me and sez:

“Ar u English, too?”

I sez yes; and him and sum uthers laft, and sed, “Stuf!”

Wel, then thay saeld in on th jeneral investigaeshun, and thair we had it, up and doun, our in, our out, and noebody never sed a werd about super, nor ever seemd to think about it—and so thay kept it up, and kept it up; and it was th werst mixt-up thing u ever see. Thay maed th king tel his yarn, and thay maed th oeld jentlman tel his’n; and enybody but a lot of prejudist chuckleheads wuud a seen that th oeld jentlman was spining trooth and t’uther wun lies. And bi and bi thay had me up to tel whut I knowed. Th king he giv me a left-handed luuk out of th corner of his ie, and so I knowed enuf to tauk on th riet sied. I begun to tel about Sheffield, and how we livd thair, and all about th English Wilkses, and so on; but I didn’t get prity fer til th doctor begun to laf; and Levi Bel, th lawyer, sez:

“Set doun, mi boy; I wouldn’t straen mieself if I was u. I rekon u ain’t uezd to lieing, it don’t seem to cum handy; whut u wont is practis. U do it prity aukward.”

I didn’t cair nuthing for th compliment, but I was glad to be let off, enyway.

Th doctor he started to say sumthing, and terns and sez:

“If u’d bin in toun at ferst, Levi Bel—” Th king broek in and reecht out his hand, and sez:

“Whi, is this mi pur ded bruther’s oeld frend that he’s roet so offen about?”

Th lawyer and him shuuk hands, and th lawyer smield and luukt pleezd, and thay taukt riet along awhiel, and then got to wun sied and taukt lo; and at last th lawyer speeks up and sez:

“That ’ll fix it. I’ll taek th order and send it, along with yur bruther’s, and then thay’ll noe it’s all riet.”

So thay got sum paeper and a pen, and th king he set doun and twisted his hed to wun sied, and chawed his tung, and scralld off sumthing; and then thay giv th pen to th duek—and then for th ferst tiem th duek luukt sik. But he tuuk th pen and roet. So then th lawyer terns to th nue oeld jentlman and sez:

“U and yur bruther pleez riet a lien or too and sien yur naems.”











Th oeld jentlman roet, but noebody couldn’t red it. Th lawyer luukt powerful astonisht, and sez:

“Wel, it beets me”—and snaekt a lot of oeld leters out of his poket, and examind them, and then examind th oeld man’s rieting, and then them agen; and then sez: “Thees oeld leters is frum Harvey Wilks; and heer’s thees too handwritings, and enybody can see thay didn’t riet them” (th king and th duek luukt soeld and foolish, I tel u, to see how th lawyer had tuuk them in), “and heer’s this oeld jentlman’s hand rieting, and enybody can tel, eezy enuf, he didn’t riet them—fact is, th scraches he maeks ain’t properly rieting at all. Now, heer’s sum leters frum—”

Th nue oeld jentlman sez:

“If u pleez, let me explaen. Noebody can red mi hand but mi bruther thair—so he copys for me. It’s his hand u’ve got thair, not mien.”

“Wel!” sez th lawyer, “this is a staet of things. I’ve got sum of William’s leters, too; so if u’ll get him to riet a lien or so we can com—”

“He can’t riet with his left hand,” sez th oeld jentlman. “If he cuud ues his riet hand, u wuud see that he roet his oen leters and mien too. Luuk at boeth, pleez—thay’re bi th saem hand.”

Th lawyer dun it, and sez:

“I beleev it’s so—and if it ain’t so, thair’s a heep strongger rezemblans than I’d noetist befor, enyway. Wel, wel, wel! I thaut we was riet on th trak of a solooshun, but it’s gon to gras, partly. But enyway, wun thing is proovd—thees too ain’t eether of ’em Wilkses”—and he wagd his hed tords th king and th duek.

Wel, whut do u think? That muleheaded oeld fool wouldn’t giv in then! Indeed he wouldn’t. Sed it worn’t no fair test. Sed his bruther William was th cussedest joeker in th werld, and hadn’t tried to riet—he see William was going to play wun of his joeks th minit he puut th pen to paeper. And so he wormd up and went worbling and worbling riet along til he was actuly begining to beleev whut he was saying himself; but prity soon th nue jentlman broek in, and sez:

“I’ve thaut of sumthing. Is thair enybody heer that helpt to lay out mi br—helpt to lay out th laet Peeter Wilks for berrying?”

“Yes,” sez sumbody, “me and Ab Terner dun it. We’re boeth heer.”

Then th oeld man terns tords th king, and sez:

“Perhaps this jentlman can tel me whut was tatood on his brest?”

Blaemd if th king didn’t hav to braes up miety qik, or he’d a squshed doun liek a bluf bank that th river has cut under, it tuuk him so suden; and, miend u, it was a thing that was calcuelaeted to maek moest enybody sqush to get fetched such a solid wun as that without eny noetis, becauz how was he going to noe whut was tatood on th man? He whietend a litl; he couldn’t help it; and it was miety stil in thair, and evrybody bending a litl forwards and gaezing at him. Sez I to mieself, now he’ll thro up th spunj—thair ain’t no mor ues. Wel, did he? A body can’t hardly beleev it, but he didn’t. I rekon he thaut he’d keep th thing up til he tierd them peepl out, so thay’d thin out, and him and th duek cuud braek loos and get away. Enyway, he set thair, and prity soon he begun to smiel, and sez:

“Mf! It’s a verry tuf qeschun, ain’t it! yes, ser, I k’n tel u whut’s tatood on his brest. It’s jest a small, thin, bloo arro—that’s whut it is; and if u don’t luuk clost, u can’t see it. now whut do u say—hay?”

Wel, I never see enything liek that oeld blister for cleen out-and-out cheek.

Th nue oeld jentlman terns brisk tords Ab Terner and his pard, and his ie liets up liek he jujd he’d got th king this tiem, and sez:

“Thair—u’ve herd whut he sed! Was thair eny such mark on Peeter Wilks’ brest?”

Boeth of them spoek up and sez:

“We didn’t see no such mark.”

“Guud!” sez th oeld jentlman. “Now, whut u did see on his brest was a small dim P, and a B (which is an inishal he dropt when he was yung), and a W, with dashes between them, so: P—B—W”—and he markt them that way on a pees of paeper. “Cum, ain’t that whut u saw?”

Boeth of them spoek up agen, and sez:

“No, we didn’t. We never seen eny marks at all.”

Wel, evrybody was in a staet of miend now, and thay sings out:

“Th hoel bilin’ of ’m ’s frauds! Le’s duk ’em! le’s droun ’em! le’s ried ’em on a rael!” and evrybody was hooping at wuns, and thair was a ratling powwow. But th lawyer he jumps on th taebl and yels, and sez:

“Jentlmen—jentlmen! Heer me just a werd—just a singgl werd—if u pleez! Thair’s wun way yet—let’s go and dig up th corps and luuk.”











That tuuk them.

“Hooray!” thay all shouted, and was starting riet off; but th lawyer and th doctor sung out:

“Hoeld on, hoeld on! Colar all thees foer men and th boy, and fech them along, too!”

“We’ll do it!” thay all shouted; “and if we don’t fiend them marks we’ll linch th hoel gang!”

I was scaird, now, I tel u. But thair worn’t no geting away, u noe. Thay gript us all, and marcht us riet along, straet for th graev-yard, which was a miel and a haf doun th river, and th hoel toun at our heels, for we maed noiz enuf, and it was oenly nien in th eevning.

As we went bi our hous I wisht I hadn’t sent Mary Jane out of toun; becauz now if I cuud tip her th wink she’d liet out and saev me, and blo on our ded-beets.

Wel, we swormd along doun th river roed, just carrying on liek wildcats; and to maek it mor scairy th skie was darking up, and th lietning begining to wink and fliter, and th wiend to shiver amungst th leevs. This was th moest awful trubl and moest dangersome I ever was in; and I was kiender stund; evrything was going so diferent frum whut I had alowd for; sted of being fixt so I cuud taek mi oen tiem if I wonted to, and see all th fun, and hav Mary Jane at mi bak to saev me and set me free when th cloez-fit cum, heer was nuthing in th werld betwixt me and suden deth but just them tatoo-marks. If thay didn’t fiend them—

I couldn’t bair to think about it; and yet, sumhow, I couldn’t think about nuthing els. It got darker and darker, and it was a buetiful tiem to giv th croud th slip; but that big husky had me bi th rist—Hines—and a body miet as wel tri to giv Goliar th slip. He dragd me riet along, he was so exsieted, and I had to run to keep up.

When thay got thair thay swormd into th graev-yard and wosht oever it liek an oeverflo. And when thay got to th graev thay found thay had about a hundred tiems as meny shuvels as thay wonted, but noebody hadn’t thaut to fech a lantern. But thay saeld into diging enyway bi th fliker of th lietning, and sent a man to th neerest hous, a haf a miel off, to borro wun.

So thay dug and dug liek evrything; and it got awful dark, and th raen started, and th wiend swisht and swushed along, and th lietning cum brisker and brisker, and th thunder boomd; but them peepl never tuuk no noetis of it, thay was so fuul of this biznes; and wun minit u cuud see evrything and evry faes in that big croud, and th shovelfuls of dert saeling up out of th graev, and th next second th dark wiept it all out, and u couldn’t see nuthing at all.

At last thay got out th coffin and begun to unscroo th lid, and then such anuther crouding and shoeldering and shuving as thair was, to scrouge in and get a siet, u never see; and in th dark, that way, it was awful. Hines he hert mi rist dredful puuling and tuging so, and I rekon he cleen forgot I was in th werld, he was so exsieted and panting.

All of a suden th lietning let go a perfect sloos of whiet glair, and sumbody sings out:

“Bi th living jingo, heer’s th bag of goeld on his brest!”

Hines let out a hoop, liek evrybody els, and dropt mi rist and giv a big serj to bust his way in and get a luuk, and th way I lit out and shinned for th roed in th dark thair ain’t noebody can tel.

I had th roed all to mieself, and I fairly floo—leastways, I had it all to mieself exsept th solid dark, and th now-and-then glairs, and th buzing of th raen, and th thrashing of th wiend, and th spliting of th thunder; and shur as u ar born I did clip it along!

When I struk th toun I see thair worn’t noebody out in th storm, so I never hunted for no bak streets, but humpt it straet thru th maen wun; and when I begun to get tords our hous I aemd mi ie and set it. No liet thair; th hous all dark—which maed me feel sorry and disapointed, I didn’t noe whi. But at last, just as I was saeling bi, flash cums th liet in Mary Jane’s windo! and mi hart sweld up suden, liek to bust; and th saem second th hous and all was behiend me in th dark, and wasn’t ever going to be befor me no mor in this werld. She was th best gerl I ever see, and had th moest sand.

Th minit I was far enuf abuv th toun to see I cuud maek th toehed, I begun to luuk sharp for a boet to borro, and th ferst tiem th lietning shoed me wun that wasn’t chained I snacht it and shuvd. It was a canoo, and worn’t fasend with nuthing but a roep. Th toehed was a ratling big distans off, away out thair in th midl of th river, but I didn’t looz no tiem; and when I struk th raft at last I was so fagd I wuud a just laed doun to blo and gasp if I cuud aforded it. But I didn’t. As I sprung abord I sung out:

“Out with u, Jim, and set her loos! Glory be to guudnes, we’re shut of them!”











Jim lit out, and was a-cuming for me with boeth arms spred, he was so fuul of joy; but when I glimpst him in th lietning mi hart shot up in mi mouth and I went oeverbord bakwards; for I forgot he was oeld King Lear and a drownded A-rab all in wun, and it moest scaird th livers and liets out of me. But Jim fished me out, and was going to hug me and bles me, and so on, he was so glad I was bak and we was shut of th king and th duek, but I sez:

“Not now; hav it for brekfast, hav it for brekfast! Cut loos and let her slied!”

So in too seconds away we went a-slieding doun th river, and it did seem so guud to be free agen and all bi ourselvs on th big river, and noebody to bother us. I had to skip around a bit, and jump up and crak mi heels a fue tiems—I couldn’t help it; but about th therd crak I noetist a sound that I knowed miety wel, and held mi breth and lisend and waeted; and shur enuf, when th next flash busted out oever th wauter, heer thay cum!—and just a-laying to thair ors and maeking thair skif hum! It was th king and th duek.

So I wilted riet doun on to th planks then, and giv up; and it was all I cuud do to keep frum crieing.














CHAPTER XXX.

When thay got abord th king went for me, and shuuk me bi th colar, and sez:

“Tryin’ to giv us th slip, was ye, u pup! Tierd of our cumpany, hay?”

I sez:

“No, yur majesty, we worn’t—pleez don’t, yur majesty!”

“Qik, then, and tel us whut was yur iedeea, or I’ll shaek th insieds out o’ u!”

“Onest, I’ll tel u evrything just as it hapend, yur majesty. Th man that had a-holt of me was verry guud to me, and kept saying he had a boy about as big as me that died last yeer, and he was sorry to see a boy in such a daenjerus fix; and when thay was all tuuk bi serpriez bi fiending th goeld, and maed a rush for th coffin, he lets go of me and whispers, ‘Heel it now, or thay’ll hang ye, shur!’ and I lit out. It didn’t seem no guud for me to stay—I couldn’t do nuthing, and I didn’t wont to be hung if I cuud get away. So I never stopt runing til I found th canoo; and when I got heer I toeld Jim to hery, or thay’d cach me and hang me yet, and sed I was afeard u and th duek wasn’t aliev now, and I was awful sorry, and so was Jim, and was awful glad when we see u cuming; u may ask Jim if I didn’t.”

Jim sed it was so; and th king toeld him to shut up, and sed, “O, yes, it’s miety liekly!” and shuuk me up agen, and sed he rekond he’d drownd me. But th duek sez:

“Leggo th boy, u oeld idiot! Wuud u a dun eny diferent? Did u inqier around for him when u got loos? I don’t remember it.”

So th king let go of me, and begun to cuss that toun and evrybody in it. But th duek sez:

“U beter a blaem’ siet giv yurself a guud cussing, for u’re th wun that’s entietld to it moest. U hain’t dun a thing frum th start that had eny sens in it, exsept cuming out so cool and cheeky with that imajinairy bloo-arro mark. That was briet—it was riet doun buuly; and it was th thing that saevd us. For if it hadn’t bin for that thay’d a jaeld us til them Englishmen’s bagej cum—and then—th penitenshery, u bet! But that trik tuuk ’em to th graev-yard, and th goeld dun us a stil biger kiendnes; for if th exsieted fools hadn’t let go all holts and maed that rush to get a luuk we’d a slept in our cravats to-niet—cravats waranted to wair, too—longger than we’d need ’em.”

Thay was stil a minit—thinking; then th king sez, kiend of absent-miended liek:

“Mf! And we rekond th niggers stoel it!”

That maed me sqerm!

“Yes,” sez th duek, kiender slo and deliberaet and sarcastic, “we did.”

After about a haf a minit th king drawls out:

“Leastways, I did.”

Th duek sez, th saem way:

“On th contrairy, I did.”

Th king kiend of rufls up, and sez:

“Luuky heer, Bilgewater, whut’r u referrin’ to?”

Th duek sez, prity brisk:

“When it cums to that, maybe u’ll let me ask, whut was u refering to?”

“Shuks!” sez th king, verry sarcastic; “but I don’t noe—maybe u was asleep, and didn’t noe whut u was about.”

Th duek brisls up now, and sez:

“O, let up on this cussed nonsens; do u taek me for a blaem’ fool? Don’t u rekon I noe hoo hid that muny in that coffin?”

“Yes, ser! I noe u do noe, becauz u dun it yurself!”

“It’s a lie!”—and th duek went for him. Th king sings out:

“Taek y’r hands off!—leggo mi throet!—I taek it all bak!”











Th duek sez:

“Wel, u just oen up, ferst, that u did hied that muny thair, intending to giv me th slip wun of thees days, and cum bak and dig it up, and hav it all to yurself.”

“Waet jest a minit, duek—anser me this wun qeschun, onest and fair; if u didn’t puut th muny thair, say it, and I’ll b’lieve u, and taek bak evrything I sed.”

“U oeld scoundrel, I didn’t, and u noe I didn’t. Thair, now!”

“Wel, then, I b’lieve u. But anser me oenly jest this wun mor—now don’t git mad; didn’t u hav it in yur miend to huuk th muny and hied it?”

Th duek never sed nuthing for a litl bit; then he sez:

“Wel, I don’t cair if I did, I didn’t do it, enyway. But u not oenly had it in miend to do it, but u dun it.”

“I wisht I never die if I dun it, duek, and that’s onest. I wun’t say I worn’t goin’ to do it, becauz I was; but u—I meen sumbody—got in ahed o’ me.”

“It’s a lie! U dun it, and u got to say u dun it, or—”

Th king began to gergl, and then he gasps out:

“’Nough!—I oen up!”

I was verry glad to heer him say that; it maed me feel much mor eezyer than whut I was feeling befor. So th duek tuuk his hands off and sez:

“If u ever deni it agen I’ll droun u. It’s wel for u to set thair and bluber liek a baeby—it’s fitten for u, after th way u’ve acted. I never see such an oeld ostrich for wonting to gobl evrything—and I a-trusting u all th tiem, liek u was mi oen faather. U aut to bin ashaemd of yurself to stand bi and heer it sadld on to a lot of pur niggers, and u never say a werd for ’em. It maeks me feel ridicuelus to think I was sofft enuf to beleev that rubbage. Cuss u, I can see now whi u was so ankshus to maek up th deffisit—u wonted to get whut muny I’d got out of th Nonesuch and wun thing or anuther, and scoop it all!”

Th king sez, timid, and stil a-snuffling:

“Whi, duek, it was u that sed maek up th deffisit; it worn’t me.”

“Dri up! I don’t wont to heer no mor out of u!” sez th duek. “And now u see whut u GOT bi it. Thay’ve got all thair oen muny bak, and all of ourn but a shekel or too besieds. G’long to bed, and don’t u deffersit me no mor deffersits, long ’s u liv!”

So th king sneekt into th wigwom and tuuk to his botl for cumfort, and befor long th duek takld HIS botl; and so in about a haf an our thay was as thik as theevs agen, and th tieter thay got th lovinger thay got, and went off a-snoring in eech uther’s arms. Thay boeth got powerful melo, but I noetist th king didn’t get melo enuf to forget to remember to not deni about hieding th muny-bag agen. That maed me feel eezy and satisfied. Of cors when thay got to snoring we had a long gabl, and I toeld Jim evrything.














CHAPTER XXXI.

We dasn’t stop agen at eny toun for days and days; kept riet along doun th river. We was doun south in th worm wether now, and a miety long ways frum hoem. We begun to cum to trees with Spanish moss on them, hanging doun frum th lims liek long, gray beerds. It was th ferst I ever see it groeing, and it maed th wuuds luuk solem and dizmal. So now th frauds rekond thay was out of daenjer, and thay begun to werk th vilejes agen.

Ferst thay dun a lekcher on temperans; but thay didn’t maek enuf for them boeth to get drunk on. Then in anuther vilej thay started a dansing-scool; but thay didn’t noe no mor how to dans than a kangaroo duz; so th ferst prans thay maed th jeneral public jumpt in and pranced them out of toun. Anuther tiem thay tried to go at yellocution; but thay didn’t yellocute long til th audyens got up and giv them a solid guud cussing, and maed them skip out. Thay takld missionarying, and mesmerizing, and doctoring, and teling forchuns, and a litl of evrything; but thay couldn’t seem to hav no luk. So at last thay got just about ded broek, and laed around th raft as she floeted along, thinking and thinking, and never saying nuthing, bi th haf a day at a tiem, and dredful bloo and desperet.

And at last thay tuuk a chaenj and begun to lay thair heds together in th wigwom and tauk lo and confidenshal too or three ours at a tiem. Jim and me got uneezy. We didn’t liek th luuk of it. We jujd thay was studying up sum kiend of wers deviltry than ever. We ternd it oever and oever, and at last we maed up our miends thay was going to braek into sumbody’s hous or stor, or was going into th counterfit-muny biznes, or sumthing. So then we was prity scaird, and maed up an agreement that we wouldn’t hav nuthing in th werld to do with such acshuns, and if we ever got th leest sho we wuud giv them th coeld shaek and cleer out and leev them behiend. Wel, erly wun morning we hid th raft in a guud, saef plaes about too miel belo a litl bit of a shaby vilej naemd Pikesville, and th king he went ashor and toeld us all to stay hid whilst he went up to toun and smelt around to see if enybody had got eny wiend of th Royal Nonesuch thair yet. (“Hous to rob, u meen,” sez I to mieself; “and when u get thru robing it u’ll cum bak heer and wunder whut has becum of me and Jim and th raft—and u’ll hav to taek it out in wundering.”) And he sed if he worn’t bak bi midday th duek and me wuud noe it was all riet, and we was to cum along.

So we stayd whair we was. Th duek he freted and sweted around, and was in a miety sour way. He scoelded us for evrything, and we couldn’t seem to do nuthing riet; he found fallt with evry litl thing. Sumthing was a-brooing, shur. I was guud and glad when midday cum and no king; we cuud hav a chaenj, enyway—and maybe a chans for th chaenj on top of it. So me and th duek went up to th vilej, and hunted around thair for th king, and bi and bi we found him in th bak room of a litl lo doggery, verry tiet, and a lot of loefers bullyragging him for sport, and he a-cussing and a-thretening with all his miet, and so tiet he couldn’t wauk, and couldn’t do nuthing to them. Th duek he begun to abues him for an oeld fool, and th king begun to sass bak, and th minit thay was fairly at it I lit out and shuuk th reefs out of mi hiend legs, and spun doun th river roed liek a deer, for I see our chans; and I maed up mi miend that it wuud be a long day befor thay ever see me and Jim agen. I got doun thair all out of breth but loeded up with joy, and sung out:

“Set her loos, Jim! we’re all riet now!”

But thair worn’t no anser, and noebody cum out of th wigwom. Jim was gon! I set up a shout—and then anuther—and then anuther wun; and run this way and that in th wuuds, hooping and screeching; but it worn’t no ues—oeld Jim was gon. Then I set doun and cried; I couldn’t help it. But I couldn’t set stil long. Prity soon I went out on th roed, trieing to think whut I beter do, and I run across a boy wauking, and askt him if he’d seen a straenj nigger drest so and so, and he sez:

“Yes.”

“Whairabouts?” sez I.

“Doun to Silas Phelps’ plaes, too miel belo heer. He’s a runaway nigger, and thay’ve got him. Was u luuking for him?”

“U bet I ain’t! I run across him in th wuuds about an our or too ago, and he sed if I holerd he’d cut mi livers out—and toeld me to lay doun and stay whair I was; and I dun it. Bin thair ever sinss; afeard to cum out.”

“Wel,” he sez, “u needn’t be afeard no mor, becuz thay’ve got him. He run off f’m doun South, som’ers.”

“It’s a guud job thay got him.”

“Wel, I rekon! Thair’s too hunderd dolars reword on him. It’s liek piking up muny out’n th roed.”

“Yes, it is—and I cuud a had it if I’d bin big enuf; I see him ferst. Hoo naeld him?”











“It was an oeld felo—a straenjer—and he soeld out his chans in him for forty dolars, becuz he’s got to go up th river and can’t waet. Think o’ that, now! U bet I’d waet, if it was seven yeer.”

“That’s me, evry tiem,” sez I. “But maybe his chans ain’t werth no mor than that, if he’ll sel it so cheep. Maybe thair’s sumthing ain’t straet about it.”

“But it is, tho—straet as a string. I see th handbil mieself. It tels all about him, to a dot—paents him liek a pikcher, and tels th plantaeshun he’s frum, belo Newrleens. No-sirree-bob, thay ain’t no trubl ’bout that specuelaeshun, u bet u. Say, gimme a chaw tobacker, wun’t ye?”

I didn’t hav nun, so he left. I went to th raft, and set doun in th wigwom to think. But I couldn’t cum to nuthing. I thaut til I wor mi hed sor, but I couldn’t see no way out of th trubl. After all this long jerny, and after all we’d dun for them scoundrels, heer it was all cum to nuthing, evrything all busted up and rooind, becauz thay cuud hav th hart to serv Jim such a trik as that, and maek him a slaev agen all his lief, and amungst straenjers, too, for forty derty dolars.

Wuns I sed to mieself it wuud be a thouzand tiems beter for Jim to be a slaev at hoem whair his family was, as long as he’d got to be a slaev, and so I’d beter riet a leter to Tom Sawyer and tel him to tel Mis Watson whair he was. But I soon giv up that noeshun for too things: she’d be mad and disgusted at his rascality and ungratefulness for leeving her, and so she’d sel him straet doun th river agen; and if she didn’t, evrybody nacheraly despiezes an ungraetful nigger, and thay’d maek Jim feel it all th tiem, and so he’d feel ornery and disgraest. And then think of me! It wuud get all around that Huck Finn helpt a nigger to get his freedom; and if I was ever to see enybody frum that toun agen I’d be redy to get doun and lik his boots for shaem. That’s just th way: a person duz a lo-doun thing, and then he don’t wont to taek no conseqenses of it. Thinks as long as he can hied it, it ain’t no disgraes. That was mi fix exactly. Th mor I studyd about this th mor mi conshens went to griending me, and th mor wiked and lo-doun and ornery I got to feeling. And at last, when it hit me all of a suden that heer was th plaen hand of Providens slaping me in th faes and leting me noe mi wikednes was being wocht all th tiem frum up thair in heven, whilst I was steeling a pur oeld wuuman’s nigger that hadn’t ever dun me no harm, and now was shoeing me thair’s Wun that’s allways on th luukout, and ain’t a-going to alow no such mizerabl doings to go oenly just so fer and no ferther, I moest dropt in mi traks I was so scaird. Wel, I tried th best I cuud to kiender soffen it up sumhow for mieself bi saying I was brung up wiked, and so I worn’t so much to blaem; but sumthing insied of me kept saying, “Thair was th Sunday-scool, u cuud a gon to it; and if u’d a dun it thay’d a learnt u thair that peepl that acts as I’d bin acting about that nigger goes to everlasting fier.”

It maed me shiver. And I about maed up mi miend to pray, and see if I couldn’t tri to qit being th kiend of a boy I was and be beter. So I neeld doun. But th werds wouldn’t cum. Whi wouldn’t thay? It worn’t no ues to tri and hied it frum Him. Nor frum me, neether. I knowed verry wel whi thay wouldn’t cum. It was becauz mi hart worn’t riet; it was becauz I worn’t sqair; it was becauz I was playing dubl. I was leting on to giv up sin, but away insied of me I was hoelding on to th bigest wun of all. I was trieing to maek mi mouth say I wuud do th riet thing and th cleen thing, and go and riet to that nigger’s oener and tel whair he was; but deep doun in me I knowed it was a lie, and He knowed it. U can’t pray a lie—I found that out.

So I was fuul of trubl, fuul as I cuud be; and didn’t noe whut to do. At last I had an iedeea; and I sez, I’ll go and riet th leter—and then see if I can pray. Whi, it was astonishing, th way I felt as liet as a fether riet straet off, and mi trubls all gon. So I got a pees of paeper and a pensil, all glad and exsieted, and set doun and roet:

Mis Watson, yur runaway nigger Jim is doun heer too miel belo Pikesville, and Mr. Phelps has got him and he wil giv him up for th reword if u send.

Huck Finn.











I felt guud and all wosht cleen of sin for th ferst tiem I had ever felt so in mi lief, and I knowed I cuud pray now. But I didn’t do it straet off, but laed th paeper doun and set thair thinking—thinking how guud it was all this hapend so, and how neer I cum to being lost and going to hel. And went on thinking. And got to thinking oever our trip doun th river; and I see Jim befor me all th tiem: in th day and in th niet-tiem, sumtiems moonliet, sumtiems storms, and we a-floeting along, tauking and singing and lafing. But sumhow I couldn’t seem to striek no plaeses to harden me agenst him, but oenly th uther kiend. I’d see him standing mi woch on top of his’n, ’sted of calling me, so I cuud go on sleeping; and see him how glad he was when I cum bak out of th fog; and when I cum to him agen in th swomp, up thair whair th fued was; and such-liek tiems; and wuud allways call me huny, and pet me and do evrything he cuud think of for me, and how guud he allways was; and at last I struk th tiem I saevd him bi teling th men we had small-pox abord, and he was so graetful, and sed I was th best frend oeld Jim ever had in th werld, and th oenly wun he’s got now; and then I hapend to luuk around and see that paeper.

It was a cloez plaes. I tuuk it up, and held it in mi hand. I was a-trembling, becauz I’d got to desied, forever, betwixt too things, and I knowed it. I studyd a minit, sort of hoelding mi breth, and then sez to mieself:

“All riet, then, I’ll go to hel”—and tore it up.

It was awful thauts and awful werds, but thay was sed. And I let them stay sed; and never thaut no mor about reforming. I shuvd th hoel thing out of mi hed, and sed I wuud taek up wikednes agen, which was in mi lien, being brung up to it, and th uther worn’t. And for a starter I wuud go to werk and steel Jim out of slaevery agen; and if I cuud think up enything wers, I wuud do that, too; becauz as long as I was in, and in for guud, I miet as wel go th hoel hog.

Then I set to thinking oever how to get at it, and ternd oever sum considerabl meny ways in mi miend; and at last fixt up a plan that sooted me. So then I tuuk th bairings of a woody ieland that was doun th river a pees, and as soon as it was fairly dark I crept out with mi raft and went for it, and hid it thair, and then ternd in. I slept th niet thru, and got up befor it was liet, and had mi brekfast, and puut on mi stor cloeths, and tied up sum uthers and wun thing or anuther in a bundl, and tuuk th canoo and cleerd for shor. I landed belo whair I jujd was Phelps’s plaes, and hid mi bundl in th wuuds, and then fild up th canoo with wauter, and loeded roks into her and sunk her whair I cuud fiend her agen when I wonted her, about a qorter of a miel belo a litl steem sawmil that was on th bank.

Then I struk up th roed, and when I past th mil I see a sien on it, “Phelps’s Sawmil,” and when I cum to th farm-houses, too or three hundred yards ferther along, I kept mi ies peeld, but didn’t see noebody around, tho it was guud dayliet now. But I didn’t miend, becauz I didn’t wont to see noebody just yet—I oenly wonted to get th lay of th land. Acording to mi plan, I was going to tern up thair frum th vilej, not frum belo. So I just tuuk a luuk, and shuvd along, straet for toun. Wel, th verry ferst man I see when I got thair was th duek. He was stiking up a bil for th Royal Nonesuch—three-niet performans—liek that uther tiem. Thay had th cheek, them frauds! I was riet on him befor I cuud sherk. He luukt astonisht, and sez:

“Hel-lo! Whair’d u cum frum?” Then he sez, kiend of glad and eeger, “Whair’s th raft?—got her in a guud plaes?”

I sez:

“Whi, that’s just whut I was going to ask yur graes.”

Then he didn’t luuk so joyful, and sez:

“Whut was yur iedeea for asking me?” he sez.

“Wel,” I sez, “when I see th king in that doggery yesterday I sez to mieself, we can’t get him hoem for ours, til he’s soberer; so I went a-loafing around toun to puut in th tiem and waet. A man up and offerd me ten sents to help him puul a skif oever th river and bak to fech a sheep, and so I went along; but when we was draging him to th boet, and th man left me a-holt of th roep and went behiend him to shuv him along, he was too strong for me and jerkt loos and run, and we after him. We didn’t hav no daug, and so we had to chaes him all oever th cuntry til we tierd him out. We never got him til dark; then we fetched him oever, and I started doun for th raft. When I got thair and see it was gon, I sez to mieself, ’Thay’ve got into trubl and had to leev; and thay’ve tuuk mi nigger, which is th oenly nigger I’ve got in th werld, and now I’m in a straenj cuntry, and ain’t got no property no mor, nor nuthing, and no way to maek mi living;’ so I set doun and cried. I slept in th wuuds all niet. But whut did becum of th raft, then?—and Jim—pur Jim!”

“Blaemd if I noe—that is, whut’s becum of th raft. That oeld fool had maed a traed and got forty dolars, and when we found him in th doggery th loefers had macht haf-dolars with him and got evry sent but whut he’d spent for whisky; and when I got him hoem laet last niet and found th raft gon, we sed, ‘That litl rascal has stoel our raft and shuuk us, and run off doun th river.’”

“I wouldn’t shaek mi nigger, wuud I?—th oenly nigger I had in th werld, and th oenly property.”

“We never thaut of that. Fact is, I rekon we’d cum to consider him our nigger; yes, we did consider him so—guudnes noes we had trubl enuf for him.
