Then Tom markt out them things on it with th nael, and set Jim to werk on them, with th nael for a chizel and an ieern boelt frum th rubbage in th leen-to for a hamer, and toeld him to werk til th rest of his candl qit on him, and then he cuud go to bed, and hied th griendstoen under his straw tik and sleep on it. Then we helpt him fix his chaen bak on th bed-leg, and was redy for bed ourselvs. But Tom thaut of sumthing, and sez:

“U got eny spieders in heer, Jim?”

“No, sah, thanks to guudnes I hain’t, Mars Tom.”

“All riet, we’ll get u sum.”

“But bles u, huny, I doan’ wont nun. I’s afeard un um. I jis’ ’s soon hav ratlsnaeks aroun’.”

Tom thaut a minit or too, and sez:

“It’s a guud iedeea. And I rekon it’s bin dun. It must a bin dun; it stands to reezon. Yes, it’s a priem guud iedeea. Whair cuud u keep it?”

“Keep whut, Mars Tom?”

“Whi, a ratlsnaek.”

“De guudnes graeshus aliev, Mars Tom! Whi, if day was a ratlsnaek to cum in heah I’d taek en bust riet out thoo dat log wall, I wuud, wid mi hed.”

“Whi, Jim, u wouldn’t be afraed of it after a litl. U cuud taem it.”

“Taem it!”

“Yes—eezy enuf. Evry animal is graetful for kiendnes and peting, and thay wouldn’t think of herting a person that pets them. Eny buuk wil tel u that. U tri—that’s all I ask; just tri for too or three days. Whi, u can get him so, in a litl whiel, that he’ll luv u; and sleep with u; and wun’t stay away frum u a minit; and wil let u rap him round yur nek and puut his hed in yur mouth.”

“Pleez, Mars Tom—doan’ tauk so! I can’t stan’ it! He’d let me shuv his hed in mi mouf—fer a faevor, hain’t it? I lay he’d waet a pow’ful long tiem ’fo’ I ast him. En mo’ en dat, I doan’ wont him to sleep wid me.”

“Jim, don’t act so foolish. A prizoner’s got to hav sum kiend of a dum pet, and if a ratlsnaek hain’t ever bin tried, whi, thair’s mor glory to be gaend in yur being th ferst to ever tri it than eny uther way u cuud ever think of to saev yur lief.”

“Whi, Mars Tom, I doan’ wont no sich glory. Snaek taek ’n biet Jim’s chin off, den whah is de glory? No, sah, I doan’ wont no sich doin’s.”

“Blaem it, can’t u tri? I oenly wont u to tri—u needn’t keep it up if it don’t werk.”

“But de trubl all dun ef de snaek biet me whiel I’s a tryin’ him. Mars Tom, I’s willin’ to takl mos’ enything ’at ain’t onreasonable, but ef u en Huck fetches a ratlsnaek in heah for me to taem, I’s gwyne to leev, dat’s shor.”

“Wel, then, let it go, let it go, if u’re so buul-heded about it. We can get u sum garter-snaeks, and u can tee sum butons on thair taels, and let on thay’re ratlsnaeks, and I rekon that ’ll hav to do.”











“I k’n stan’ dem, Mars Tom, but blaem’ ’f I couldn’ get along widout um, I tel u dat. I never knowed b’fo’ ’t was so much bother and trubl to be a prizoner.”

“Wel, it allways is when it’s dun riet. U got eny rats around heer?”

“No, sah, I hain’t seed nun.”

“Wel, we’ll get u sum rats.”

“Whi, Mars Tom, I doan’ wont no rats. Day’s de dadblamedest creturs to ’sturb a body, en rusl roun’ oever ’im, en biet his feet, when he’s tryin’ to sleep, I ever see. No, sah, gimme g’yarter-snaeks, ’f I’s got to hav ’m, but doan’ gimme no rats; I hain’ got no ues f’r um, skasely.”

“But, Jim, u got to hav ’em—thay all do. So don’t maek no mor fus about it. Prizoners ain’t ever without rats. Thair ain’t no instans of it. And thay traen them, and pet them, and lern them triks, and thay get to be as soeshabl as flies. But u got to play muezic to them. U got enything to play muezic on?”

“I ain’ got nuffn but a coase coem en a pees o’ paeper, en a joos-harp; but I reck’n day wouldn’ taek no stok in a joos-harp.”

“Yes thay wuud thay don’t cair whut kiend of muezic ’tis. A jews-harp’s plenty guud enuf for a rat. All animals liek muezic—in a prizon thay dote on it. Speshaly, paenful muezic; and u can’t get no uther kiend out of a jews-harp. It allways interests them; thay cum out to see whut’s th mater with u. Yes, u’re all riet; u’re fixt verry wel. U wont to set on yur bed niets befor u go to sleep, and erly in th mornings, and play yur jews-harp; play ‘Th Last Link is Broeken’—that’s th thing that ’ll scoop a rat qiker ’n enything els; and when u’ve playd about too minits u’ll see all th rats, and th snaeks, and spieders, and things begin to feel weryd about u, and cum. And thay’ll just fairly sworm oever u, and hav a noebl guud tiem.”

“Yes, day wil, I reck’n, Mars Tom, but whut kine er tiem is Jim havin’? Blest if I kin see de pient. But I’ll do it ef I got to. I reck’n I beter keep de animals satisfied, en not hav no trubl in de hous.”

Tom waeted to think it oever, and see if thair wasn’t nuthing els; and prity soon he sez:

“O, thair’s wun thing I forgot. Cuud u raez a flower heer, do u rekon?”

“I doan noe but maybe I cuud, Mars Tom; but it’s tolable dark in heah, en I ain’ got no ues f’r no flower, nohow, en she’d be a pow’ful siet o’ trubl.”

“Wel, u tri it, enyway. Sum uther prizoners has dun it.”

“Wun er dem big cat-tael-lookin’ mullen-stauks wuud gro in heah, Mars Tom, I reck’n, but she wouldn’t be wuth haf de trubl she’d coss.”

“Don’t u beleev it. We’ll fech u a litl wun and u plant it in th corner oever thair, and raez it. And don’t call it mullen, call it Pitchiola—that’s its riet naem when it’s in a prizon. And u wont to wauter it with yur teers.”

“Whi, I got plenty spring wauter, Mars Tom.”

“U don’t wont spring wauter; u wont to wauter it with yur teers. It’s th way thay allways do.”

“Whi, Mars Tom, I lay I kin raez wun er dem mullen-stauks twyste wid spring wauter whiles anuther man’s a start’n wun wid teers.”











“That ain’t th iedeea. U got to do it with teers.”

“She’ll die on mi han’s, Mars Tom, she sholy wil; kase I doan’ skasely ever cri.”

So Tom was stumpt. But he studyd it oever, and then sed Jim wuud hav to wery along th best he cuud with an unyon. He promist he wuud go to th nigger cabins and drop wun, prievet, in Jim’s coffy-pot, in th morning. Jim sed he wuud “jis’ ’s soon hav tobacker in his coffy;” and found so much fallt with it, and with th werk and bother of raezing th mullen, and jews-harping th rats, and peting and flatering up th snaeks and spieders and things, on top of all th uther werk he had to do on pens, and inscripshuns, and jernals, and things, which maed it mor trubl and wery and responsibility to be a prizoner than enything he ever undertuuk, that Tom moest lost all paeshens with him; and sed he was just loadened doun with mor gaudier chanses than a prizoner ever had in th werld to maek a naem for himself, and yet he didn’t noe enuf to apreeshiaet them, and thay was just about waested on him. So Jim he was sorry, and sed he wouldn’t behaev so no mor, and then me and Tom shuvd for bed.














CHAPTER XXXIX.

In th morning we went up to th vilej and baut a wier rat-trap and fetched it doun, and unstopped th best rat-hoel, and in about an our we had fifteen of th bulliest kiend of wuns; and then we tuuk it and puut it in a saef plaes under Ant Sally’s bed. But whiel we was gon for spieders litl Thomas Franklin Benjamin Jefferson Elexander Phelps found it thair, and oepend th dor of it to see if th rats wuud cum out, and thay did; and Ant Sally she cum in, and when we got bak she was a-standing on top of th bed raezing Cain, and th rats was doing whut thay cuud to keep off th dul tiems for her. So she tuuk and dusted us boeth with th hickry, and we was as much as too ours caching anuther fifteen or sixteen, drat that medlsum cub, and thay worn’t th likeliest, nuther, becauz th ferst hall was th pik of th flok. I never see a likelier lot of rats than whut that ferst hall was.

We got a splendid stok of sorted spieders, and bugs, and frogs, and caterpilars, and wun thing or anuther; and we liek to got a hornet’s nest, but we didn’t. Th family was at hoem. We didn’t giv it riet up, but stayd with them as long as we cuud; becauz we alowd we’d tier them out or thay’d got to tier us out, and thay dun it. Then we got allycumpain and rubd on th plaeses, and was prity neer all riet agen, but couldn’t set doun conveenyunt. And so we went for th snaeks, and grabd a cupl of duzen garters and hous-snaeks, and puut them in a bag, and puut it in our room, and bi that tiem it was super-tiem, and a ratling guud onest day’s werk: and hunggry?—o, no, I rekon not! And thair worn’t a blest snaek up thair when we went bak—we didn’t haf tee th sak, and thay werkt out sumhow, and left. But it didn’t mater much, becauz thay was stil on th premises somewheres. So we jujd we cuud get sum of them agen. No, thair worn’t no reeal scairsity of snaeks about th hous for a considerabl spel. U’d see them driping frum th rafters and plaeses evry now and then; and thay generly landed in yur plaet, or doun th bak of yur nek, and moest of th tiem whair u didn’t wont them. Wel, thay was hansum and striept, and thair worn’t no harm in a milyon of them; but that never maed no diferens to Ant Sally; she despiezd snaeks, be th breed whut thay miet, and she couldn’t stand them no way u cuud fix it; and evry tiem wun of them flopt doun on her, it didn’t maek no diferens whut she was doing, she wuud just lay that werk doun and liet out. I never see such a wuuman. And u cuud heer her hoop to Jericho. U couldn’t get her to taek a-holt of wun of them with th tongs. And if she ternd oever and found wun in bed she wuud scrambl out and lift a houl that u wuud think th hous was afier. She disterbd th oeld man so that he sed he cuud moest wish thair hadn’t ever bin no snaeks creaeted. Whi, after evry last snaek had bin gon cleer out of th hous for as much as a week Ant Sally worn’t oever it yet; she worn’t neer oever it; when she was seting thinking about sumthing u cuud tuch her on th bak of her nek with a fether and she wuud jump riet out of her stokings. It was verry cuerius. But Tom sed all wimen was just so. He sed thay was maed that way for sum reezon or uther.

We got a liking evry tiem wun of our snaeks cum in her way, and she alowd thees lickings worn’t nuthing to whut she wuud do if we ever loeded up th plaes agen with them. I didn’t miend th lickings, becauz thay didn’t amount to nuthing; but I miended th trubl we had to lay in anuther lot. But we got them laed in, and all th uther things; and u never see a cabin as bliethsum as Jim’s was when thay’d all sworm out for muezic and go for him. Jim didn’t liek th spieders, and th spieders didn’t liek Jim; and so thay’d lay for him, and maek it miety worm for him. And he sed that between th rats and th snaeks and th griendstoen thair worn’t no room in bed for him, skasely; and when thair was, a body couldn’t sleep, it was so lievly, and it was allways lievly, he sed, becauz thay never all slept at wun tiem, but tuuk tern about, so when th snaeks was asleep th rats was on dek, and when th rats ternd in th snaeks cum on woch, so he allways had wun gang under him, in his way, and t’uther gang having a sercus oever him, and if he got up to hunt a nue plaes th spieders wuud taek a chans at him as he crosst oever. He sed if he ever got out this tiem he wouldn’t ever be a prizoner agen, not for a salary.

Wel, bi th end of three weeks evrything was in prity guud shaep. Th shert was sent in erly, in a pi, and evry tiem a rat bit Jim he wuud get up and riet a litl in his jernal whilst th ink was fresh; th pens was maed, th inscripshuns and so on was all carvd on th griendstoen; th bed-leg was sawd in too, and we had et up th sawdust, and it giv us a moest amaezing stumac-aek. We rekond we was all going to die, but didn’t. It was th moest undigestible sawdust I ever see; and Tom sed th saem.











But as I was saying, we’d got all th werk dun now, at last; and we was all prity much fagd out, too, but maenly Jim. Th oeld man had roet a cupl of tiems to th plantaeshun belo Orleans to cum and get thair runaway nigger, but hadn’t got no anser, becauz thair worn’t no such plantaeshun; so he alowd he wuud advertiez Jim in th St. Louis and Nue Orleans paepers; and when he menshund th St. Louis wuns it giv me th coeld shivers, and I see we hadn’t no tiem to looz. So Tom sed, now for th nonnamous leters.

“Whut’s them?” I sez.

“Wornings to th peepl that sumthing is up. Sumtiems it’s dun wun way, sumtiems anuther. But thair’s allways sumbody spieing around that givs noetis to th guvernor of th casl. When Louis XVI. was going to liet out of th Tooleries, a servant-gerl dun it. It’s a verry guud way, and so is th nonnamous leters. We’ll ues them boeth. And it’s uezhual for th prizoner’s muther to chaenj cloeths with him, and she stays in, and he slieds out in her cloeths. We’ll do that, too.”

“But luuky heer, Tom, whut do we wont to worn enybody for that sumthing’s up? Let them fiend it out for themselvs—it’s thair luukout.”

“Yes, I noe; but u can’t depend on them. It’s th way thay’ve acted frum th verry start—left us to do evrything. Thay’re so confieding and mulet-heded thay don’t taek noetis of nuthing at all. So if we don’t giv them noetis thair wun’t be noebody nor nuthing to interfeer with us, and so after all our hard werk and trubl this escaep ’ll go off perfectly flat; wun’t amount to nuthing—wun’t be nuthing to it.”

“Wel, as for me, Tom, that’s th way I’d liek.”

“Shuks!” he sez, and luukt disgusted. So I sez:

“But I ain’t going to maek no complaent. Eny way that soots u soots me. Whut u going to do about th servant-gerl?”

“U’ll be her. U slied in, in th midl of th niet, and huuk that yaller gerl’s frok.”

“Whi, Tom, that ’ll maek trubl next morning; becauz, of cors, she prob’bly hain’t got eny but that wun.”

“I noe; but u don’t wont it but fifteen minits, to carry th nonnamous leter and shuv it under th frunt dor.”

“All riet, then, I’ll do it; but I cuud carry it just as handy in mi oen togs.”

“U wouldn’t luuk liek a servant-gerl then, wuud u?”

“No, but thair wun’t be noebody to see whut I luuk liek, enyway.”

“That ain’t got nuthing to do with it. Th thing for us to do is just to do our duety, and not wery about whether enybody sees us do it or not. Hain’t u got no prinsipl at all?”

“All riet, I ain’t saying nuthing; I’m th servant-gerl. Hoo’s Jim’s muther?”

“I’m his muther. I’ll huuk a goun frum Ant Sally.”

“Wel, then, u’ll hav to stay in th cabin when me and Jim leevs.”

“Not much. I’ll stuf Jim’s cloeths fuul of straw and lay it on his bed to reprezent his muther in disgiez, and Jim ’ll taek th nigger wuuman’s goun off of me and wair it, and we’ll all evaed together. When a prizoner of stiel escaeps it’s calld an evaezhun. It’s allways calld so when a king escaeps, f’rinstance. And th saem with a king’s sun; it don’t maek no diferens whether he’s a nacheral wun or an unnacheral wun.”

So Tom he roet th nonnamous leter, and I smouched th yaller wench’s frok that niet, and puut it on, and shuvd it under th frunt dor, th way Tom toeld me to. It sed:

Bewair. Trubl is brooing. Keep a sharp luukout. Unnoen Frend.











Next niet we stuk a pikcher, which Tom drawed in blud, of a skul and crossbones on th frunt dor; and next niet anuther wun of a coffin on th bak dor. I never see a family in such a swet. Thay couldn’t a bin wers scaird if th plaes had a bin fuul of goests laying for them behiend evrything and under th beds and shivering thru th air. If a dor bangd, Ant Sally she jumpt and sed “ouch!” if enything fel, she jumpt and sed “ouch!” if u hapend to tuch her, when she worn’t noetising, she dun th saem; she couldn’t faes noeway and be satisfied, becauz she alowd thair was sumthing behiend her evry tiem—so she was allways a-wherling around suden, and saying “ouch,” and befor she’d got too-therds around she’d wherl bak agen, and say it agen; and she was afraed to go to bed, but she dasn’t set up. So th thing was werking verry wel, Tom sed; he sed he never see a thing werk mor satisfactory. He sed it shoed it was dun riet.

So he sed, now for th grand bulj! So th verry next morning at th streek of daun we got anuther leter redy, and was wundering whut we beter do with it, becauz we herd them say at super thay was going to hav a nigger on woch at boeth dors all niet. Tom he went doun th lietning-rod to spi around; and th nigger at th bak dor was asleep, and he stuk it in th bak of his nek and cum bak. This leter sed:

Don’t betray me, I wish to be yur frend. Thair is a desprate gang of cutthroats frum oever in th Indian Territory going to steel yur runaway nigger to-niet, and thay hav bin trieing to scair u so as u wil stay in th hous and not bother them. I am wun of th gang, but hav got religgion and wish to qit it and leed an onest lief agen, and wil betray th helish dezien. Thay wil sneek doun frum northards, along th fens, at midniet exact, with a falls kee, and go in th nigger’s cabin to get him. I am to be off a pees and blo a tin horn if I see eny daenjer; but sted of that I wil baa liek a sheep soon as thay get in and not blo at all; then whilst thay ar geting his chaens loos, u slip thair and lok them in, and can kil them at yur leezher. Don’t do enything but just th way I am teling u, if u do thay wil suspishun sumthing and raez hoop-jamboreehoo. I do not wish eny reword but to noe I hav dun th riet thing. Unnoen Frend.














CHAPTER XL.

We was feeling prity guud after brekfast, and tuuk mi canoo and went oever th river a-fishing, with a lunch, and had a guud tiem, and tuuk a luuk at th raft and found her all riet, and got hoem laet to super, and found them in such a swet and wery thay didn’t noe which end thay was standing on, and maed us go riet off to bed th minit we was dun super, and wouldn’t tel us whut th trubl was, and never let on a werd about th nue leter, but didn’t need to, becauz we knowed as much about it as enybody did, and as soon as we was haf up stairs and her bak was ternd we slid for th selar cubord and loeded up a guud lunch and tuuk it up to our room and went to bed, and got up about haf-past eleven, and Tom puut on Ant Sally’s dres that he stoel and was going to start with th lunch, but sez:

“Whair’s th buter?”

“I laed out a hunk of it,” I sez, “on a pees of a corn-pone.”

“Wel, u left it laed out, then—it ain’t heer.”

“We can get along without it,” I sez.

“We can get along with it, too,” he sez; “just u slied doun selar and fech it. And then moezy riet doun th lietning-rod and cum along. I’ll go and stuf th straw into Jim’s cloeths to reprezent his muther in disgiez, and be redy to baa liek a sheep and shuv soon as u get thair.”

So out he went, and doun selar went I. Th hunk of buter, big as a person’s fist, was whair I had left it, so I tuuk up th slab of corn-pone with it on, and blowed out mi liet, and started up stairs verry stelthy, and got up to th maen flor all riet, but heer cums Ant Sally with a candl, and I clapt th truk in mi hat, and clapt mi hat on mi hed, and th next second she see me; and she sez:

“U bin doun selar?”

“Yes’m.”

“Whut u bin doing doun thair?”

“Noth’n.”

“Noth’n!”

“No’m.”

“Wel, then, whut pozest u to go doun thair this tiem of niet?”

“I don’t noe ’m.”

“U don’t noe? Don’t anser me that way. Tom, I wont to noe whut u bin doing doun thair.”

“I hain’t bin doing a singgl thing, Ant Sally, I hoep to graeshus if I hav.”

I rekond she’d let me go now, and as a generl thing she wuud; but I s’poez thair was so meny straenj things going on she was just in a swet about evry litl thing that worn’t yard-stik straet; so she sez, verry desieded:

“U just march into that seting-room and stay thair til I cum. U bin up to sumthing u no biznes to, and I lay I’ll fiend out whut it is befor I’M dun with u.”

So she went away as I oepend th dor and waukt into th seting-room. Mi, but thair was a croud thair! Fifteen farmers, and evry wun of them had a gun. I was moest powerful sik, and slunk to a chair and set doun. Thay was seting around, sum of them tauking a litl, in a lo vois, and all of them fijety and uneezy, but trieing to luuk liek thay worn’t; but I knowed thay was, becauz thay was allways taeking off thair hats, and puuting them on, and scraching thair heds, and chaenjing thair seets, and fumbling with thair butons. I worn’t eezy mieself, but I didn’t taek mi hat off, all th saem.











I did wish Ant Sally wuud cum, and get dun with me, and lik me, if she wonted to, and let me get away and tel Tom how we’d oeverdun this thing, and whut a thundering hornet’s-nest we’d got ourselvs into, so we cuud stop fooling around straet off, and cleer out with Jim befor thees rips got out of paeshens and cum for us.

At last she cum and begun to ask me qeschuns, but I couldn’t anser them straet, I didn’t noe which end of me was up; becauz thees men was in such a fijet now that sum was wonting to start riet NOW and lay for them desperaadoes, and saying it worn’t but a fue minits to midniet; and uthers was trieing to get them to hoeld on and waet for th sheep-signal; and heer was Aunty peging away at th qeschuns, and me a-shaeking all oever and redy to sink doun in mi traks I was that scaird; and th plaes geting hoter and hoter, and th buter begining to melt and run doun mi nek and behiend mi eers; and prity soon, when wun of them sez, “I’M for going and geting in th cabin ferst and riet now, and caching them when thay cum,” I moest dropt; and a streek of buter cum a-trikling doun mi forhed, and Ant Sally she see it, and terns whiet as a sheet, and sez:

“For th land’s saek, whut is th mater with th chield? He’s got th braen-feever as shor as u’re born, and thay’re oozing out!”

And evrybody runs to see, and she snaches off mi hat, and out cums th bred and whut was left of th buter, and she grabd me, and hugd me, and sez:

“O, whut a tern u did giv me! and how glad and graetful I am it ain’t no wers; for luk’s agenst us, and it never raens but it pors, and when I see that truk I thaut we’d lost u, for I knowed bi th culor and all it was just liek yur braens wuud be if—Deer, deer, whyd’nt u tel me that was whut u’d bin doun thair for, I wouldn’t a caird. Now cler out to bed, and don’t lemme see no mor of u til morning!”

I was up stairs in a second, and doun th lietning-rod in anuther wun, and shinning thru th dark for th leen-to. I couldn’t hardly get mi werds out, I was so ankshus; but I toeld Tom as qik as I cuud we must jump for it now, and not a minit to looz—th hous fuul of men, yonder, with guns!

His ies just blaezd; and he sez:

“No!—is that so? ain’t it buuly! Whi, Huck, if it was to do oever agen, I bet I cuud fech too hundred! If we cuud puut it off til—”

“Hery! Hery!” I sez. “Whair’s Jim?”

“Riet at yur elbo; if u reech out yur arm u can tuch him. He’s drest, and evrything’s redy. Now we’ll slied out and giv th sheep-signal.”

But then we herd th tramp of men cuming to th dor, and herd them begin to fumbl with th pad-lok, and herd a man say:

“I toeld u we’d be too soon; thay haeven’t cum—th dor is lokt. Heer, I’ll lok sum of u into th cabin, and u lay for ’em in th dark and kil ’em when thay cum; and th rest scater around a pees, and lisen if u can heer ’em cuming.”

So in thay cum, but couldn’t see us in th dark, and moest trod on us whilst we was husling to get under th bed. But we got under all riet, and out thru th hoel, swift but sofft—Jim ferst, me next, and Tom last, which was acording to Tom’s orders. Now we was in th leen-to, and herd trampings cloez bi outsied. So we crept to th dor, and Tom stopt us thair and puut his ie to th crak, but couldn’t maek out nuthing, it was so dark; and whisperd and sed he wuud lisen for th steps to get ferther, and when he nujd us Jim must glied out ferst, and him last. So he set his eer to th crak and lisend, and lisend, and lisend, and th steps a-scraeping around out thair all th tiem; and at last he nujd us, and we slid out, and stoopt doun, not breething, and not maeking th leest noiz, and slipt stelthy tords th fens in Injun fiel, and got to it all riet, and me and Jim oever it; but Tom’s briches catched fast on a splinter on th top rael, and then he heer th steps cuming, so he had to puul loos, which snapt th splinter and maed a noiz; and as he dropt in our traks and started sumbody sings out:











“Hoo’s that? Anser, or I’ll shoot!”

But we didn’t anser; we just unferld our heels and shuvd. Then thair was a rush, and a Bang, Bang, Bang! and th buulets fairly whizd around us! We herd them sing out:

“Heer thay ar! Thay’ve broek for th river! After ’em, boys, and tern loos th daugs!”

So heer thay cum, fuul tilt. We cuud heer them becauz thay wor boots and yeld, but we didn’t wair no boots and didn’t yel. We was in th path to th mil; and when thay got prity cloez on to us we dojd into th buush and let them go bi, and then dropt in behiend them. Thay’d had all th daugs shut up, so thay wouldn’t scair off th robers; but bi this tiem sumbody had let them loos, and heer thay cum, maeking powwow enuf for a milyon; but thay was our daugs; so we stopt in our traks til thay catched up; and when thay see it worn’t noebody but us, and no exsietment to offer them, thay oenly just sed houdy, and tore riet ahed tords th shouting and clatering; and then we up-steem agen, and whizd along after them til we was neerly to th mil, and then struk up thru th buush to whair mi canoo was tied, and hopt in and puuld for deer lief tords th midl of th river, but didn’t maek no mor noiz than we was obleeged to. Then we struk out, eezy and cumfortabl, for th ieland whair mi raft was; and we cuud heer them yeling and barking at eech uther all up and doun th bank, til we was so far away th sounds got dim and died out. And when we stept on to th raft I sez:

“Now, oeld Jim, u’re a free man agen, and I bet u wun’t ever be a slaev no mor.”

“En a miety guud job it wuz, too, Huck. It ’uz pland buetiful, en it ’uz dun buetiful; en day ain’t noebody kin git up a plan dat’s mo’ mixt-up en splendid den whut dat wun wuz.”

We was all glad as we cuud be, but Tom was th gladdest of all becauz he had a buulet in th caf of his leg.

When me and Jim herd that we didn’t feel so brash as whut we did befor. It was herting him considerabl, and bleeding; so we laed him in th wigwom and tore up wun of th duek’s sherts for to bandej him, but he sez:

“Gimme th rags; I can do it mieself. Don’t stop now; don’t fool around heer, and th evaezhun booming along so hansum; man th sweeps, and set her loos! Boys, we dun it elegant!—’deed we did. I wish we’d a had th handling of Louis XVI., thair wouldn’t a bin no ‘Sun of Saent Louis, asend to heven!’ roet doun in his bieografy; no, ser, we’d a whooped him oever th border—that’s whut we’d a dun with him—and dun it just as slik as nuthing at all, too. Man th sweeps—man th sweeps!”

But me and Jim was consulting—and thinking. And after we’d thaut a minit, I sez:

“Say it, Jim.”

So he sez:

“Wel, den, dis is de way it luuk to me, Huck. Ef it wuz him dat ’uz bein’ sot free, en wun er de boys wuz to git shot, wuud he say, ‘Go on en saev me, nemmine ’bout a doctor f’r to saev dis wun?’ Is dat liek Mars Tom Sawyer? Wuud he say dat? U bet he wouldn’t! wel, den, is Jim gywne to say it? No, sah—I doan’ buj a step out’n dis plaes ’dout a doctor, not if it’s forty yeer!”











I knowed he was whiet insied, and I rekond he’d say whut he did say—so it was all riet now, and I toeld Tom I was a-going for a doctor. He raezd considerabl ro about it, but me and Jim stuk to it and wouldn’t buj; so he was for cralling out and seting th raft loos himself; but we wouldn’t let him. Then he giv us a pees of his miend, but it didn’t do no guud.

So when he sees me geting th canoo redy, he sez:

“Wel, then, if u’re bound to go, I’ll tel u th way to do when u get to th vilej. Shut th dor and bliendfoeld th doctor tiet and fast, and maek him swair to be sielent as th graev, and puut a pers fuul of goeld in his hand, and then taek and leed him all around th bak alys and everywheres in th dark, and then fech him heer in th canoo, in a roundabout way amungst th ielands, and serch him and taek his chauk away frum him, and don’t giv it bak to him til u get him bak to th vilej, or els he wil chauk this raft so he can fiend it agen. It’s th way thay all do.”

So I sed I wuud, and left, and Jim was to hied in th wuuds when he see th doctor cuming til he was gon agen.














CHAPTER XLI.

Th doctor was an oeld man; a verry nies, kiend-luuking oeld man when I got him up. I toeld him me and mi bruther was oever on Spanish Ieland hunting yesterday afternoon, and campt on a pees of a raft we found, and about midniet he must a kikt his gun in his dreems, for it went off and shot him in th leg, and we wonted him to go oever thair and fix it and not say nuthing about it, nor let enybody noe, becauz we wonted to cum hoem this eevning and serpriez th foeks.

“Hoo is yur foeks?” he sez.

“Th Phelpses, doun yonder.”

“O,” he sez. And after a minit, he sez:

“How’d u say he got shot?”

“He had a dreem,” I sez, “and it shot him.”

“Singguelar dreem,” he sez.

So he lit up his lantern, and got his sadl-bags, and we started. But when he sees th canoo he didn’t liek th luuk of her—sed she was big enuf for wun, but didn’t luuk prity saef for too. I sez:

“O, u needn’t be afeard, ser, she carryd th three of us eezy enuf.”

“Whut three?”

“Whi, me and Sid, and—and—and th guns; that’s whut I meen.”

“O,” he sez.

But he puut his fuut on th gunel and rokt her, and shuuk his hed, and sed he rekond he’d luuk around for a biger wun. But thay was all lokt and chained; so he tuuk mi canoo, and sed for me to waet til he cum bak, or I cuud hunt around ferther, or maybe I beter go doun hoem and get them redy for th serpriez if I wonted to. But I sed I didn’t; so I toeld him just how to fiend th raft, and then he started.

I struk an iedeea prity soon. I sez to mieself, spos’n he can’t fix that leg just in three shaeks of a sheep’s tael, as th saying is? spos’n it taeks him three or foer days? Whut ar we going to do?—lay around thair til he lets th cat out of th bag? No, ser; I noe whut I’ll do. I’ll waet, and when he cums bak if he sez he’s got to go eny mor I’ll get doun thair, too, if I swim; and we’ll taek and tee him, and keep him, and shuv out doun th river; and when Tom’s dun with him we’ll giv him whut it’s werth, or all we got, and then let him get ashor.

So then I crept into a lumber-piel to get sum sleep; and next tiem I waekt up th sun was away up oever mi hed! I shot out and went for th doctor’s hous, but thay toeld me he’d gon away in th niet sum tiem or uther, and worn’t bak yet. Wel, thinks I, that luuks powerful bad for Tom, and I’ll dig out for th ieland riet off. So away I shuvd, and ternd th corner, and neerly ramd mi hed into Unkl Silas’s stumac! He sez:

“Whi, Tom! Whair u bin all this tiem, u rascal?”











“I hain’t bin nowheres,” I sez, “oenly just hunting for th runaway nigger—me and Sid.”

“Whi, whair ever did u go?” he sez. “Yur ant’s bin miety uneezy.”

“She needn’t,” I sez, “becauz we was all riet. We foloed th men and th daugs, but thay outrun us, and we lost them; but we thaut we herd them on th wauter, so we got a canoo and tuuk out after them and crosst oever, but couldn’t fiend nuthing of them; so we cruised along up-shor til we got kiend of tierd and beet out; and tied up th canoo and went to sleep, and never waekt up til about an our ago; then we paddled oever heer to heer th nues, and Sid’s at th poest-offis to see whut he can heer, and I’m a-branching out to get sumthing to eet for us, and then we’re going hoem.”

So then we went to th poest-offis to get “Sid”; but just as I suspicioned, he worn’t thair; so th oeld man he got a leter out of th offis, and we waeted awhiel longger, but Sid didn’t cum; so th oeld man sed, cum along, let Sid fuut it hoem, or canoo it, when he got dun fooling around—but we wuud ried. I couldn’t get him to let me stay and waet for Sid; and he sed thair worn’t no ues in it, and I must cum along, and let Ant Sally see we was all riet.

When we got hoem Ant Sally was that glad to see me she laft and cried boeth, and hugd me, and giv me wun of them lickings of hern that don’t amount to shuks, and sed she’d serv Sid th saem when he cum.

And th plaes was plum fuul of farmers and farmers’ wievs, to diner; and such anuther clack a body never herd. Oeld Mrs. Hotchkiss was th werst; her tung was a-going all th tiem. She sez:

“Wel, Sister Phelps, I’ve ransakt that-air cabin oever, an’ I b’lieve th nigger was craezy. I sez to Sister Damrell—didn’t I, Sister Damrell?—s’I, he’s craezy, s’I—them’s th verry werds I sed. U all hearn me: he’s craezy, s’I; evrything shoes it, s’I. Luuk at that-air griendstoen, s’I; wont to tel me’t eny cretur ’t’s in his riet miend ’s a goin’ to scrabble all them craezy things onto a griendstoen, s’I? Heer sich ’n’ sich a person busted his hart; ’n’ heer so ’n’ so pegd along for therty-seven yeer, ’n’ all that—natcherl sun o’ Louis sumbody, ’n’ sich everlast’n rubbage. He’s plum craezy, s’I; it’s whut I sez in th fust plaes, it’s whut I sez in th midl, ’n’ it’s whut I sez last ’n’ all th tiem—th nigger’s craezy—craezy ‘s Nebokoodneezer, s’I.”











“An’ luuk at that-air lader maed out’n rags, Sister Hotchkiss,” sez oeld Mrs. Damrell; “whut in th naem o’ guudnes cuud he ever wont of—”

“Th verry werds I was a-sayin’ no longger ago th’n this minit to Sister Utterback, ’n’ she’ll tel u so herself. Sh-she, luuk at that-air rag lader, sh-she; ’n’ s’I, yes, luuk at it, s’I—whut cuud he a-wonted of it, s’I. Sh-she, Sister Hotchkiss, sh-she—”

“But how in th naeshun’d thay ever git that griendstoen in thair, enyway? ’n’ hoo dug that-air hoel? ’n’ hoo—”

“Mi verry werds, Brer Penrod! I was a-sayin’—pas that-air sasser o’ m’lases, wun’t ye?—I was a-sayin’ to Sister Dunlap, jist this minit, how did thay git that griendstoen in thair, s’I. Without help, miend u—’thout help! that’s wher ’tis. Don’t tel me, s’I; thair wuz help, s’I; ’n’ ther’ wuz a plenty help, too, s’I; ther’s ben a duzen a-helpin’ that nigger, ’n’ I lay I’d skin evry last nigger on this plaes but I’d fiend out hoo dun it, s’I; ’n’ moroever, s’I—”

“A duzen sez u!—forty couldn’t a dun evry thing that’s bin dun. Luuk at them caes-nief saws and things, how teedius thay’ve bin maed; luuk at that bed-leg sawd off with ’m, a week’s werk for six men; luuk at that nigger maed out’n straw on th bed; and luuk at—”

“U may wel say it, Brer Hightower! It’s jist as I was a-sayin’ to Brer Phelps, his oen self. S’e, whut do u think of it, Sister Hotchkiss, s’e? Think o’ whut, Brer Phelps, s’I? Think o’ that bed-leg sawd off that a way, s’e? think of it, s’I? I lay it never sawd itself off, s’I—sumbody sawd it, s’I; that’s mi opinyon, taek it or leev it, it mayn’t be no ’count, s’I, but sich as ’t is, it’s mi opinyon, s’I, ’n’ if eny body k’n start a beter wun, s’I, let him do it, s’I, that’s all. I sez to Sister Dunlap, s’I—”

“Whi, daug mi cats, thay must a ben a hous-fuul o’ niggers in thair evry niet for foer weeks to a dun all that werk, Sister Phelps. Luuk at that shert—evry last inch of it kivered oever with seecret African rit’n dun with blud! Must a ben a raft uv ’m at it riet along, all th tiem, amost. Whi, I’d giv too dolars to hav it red to me; ’n’ as for th niggers that roet it, I ’lo I’d taek ’n’ lash ’m t’ll—”

“Peepl to help him, Bruther Marples! Wel, I rekon u’d think so if u’d a bin in this hous for a whiel bak. Whi, thay’ve stoel evrything thay cuud lay thair hands on—and we a-woching all th tiem, miend u. Thay stoel that shert riet off o’ th lien! and as for that sheet thay maed th rag lader out of, ther’ ain’t no teling how meny tiems thay didn’t steel that; and flour, and candls, and candlesticks, and spoons, and th oeld worming-pan, and moest a thouzand things that I disremember now, and mi nue calico dres; and me and Silas and mi Sid and Tom on th constant woch day and niet, as I was a-teling u, and not a wun of us cuud cach hied nor hair nor siet nor sound of them; and heer at th last minit, lo and behoeld u, thay slieds riet in under our noezes and fools us, and not oenly fools us but th Injun Territory robers too, and actuly gets away with that nigger saef and sound, and that with sixteen men and twenty-too daugs riet on thair verry heels at that verry tiem! I tel u, it just bangs enything I ever herd of. Whi, sperits couldn’t a dun beter and bin no smarter. And I rekon thay must a bin sperits—becauz, u noe our daugs, and ther’ ain’t no beter; wel, them daugs never eeven got on th trak of ’m wuns! U explaen that to me if u can!—eny of u!”

“Wel, it duz beet—”

“Laws aliev, I never—”

“So help me, I wouldn’t a be—”

“Hous-theevs as wel as—”

“Goodnessgracioussakes, I’d a ben afeard to liv in sich a—”

“’Fraid to liv!—whi, I was that scaird I dasn’t hardly go to bed, or get up, or lay doun, or set doun, Sister Ridgeway. Whi, thay’d steel th verry—whi, guudnes sakes, u can ges whut kiend of a fluster I was in bi th tiem midniet cum last niet. I hoep to graeshus if I worn’t afraed thay’d steel sum o’ th family! I was just to that pas I didn’t hav no reezoning facultys no mor. It luuks foolish enuf now, in th daytiem; but I sez to mieself, thair’s mi too pur boys asleep, ’way up stairs in that loensum room, and I declair to guudnes I was that uneezy ’t I crep’ up thair and lokt ’em in! I did. And enybody wuud. Becauz, u noe, when u get scaird that way, and it keeps runing on, and geting wers and wers all th tiem, and yur wits gets to addling, and u get to doing all sorts o’ wield things, and bi and bi u think to yurself, spos’n I was a boy, and was away up thair, and th dor ain’t lokt, and u—” She stopt, luuking kiend of wundering, and then she ternd her hed around slo, and when her ie lit on me—I got up and tuuk a wauk.

Sez I to mieself, I can explaen beter how we cum to not be in that room this morning if I go out to wun sied and study oever it a litl. So I dun it. But I dasn’t go fer, or she’d a sent for me. And when it was laet in th day th peepl all went, and then I cum in and toeld her th noiz and shooting waekt up me and “Sid,” and th dor was lokt, and we wonted to see th fun, so we went doun th lietning-rod, and boeth of us got hert a litl, and we didn’t never wont to tri that no mor. And then I went on and toeld her all whut I toeld Unkl Silas befor; and then she sed she’d forgiv us, and maybe it was all riet enuf enyway, and about whut a body miet expect of boys, for all boys was a prity harum-scarum lot as fer as she cuud see; and so, as long as no harm hadn’t cum of it, she jujd she beter puut in her tiem being graetful we was aliev and wel and she had us stil, sted of freting oever whut was past and dun. So then she kist me, and pated me on th hed, and dropt into a kiend of a broun study; and prity soon jumps up, and sez:

“Whi, lawsamercy, it’s moest niet, and Sid not cum yet! Whut has becum of that boy?”

I see mi chans; so I skips up and sez:

“I’ll run riet up to toun and get him,” I sez.

“No u wun’t,” she sez. “U’ll stay riet wher’ u ar; wun’s enuf to be lost at a tiem. If he ain’t heer to super, yur unkl ’ll go.”

Wel, he worn’t thair to super; so riet after super unkl went.

He cum bak about ten a litl bit uneezy; hadn’t run across Tom’s trak. Ant Sally was a guud deel uneezy; but Unkl Silas he sed thair worn’t no ocaezhun to be—boys wil be boys, he sed, and u’ll see this wun tern up in th morning all sound and riet. So she had to be satisfied. But she sed she’d set up for him a whiel enyway, and keep a liet berning so he cuud see it.











And then when I went up to bed she cum up with me and fetched her candl, and tukt me in, and mutherd me so guud I felt meen, and liek I couldn’t luuk her in th faes; and she set doun on th bed and taukt with me a long tiem, and sed whut a splendid boy Sid was, and didn’t seem to wont to ever stop tauking about him; and kept asking me evry now and then if I rekond he cuud a got lost, or hert, or maybe drownded, and miet be laying at this minit somewheres sufering or ded, and she not bi him to help him, and so th teers wuud drip doun sielent, and I wuud tel her that Sid was all riet, and wuud be hoem in th morning, shur; and she wuud sqeez mi hand, or maybe kis me, and tel me to say it agen, and keep on saying it, becauz it dun her guud, and she was in so much trubl. And when she was going away she luukt doun in mi ies so stedy and jentl, and sez:

“Th dor ain’t going to be lokt, Tom, and thair’s th windo and th rod; but u’ll be guud, wun’t u? And u wun’t go? For mi saek.”

Laws noes I wonted to go bad enuf to see about Tom, and was all intending to go; but after that I wouldn’t a went, not for kingdoms.

But she was on mi miend and Tom was on mi miend, so I slept verry restles. And twies I went doun th rod away in th niet, and slipt around frunt, and see her seting thair bi her candl in th windo with her ies tords th roed and th teers in them; and I wisht I cuud do sumthing for her, but I couldn’t, oenly to swair that I wouldn’t never do nuthing to greev her eny mor. And th therd tiem I waekt up at daun, and slid doun, and she was thair yet, and her candl was moest out, and her oeld gray hed was resting on her hand, and she was asleep.














CHAPTER XLII.

Th oeld man was uptoun agen befor brekfast, but couldn’t get no trak of Tom; and boeth of them set at th taebl thinking, and not saying nuthing, and luuking mornful, and thair coffy geting coeld, and not eeting enything. And bi and bi th oeld man sez:

“Did I giv u th leter?”

“Whut leter?”

“Th wun I got yesterday out of th poest-offis.”

“No, u didn’t giv me no leter.”

“Wel, I must a forgot it.”

So he rumejd his pokets, and then went off somewheres whair he had laed it doun, and fetched it, and giv it to her. She sez:

“Whi, it’s frum St. Petersburg—it’s frum Sis.”

I alowd anuther wauk wuud do me guud; but I couldn’t ster. But befor she cuud braek it oepen she dropt it and run—for she see sumthing. And so did I. It was Tom Sawyer on a matres; and that oeld doctor; and Jim, in her calico dres, with his hands tied behiend him; and a lot of peepl. I hid th leter behiend th ferst thing that cum handy, and rusht. She flung herself at Tom, crieing, and sez:

“O, he’s ded, he’s ded, I noe he’s ded!”

And Tom he ternd his hed a litl, and muterd sumthing or uther, which shoed he worn’t in his riet miend; then she flung up her hands, and sez:

“He’s aliev, thank God! And that’s enuf!” and she snacht a kis of him, and floo for th hous to get th bed redy, and scatering orders riet and left at th niggers and evrybody els, as fast as her tung cuud go, evry jump of th way.

I foloed th men to see whut thay was going to do with Jim; and th oeld doctor and Unkl Silas foloed after Tom into th hous. Th men was verry hufy, and sum of them wonted to hang Jim for an exampl to all th uther niggers around thair, so thay wouldn’t be trieing to run away liek Jim dun, and maeking such a raft of trubl, and keeping a hoel family scaird moest to deth for days and niets. But th uthers sed, don’t do it, it wouldn’t anser at all; he ain’t our nigger, and his oener wuud tern up and maek us pay for him, shur. So that coold them doun a litl, becauz th peepl that’s allways th moest ankshus for to hang a nigger that hain’t dun just riet is allways th verry wuns that ain’t th moest ankshus to pay for him when thay’ve got thair satisfacshun out of him.

Thay cussed Jim considerble, tho, and giv him a cuf or too sied th hed wuns in a whiel, but Jim never sed nuthing, and he never let on to noe me, and thay tuuk him to th saem cabin, and puut his oen cloeths on him, and chained him agen, and not to no bed-leg this tiem, but to a big staepl droev into th botom log, and chained his hands, too, and boeth legs, and sed he worn’t to hav nuthing but bred and wauter to eet after this til his oener cum, or he was soeld at aucshun becauz he didn’t cum in a serten length of tiem, and fild up our hoel, and sed a cupl of farmers with guns must stand woch around about th cabin evry niet, and a buuldaug tied to th dor in th daytiem; and about this tiem thay was thru with th job and was taepering off with a kiend of generl guud-bi cussing, and then th oeld doctor cums and taeks a luuk, and sez:

“Don’t be no rufer on him than u’re obleeged to, becauz he ain’t a bad nigger. When I got to whair I found th boy I see I couldn’t cut th buulet out without sum help, and he worn’t in no condishun for me to leev to go and get help; and he got a litl wers and a litl wers, and after a long tiem he went out of his hed, and wouldn’t let me cum a-ni him eny mor, and sed if I chaukt his raft he’d kil me, and no end of wield foolishnes liek that, and I see I couldn’t do enything at all with him; so I sez, I got to hav help sumhow; and th minit I sez it out cralls this nigger frum somewheres and sez he’ll help, and he dun it, too, and dun it verry wel. Of cors I jujd he must be a runaway nigger, and thair I was! and thair I had to stik riet straet along all th rest of th day and all niet. It was a fix, I tel u! I had a cupl of paeshents with th chils, and of cors I’d of liekt to run up to toun and see them, but I dasn’t, becauz th nigger miet get away, and then I’d be to blaem; and yet never a skif cum cloez enuf for me to hael. So thair I had to stik plum until dayliet this morning; and I never see a nigger that was a beter nuss or faithfuller, and yet he was risking his freedom to do it, and was all tierd out, too, and I see plaen enuf he’d bin werkt maen hard laetly. I liekt th nigger for that; I tel u, jentlmen, a nigger liek that is werth a thouzand dolars—and kiend treetment, too. I had evrything I needed, and th boy was doing as wel thair as he wuud a dun at hoem—beter, maybe, becauz it was so qieet; but thair I was, with boeth of ’m on mi hands, and thair I had to stik til about daun this morning; then sum men in a skif cum bi, and as guud luk wuud hav it th nigger was seting bi th palet with his hed propt on his nees sound asleep; so I moeshund them in qieet, and thay slipt up on him and grabd him and tied him befor he knowed whut he was about, and we never had no trubl. And th boy being in a kiend of a fliety sleep, too, we mufld th ors and hicht th raft on, and toed her oever verry nies and qieet, and th nigger never maed th leest ro nor sed a werd frum th start. He ain’t no bad nigger, jentlmen; that’s whut I think about him.”











Sumbody sez:

“Wel, it sounds verry guud, doctor, I’m obleeged to say.”

Then th uthers soffend up a litl, too, and I was miety thankful to that oeld doctor for doing Jim that guud tern; and I was glad it was acording to mi jujment of him, too; becauz I thaut he had a guud hart in him and was a guud man th ferst tiem I see him. Then thay all agreed that Jim had acted verry wel, and was dezerving to hav sum noetis tuuk of it, and reword. So evry wun of them promist, riet out and harty, that thay wouldn’t cuss him no mor.

Then thay cum out and lokt him up. I hoept thay was going to say he cuud hav wun or too of th chaens tuuk off, becauz thay was roten hevy, or cuud hav meet and greens with his bred and wauter; but thay didn’t think of it, and I rekond it worn’t best for me to mix in, but I jujd I’d get th doctor’s yarn to Ant Sally sumhow or uther as soon as I’d got thru th braekers that was laying just ahed of me—explanaeshuns, I meen, of how I forgot to menshun about Sid being shot when I was teling how him and me puut in that dratted niet padling around hunting th runaway nigger.

But I had plenty tiem. Ant Sally she stuk to th sik-room all day and all niet, and evry tiem I see Unkl Silas mooning around I dojd him.

Next morning I herd Tom was a guud deel beter, and thay sed Ant Sally was gon to get a nap. So I slips to th sik-room, and if I found him awaek I rekond we cuud puut up a yarn for th family that wuud wosh. But he was sleeping, and sleeping verry peesful, too; and pael, not fier-faest th way he was when he cum. So I set doun and laed for him to waek. In about haf an our Ant Sally cums gliding in, and thair I was, up a stump agen! She moeshund me to be stil, and set doun bi me, and begun to whisper, and sed we cuud all be joyful now, becauz all th simptoms was ferst-raet, and he’d bin sleeping liek that for ever so long, and luuking beter and peacefuller all th tiem, and ten to wun he’d waek up in his riet miend.

So we set thair woching, and bi and bi he sters a bit, and oepend his ies verry nacheral, and taeks a luuk, and sez:

“Helo!—whi, I’m at hoem! How’s that? Whair’s th raft?”

“It’s all riet,” I sez.

“And Jim?”

“Th saem,” I sez, but couldn’t say it prity brash. But he never noetist, but sez:

“Guud! Splendid! Now we’re all riet and saef! Did u tel Aunty?”

I was going to say yes; but she chipt in and sez: “About whut, Sid?”

“Whi, about th way th hoel thing was dun.”

“Whut hoel thing?”

“Whi, th hoel thing. Thair ain’t but wun; how we set th runaway nigger free—me and Tom.”

“Guud land! Set th run—Whut is th chield tauking about! Deer, deer, out of his hed agen!”

“No, I ain’t out of mi hed; I noe all whut I’m tauking about. We did set him free—me and Tom. We laed out to do it, and we dun it. And we dun it elegant, too.” He’d got a start, and she never chekt him up, just set and staird and staird, and let him clip along, and I see it worn’t no ues for me to puut in. “Whi, Aunty, it cost us a power of werk—weeks of it—ours and ours, evry niet, whilst u was all asleep. And we had to steel candls, and th sheet, and th shert, and yur dres, and spoons, and tin plates, and caes-nievs, and th worming-pan, and th griendstoen, and flour, and just no end of things, and u can’t think whut werk it was to maek th saws, and pens, and inscripshuns, and wun thing or anuther, and u can’t think haf th fun it was. And we had to maek up th pikchers of coffins and things, and nonnamous leters frum th robers, and get up and doun th lietning-rod, and dig th hoel into th cabin, and maed th roep lader and send it in cuukt up in a pi, and send in spoons and things to werk with in yur aepron poket—”

“Mersy sakes!”

“—and loed up th cabin with rats and snaeks and so on, for cumpany for Jim; and then u kept Tom heer so long with th buter in his hat that u cum neer spiling th hoel biznes, becauz th men cum befor we was out of th cabin, and we had to rush, and thay herd us and let driev at us, and I got mi shair, and we dojd out of th path and let them go bi, and when th daugs cum thay worn’t interested in us, but went for th moest noiz, and we got our canoo, and maed for th raft, and was all saef, and Jim was a free man, and we dun it all bi ourselvs, and wasn’t it buuly, Aunty!”

“Wel, I never herd th lieks of it in all mi born days! So it was u, u litl rapscallions, that’s bin maeking all this trubl, and ternd evrybody’s wits cleen insied out and scaird us all moest to deth. I’ve as guud a noeshun as ever I had in mi lief to taek it out o’ u this verry minit. To think, heer I’ve bin, niet after niet, a—u just get wel wuns, u yung scamp, and I lay I’ll tan th Oeld Harry out o’ boeth o’ ye!”

But Tom, he was so proud and joyful, he just couldn’t hoeld in, and his tung just went it—she a-chiping in, and spiting fier all along, and boeth of them going it at wuns, liek a cat convenshun; and she sez:

“Wel, u get all th enjoyment u can out of it now, for miend I tel u if I cach u medling with him agen—”

“Medling with hoo?” Tom sez, droping his smiel and luuking serpriezd.

“With hoo? Whi, th runaway nigger, of cors. Hoo’d u rekon?”

Tom luuks at me verry graev, and sez:

“Tom, didn’t u just tel me he was all riet? Hasn’t he got away?”

“Him?” sez Ant Sally; “th runaway nigger? ’Deed he hasn’t. Thay’ve got him bak, saef and sound, and he’s in that cabin agen, on bred and wauter, and loeded doun with chaens, til he’s claemd or soeld!”











Tom roez sqair up in bed, with his ie hot, and his nostrils oepening and shuting liek gils, and sings out to me:

“Thay hain’t no riet to shut him up! Shuv!—and don’t u looz a minit. Tern him loos! he ain’t no slaev; he’s as free as eny cretur that wauks this erth!”

“Whut duz th chield meen?”

“I meen evry werd I say, Ant Sally, and if sumbody don’t go, I’ll go. I’ve knowed him all his lief, and so has Tom, thair. Oeld Mis Watson died too munths ago, and she was ashaemd she ever was going to sel him doun th river, and sed so; and she set him free in her wil.”

“Then whut on erth did u wont to set him free for, seeing he was allredy free?”

“Wel, that is a qeschun, I must say; and just liek wimen! Whi, I wonted th advencher of it; and I’d a waeded nek-deep in blud to—guudnes aliev, Ant Polly!”

If she worn’t standing riet thair, just insied th dor, luuking as sweet and contented as an aenjel haf fuul of pi, I wish I may never!

Ant Sally jumpt for her, and moest hugd th hed off of her, and cried oever her, and I found a guud enuf plaes for me under th bed, for it was geting prity sultry for us, seemd to me. And I peeped out, and in a litl whiel Tom’s Ant Polly shuuk herself loos and stuud thair luuking across at Tom oever her spectacls—kiend of griending him into th erth, u noe. And then she sez:

“Yes, u beter tern y’r hed away—I wuud if I was u, Tom.”

“O, deary me!” sez Ant Sally; “Is he chaenjd so? Whi, that ain’t Tom, it’s Sid; Tom’s—Tom’s—whi, whair is Tom? He was heer a minit ago.”

“U meen whair’s Huck Finn—that’s whut u meen! I rekon I hain’t raezd such a scamp as mi Tom all thees yeers not to noe him when I see him. That wuud be a prity houdy-do. Cum out frum under that bed, Huck Finn.”

So I dun it. But not feeling brash.

Ant Sally she was wun of th mixt-upest-luuking persons I ever see—exsept wun, and that was Unkl Silas, when he cum in and thay toeld it all to him. It kiend of maed him drunk, as u may say, and he didn’t noe nuthing at all th rest of th day, and preecht a prair-meeting sermon that niet that gaev him a ratling ruputation, becauz th oeldest man in th werld couldn’t a understuud it. So Tom’s Ant Polly, she toeld all about hoo I was, and whut; and I had to up and tel how I was in such a tiet plaes that when Mrs. Phelps tuuk me for Tom Sawyer—she chipt in and sez, “O, go on and call me Ant Sally, I’m uezd to it now, and ’tain’t no need to chaenj”—that when Ant Sally tuuk me for Tom Sawyer I had to stand it—thair worn’t no uther way, and I knowed he wouldn’t miend, becauz it wuud be nuts for him, being a mistery, and he’d maek an advencher out of it, and be perfectly satisfied. And so it ternd out, and he let on to be Sid, and maed things as sofft as he cuud for me.

And his Ant Polly she sed Tom was riet about oeld Mis Watson seting Jim free in her wil; and so, shur enuf, Tom Sawyer had gon and tuuk all that trubl and bother to set a free nigger free! and I couldn’t ever understand befor, until that minit and that tauk, how he cuud help a body set a nigger free with his bringing-up.

Wel, Ant Polly she sed that when Ant Sally roet to her that Tom and Sid had cum all riet and saef, she sez to herself:

“Luuk at that, now! I miet hav expected it, leting him go off that way without enybody to woch him. So now I got to go and trapse all th way doun th river, eleven hundred miel, and fiend out whut that creetur’s up to this tiem, as long as I couldn’t seem to get eny anser out of u about it.”

“Whi, I never herd nuthing frum u,” sez Ant Sally.

“Wel, I wunder! Whi, I roet u twies to ask u whut u cuud meen bi Sid being heer.”

“Wel, I never got ’em, Sis.”

Ant Polly she terns around slo and seveer, and sez:

“U, Tom!”

“Wel—whut?” he sez, kiend of pettish.

“Don’t u whut me, u impuedent thing—hand out them leters.”











“Whut leters?”

“Them leters. I be bound, if I hav to taek a-holt of u I’ll—”

“Thay’re in th trunk. Thair, now. And thay’re just th saem as thay was when I got them out of th offis. I hain’t luukt into them, I hain’t tucht them. But I knowed thay’d maek trubl, and I thaut if u worn’t in no hery, I’d—”

“Wel, u do need skining, thair ain’t no mistaek about it. And I roet anuther wun to tel u I was cuming; and I s’poez he—”

“No, it cum yesterday; I hain’t red it yet, but it’s all riet, I’ve got that wun.”

I wonted to offer to bet too dolars she hadn’t, but I rekond maybe it was just as saef to not to. So I never sed nuthing.














CHAPTER Th LAST

Th ferst tiem I catched Tom prievet I askt him whut was his iedeea, tiem of th evaezhun?—whut it was he’d pland to do if th evaezhun werkt all riet and he manejd to set a nigger free that was allredy free befor? And he sed, whut he had pland in his hed frum th start, if we got Jim out all saef, was for us to run him doun th river on th raft, and hav advenchers plum to th mouth of th river, and then tel him about his being free, and taek him bak up hoem on a steemboet, in stiel, and pay him for his lost tiem, and riet werd ahed and get out all th niggers around, and hav them wallts him into toun with a torchliet proseshun and a bras-band, and then he wuud be a heero, and so wuud we. But I rekond it was about as wel th way it was.

We had Jim out of th chaens in no tiem, and when Ant Polly and Unkl Silas and Ant Sally found out how guud he helpt th doctor ners Tom, thay maed a heep of fus oever him, and fixt him up priem, and giv him all he wonted to eet, and a guud tiem, and nuthing to do. And we had him up to th sik-room, and had a hi tauk; and Tom giv Jim forty dolars for being prizoner for us so paeshent, and doing it up so guud, and Jim was pleezd moest to deth, and busted out, and sez:











“Dah, now, Huck, whut I tel u?—whut I tel u up dah on Jackson islan’? I toel u I got a hairy breas’, en whut’s de sien un it; en I toel u I ben rich wunst, en gwineter to be rich agin; en it’s cum troo; en heah she is! dah, now! doan’ tauk to me—siens is siens, mien I tel u; en I knowed jis’ ’s wel ’at I ’uz gwineter be rich agin as I’s a-stannin’ heah dis minit!”

And then Tom he taukt along and taukt along, and sez, le’s all three slied out of heer wun of thees niets and get an outfit, and go for houling advenchers amungst th Injuns, oever in th Territory, for a cupl of weeks or too; and I sez, all riet, that soots me, but I ain’t got no muny for to bi th outfit, and I rekon I couldn’t get nun frum hoem, becauz it’s liekly pap’s bin bak befor now, and got it all away frum Juj Thatcher and drunk it up.

“No, he hain’t,” Tom sez; “it’s all thair yet—six thouzand dolars and mor; and yur pap hain’t ever bin bak sinss. Hadn’t when I cum away, enyhow.”

Jim sez, kiend of solem:

“He ain’t a-comin’ bak no mo’, Huck.”

I sez:

“Whi, Jim?”

“Nemmine whi, Huck—but he ain’t comin’ bak no mo.”

But I kept at him; so at last he sez:

“Doan’ u ’member de hous dat was floet’n doun de river, en day wuz a man in dah, kivered up, en I went in en unkivered him and didn’ let u cum in? Wel, den, u kin git yo’ muny when u wonts it, kase dat wuz him.”

Tom’s moest wel now, and got his buulet around his nek on a woch-gard for a woch, and is allways seeing whut tiem it is, and so thair ain’t nuthing mor to riet about, and I am roten glad of it, becauz if I’d a knowed whut a trubl it was to maek a buuk I wouldn’t a takld it, and ain’t a-going to no mor. But I rekon I got to liet out for th Territory ahed of th rest, becauz Ant Sally she’s going to adopt me and sivilize me, and I can’t stand it. I bin thair befor.

Th END. Yurs Trooly, HUCK FINN.
